"Faith" Is A Fine Invention 
 
"Faith" is a fine invention 
When Gentlemen can see&mdash; 
But Microscopes are prudent 
In an Emergency. 
"Heaven" Has Different Signs&Mdash;To Me 
 
"Heaven" has different Signs&mdash;to me&mdash; 
Sometimes, I think that Noon 
Is but a symbol of the Place&mdash; 
And when again, at Dawn, 
A mighty look runs round the World 
And settles in the Hills&mdash; 
An Awe if it should be like that 
Upon the Ignorance steals&mdash; 
The Orchard, when the Sun is on&mdash; 
The Triumph of the Birds 
When they together Victory make&mdash; 
Some Carnivals of Clouds&mdash; 
The Rapture of a finished Day&mdash; 
Returning to the West&mdash; 
All these&mdash;remind us of the place 
That Men call "paradise"&mdash; 
Itself be fairer&mdash;we suppose&mdash; 
But how Ourself, shall be 
Adorned, for a Superior Grace&mdash; 
Not yet, our eyes can see&mdash; 
"Heaven"&mdash;Is What I Cannot Reach! 
 
"Heaven"&mdash;is what I cannot reach! 
The Apple on the Tree&mdash; 
Provided it do hopeless&mdash;hang&mdash; 
That&mdash;"Heaven" is&mdash;to Me! 
The Color, on the Cruising Cloud&mdash; 
The interdicted Land&mdash; 
Behind the Hill&mdash;the House behind&mdash; 
There&mdash;Paradise&mdash;is found! 
Her teasing Purples&mdash;Afternoons&mdash; 
The credulous&mdash;decoy&mdash; 
Enamored&mdash;of the Conjuror&mdash; 
That spurned us&mdash;Yesterday! 
"Houses"&Mdash;So The Wise Men Tell Me 
 
"Houses"&mdash;so the Wise Men tell me&mdash; 
"Mansions"! Mansions must be warm! 
Mansions cannot let the tears in, 
Mansions must exclude the storm! 
"Many Mansions," by "his Father," 
I don't know him; snugly built! 
Could the Children find the way there&mdash; 
Some, would even trudge tonight! 
"I Want"&Mdash;It Pleaded&Mdash;All Its Life 
 
"I want"&mdash;it pleaded&mdash;All its life&mdash; 
I want&mdash;was chief it said 
When Skill entreated it&mdash;the last&mdash; 
And when so newly dead&mdash; 
I could not deem it late&mdash;to hear 
That single&mdash;steadfast sigh&mdash; 
The lips had placed as with a "Please" 
Toward Eternity&mdash; 
"Nature" Is What We See 
 
"Nature" is what we see&mdash; 
The Hill&mdash;the Afternoon&mdash; 
Squirrel&mdash;Eclipse&mdash;the Bumble bee&mdash; 
Nay&mdash;Nature is Heaven&mdash; 
Nature is what we hear&mdash; 
The Bobolink&mdash;the Sea&mdash; 
Thunder&mdash;the Cricket&mdash; 
Nay&mdash;Nature is Harmony&mdash; 
Nature is what we know&mdash; 
Yet have no art to say&mdash; 
So impotent Our Wisdom is 
To her Simplicity. 
"Unto Me?" I Do Not Know You 
 
"Unto Me?" I do not know you&mdash; 
Where may be your House? 
"I am Jesus&mdash;Late of Judea&mdash; 
Now&mdash;of Paradise"&mdash; 
Wagons&mdash;have you&mdash;to convey me? 
This is far from Thence&mdash; 
"Arms of Mine&mdash;sufficient Phaeton&mdash; 
Trust Omnipotence"&mdash; 
I am spotted&mdash;"I am Pardon"&mdash; 
I am small&mdash;"The Least 
Is esteemed in Heaven the Chiefest&mdash; 
Occupy my House"&mdash; 
"Why Do I Love" You, Sir? 
 
"Why do I love" You, Sir? 
Because&mdash; 
The Wind does not require the Grass 
To answer&mdash;Wherefore when He pass 
She cannot keep Her place. 
Because He knows&mdash;and 
Do not You&mdash; 
And We know not&mdash; 
Enough for Us 
The Wisdom it be so&mdash; 
The Lightning&mdash;never asked an Eye 
Wherefore it shut&mdash;when He was by&mdash; 
Because He knows it cannot speak&mdash; 
And reasons not contained&mdash; 
&mdash;Of Talk&mdash; 
There be&mdash;preferred by Daintier Folk&mdash; 
The Sunrise&mdash;Sire&mdash;compelleth Me&mdash; 
Because He's Sunrise&mdash;and I see&mdash; 
Therefore&mdash;Then&mdash; 
I love Thee&mdash; 
&quot;470&quot; 
How good—to be alive! 
How infinite—to be 
Alive—two-fold—The Birth I had 
And this—besides, in—Thee! 
A Bird Came Down 
A bird came down the walk: 
He did not know I saw; 
He bit an angle-worm in halves 
And ate the fellow, raw. 
And then he drank a dew 
From a convenient grass, 
And then hopped sidewise to the wall 
To let a beetle pass. 
He glanced with rapid eyes 
That hurried all abroad,They 
looked like frightened beads, I thought; 
He stirred his velvet head 
Like one in danger; cautious, 
I offered him a crumb, 
And he unrolled his feathers 
And rowed him softer home 
Than oars divide the ocean, 
Too silver for a seam, 
Or butterflies, off banks of noon, 
Leap, splashless, as they swim. 
A Book 
There is no frigate like a book 
To take us lands away, 
Nor any coursers like a page 
Of prancing poetry. 
This traverse may the poorest take 
Without oppress of toll; 
How frugal is the chariot 
That bears a human soul! 
A Burdock&Mdash;Clawed My Gown 
 
A Burdock&mdash;clawed my Gown&mdash; 
Not Burdock's&mdash;blame&mdash; 
But mine&mdash; 
Who went too near 
The Burdock's Den&mdash; 
A Bog&mdash;affronts my shoe&mdash; 
What else have Bogs&mdash;to do&mdash; 
The only Trade they know&mdash; 
The splashing Men! 
Ah, pity&mdash;then! 
'Tis Minnows can despise! 
The Elephant's&mdash;calm eyes 
Look further on! 
A Charm Invests A Face 
 
A Charm invests a face 
Imperfectly beheld— 
The Lady dare not lift her Veil 
For fear it be dispelled— 
But peers beyond her mesh— 
And wishes—and denies— 
Lest Interview—annul a want 
That Image—satisfies— 
A chilly Peace infests the Grass 
A chilly Peace infests the Grass 
The Sun respectful lies Not 
any Trance of industry 
These shadows scrutinize 
Whose Allies go no more astray 
For service or for Glee But 
all mankind deliver here 
From whatsoever sea 
A Clock Stopped -- Not The Mantel's 
A clock stopped -- not the mantel's 
Geneva's farthest skill 
Can't put the puppet bowing 
That just now dangled still. 
An awe came on the trinket! 
The figures hunched with pain, 
Then quivered out of decimals 
Into degreeless noon. 
It will not stir for doctors, 
This pendulum of snow; 
The shopman importunes it, 
While cool, concernless No 
Nods from the gilded pointers, 
Nods from seconds slim, 
Decades of arrogance between 
The dial life and him. 
A Cloud Withdrew From The Sky 
 
A Cloud withdrew from the Sky 
Superior Glory be 
But that Cloud and its Auxiliaries 
Are forever lost to me 
Had I but further scanned 
Had I secured the Glow 
In an Hermetic Memory 
It had availed me now. 
Never to pass the Angel 
With a glance and a Bow 
Till I am firm in Heaven 
Is my intention now. 
A Coffin—is A Small Domain 
A Coffin—is a small Domain, 
Yet able to contain 
A Citizen of Paradise 
In it diminished Plane. 
A Grave—is a restricted Breadth— 
Yet ampler than the Sun— 
And all the Seas He populates 
And Lands He looks upon 
To Him who on its small Repose 
Bestows a single Friend— 
Circumference without Relief— 
Or Estimate—or End— 
A Counterfeit -a Plated Person 
A Counterfeit -a Plated Person I 
would not be Whatever 
strata of Iniquity 
My Nature underlie Truth 
is good Health -and Safety, and the Sky. 
How meagre, what an Exile -is a Lie, 
And Vocal -when we die 
A Darting Fear&Mdash;A Pomp&Mdash;A Tear 
 
A darting fear&mdash;a pomp&mdash;a tear&mdash; 
A waking on a morn 
To find that what one waked for, 
Inhales the different dawn. 
A Day! Help! Help! Another Day! 
 
A Day! Help! Help! Another Day! 
Your prayers, oh Passer by! 
From such a common ball as this 
Might date a Victory! 
From marshallings as simple 
The flags of nations swang. 
Steady&mdash;my soul: What issues 
Upon thine arrow hang! 
A Death Blow Is A Life Blow To Some 
 
A Death blow is a Life blow to Some 
Who till they died, did not alive become&mdash; 
Who had they lived, had died but when 
They died, Vitality begun. 
A Door Just Opened On A Street 
A door just opened on a street-I, 
lost, was passing by-
An instant's width of warmth disclosed 
And wealth, and company. 
The door as sudden shut, and I, 
I, lost, was passing by,-
Lost doubly, but by contrast most, 
Enlightening misery. 
A Doubt If It Be Us 
 
A doubt if it be Us 
Assists the staggering Mind 
In an extremer Anguish 
Until it footing find. 
An Unreality is lent, 
A merciful Mirage 
That makes the living possible 
While it suspends the lives. 
A Drop Fell On The Apple Tree 
A drop fell on the apple tree 
Another on the roof; 
A half a dozen kissed the eaves, 
And made the gables laugh. 
A few went out to help the brook, 
That went to help the sea. 
Myself conjectured, Were they pearls, 
What necklaces could be! 
The dust replaced in hoisted roa 
The birds jocoser sung; 
The sunshine threw his hat away, 
The orchards spangles hung. 
The breezes brought dejected 
And bathed them in the glee; 
The East put out a single flag, 
And signed the fete away. 
A Dying Tiger&Mdash;Moaned For Drink 
 
A Dying Tiger&mdash;moaned for Drink&mdash; 
I hunted all the Sand&mdash; 
I caught the Dripping of a Rock 
And bore it in my Hand&mdash; 
His Mighty Balls&mdash;in death were thick&mdash; 
But searching&mdash;I could see 
A Vision on the Retina 
Of Water&mdash;and of me&mdash; 
'Twas not my blame&mdash;who sped too slow&mdash; 
'Twas not his blame&mdash;who died 
While I was reaching him&mdash; 
But 'twas&mdash;the fact that He was dead&mdash; 
A Feather From The Whippoorwill 
 
A feather from the Whippoorwill 
That everlasting&mdash;sings! 
Whose galleries&mdash;are Sunrise&mdash; 
Whose Opera&mdash;the Springs&mdash; 
Whose Emerald Nest the Ages spin 
Of mellow&mdash;murmuring thread&mdash; 
Whose Beryl Egg, what Schoolboys hunt 
In "Recess"&mdash;Overhead! 
A First Mute Coming 
 
A first Mute Coming&mdash; 
In the Stranger's House&mdash; 
A first fair Going&mdash; 
When the Bells rejoice&mdash; 
A first Exchange&mdash;of 
What hath mingled&mdash;been&mdash; 
For Lot&mdash;exhibited to 
Faith&mdash;alone&mdash; 
A Fuzzy Fellow, Without Feet 
 
A fuzzy fellow, without feet, 
Yet doth exceeding run! 
Of velvet, is his Countenance, 
And his Complexion, dun! 
Sometime, he dwelleth in the grass! 
Sometime, upon a bough, 
From which he doth descend in plush 
Upon the Passer-by! 
All this in summer. 
But when winds alarm the Forest Folk, 
He taketh Damask Residence&mdash; 
And struts in sewing silk! 
Then, finer than a Lady, 
Emerges in the spring! 
A Feather on each shoulder! 
You'd scarce recognize him! 
By Men, yclept Caterpillar! 
By me! But who am I, 
To tell the pretty secret 
Of the Butterfly! 
A Great Hope Fell 
A great Hope fell 
You heard no noise 
The Ruin was within 
Oh cunning wreck that told no tale 
And let no Witness in 
The mind was built for mighty Freight 
For dread occasion planned 
How often foundering at Sea 
Ostensibly, on Land 
A not admitting of the wound 
Until it grew so wide 
That all my Life had entered it 
And there were troughs beside 
A closing of the simple lid 
That opened to the sun 
Until the tender Carpenter 
Perpetual nail it down 
A Happy Lip&Mdash;Breaks Sudden 
 
A happy lip&mdash;breaks sudden&mdash; 
It doesn't state you how 
It contemplated&mdash;smiling&mdash; 
Just consummated&mdash;now&mdash; 
But this one, wears its merriment 
So patient&mdash;like a pain&mdash; 
Fresh gilded&mdash;to elude the eyes 
Unqualified, to scan&mdash; 
A House Upon The Height 
 
A House upon the Height&mdash; 
That Wagon never reached&mdash; 
No Dead, were ever carried down&mdash; 
No Peddler's Cart&mdash;approached&mdash; 
Whose Chimney never smoked&mdash; 
Whose Windows&mdash;Night and Morn&mdash; 
Caught Sunrise first&mdash;and Sunset&mdash;last&mdash; 
Then&mdash;held an Empty Pane&mdash; 
Whose fate&mdash;Conjecture knew&mdash; 
No other neighbor&mdash;did&mdash; 
And what it was&mdash;we never lisped&mdash; 
Because He&mdash;never told&mdash; 
A Lady Red&Mdash;Amid The Hill 
 
A Lady red&mdash;amid the Hill 
Her annual secret keeps! 
A Lady white, within the Field 
In placid Lily sleeps! 
The tidy Breezes, with their Brooms&mdash; 
Sweep vale&mdash;and hill&mdash;and tree! 
Prithee, My pretty Housewives! 
Who may expected be? 
The Neighbors do not yet suspect! 
The Woods exchange a smile! 
Orchard, and Buttercup, and Bird&mdash; 
In such a little while! 
And yet, how still the Landscape stands! 
How nonchalant the Hedge! 
As if the "Resurrection" 
Were nothing very strange! 
A lane of Yellow led the eye 
A lane of Yellow led the eye 
Unto a Purple Wood 
Whose soft inhabitants to be 
Surpasses solitude 
If Bird the silence contradict 
Or flower presume to show 
In that low summer of the West 
Impossible to know 
A Light Exists In Spring 
A light exists in spring 
Not present on the year 
At any other period. 
When March is scarcely here 
A color stands abroad 
On solitary hills 
That science cannot overtake, 
But human naturefeels. 
It waits upon the lawn; 
It shows the furthest tree 
Upon the furthest slope we know; 
It almost speaks to me. 
Then, as horizons step, 
Or noons report away, 
Without the formula of sound, 
It passes, and we stay: 
A quality of loss 
Affecting our content, 
As trade had suddenly encroached 
Upon a sacrament. 
A Little Bread&Mdash;A Crust&Mdash;A Crumb 
 
A little bread&mdash;a crust&mdash;a crumb&mdash; 
A little trust&mdash;a demijohn&mdash; 
Can keep the soul alive&mdash; 
Not portly, mind! but breathing&mdash;warm&mdash; 
Conscious&mdash;as old Napoleon, 
The night before the Crown! 
A modest lot&mdash;A fame petite&mdash; 
A brief Campaign of sting and sweet 
Is plenty! Is enough! 
A Sailor's business is the shore! 
A Soldier's&mdash;balls! Who asketh more, 
Must seek the neighboring life! 
A Little Dog That Wags His Tail 
A little Dog that wags his tail 
And knows no other joy 
Of such a little Dog am I 
Reminded by a Boy 
Who gambols all the living Day 
Without an earthly cause 
Because he is a little Boy 
I honestly suppose 
The Cat that in the Corner dwells 
Her martial Day forgot 
The Mouse but a Tradition now 
Of her desireless Lot 
Another class remind me 
Who neither please nor play 
But not to make a 'bit of noise' 
Beseech each little Boy 
A Little East Of Jordan 
 
A little East of Jordan, 
Evangelists record, 
A Gymnast and an Angel 
Did wrestle long and hard&mdash; 
Till morning touching mountain&mdash; 
And Jacob, waxing strong, 
The Angel begged permission 
To Breakfast&mdash;to return&mdash; 
Not so, said cunning Jacob! 
"I will not let thee go 
Except thou bless me"&mdash;Stranger! 
The which acceded to&mdash; 
Light swung the silver fleeces 
"Peniel" Hills beyond, 
And the bewildered Gymnast 
Found he had worsted God!

ponders this tremendous scene This

A Little Road Not Made Man 
A little road not made of man, 
Enabled of the eye, 
Accessible to thill of bee, 
Or cart of butterfly. 
If town it have, beyond itself, 
'T is that I cannot say; 
I only sigh,--no vehicle 
Bears me along that way.

A little Snow was here and there 
Disseminated in her Hair Since 
she and I had met and played

But Time had added not obtained 
Impregnable the Rose 
For summer too indelible 
Too obdurate for Snows 
A Long, Long Sleep, A Famous Sleep 
A long, long sleep, a famous sleep 
That makes no show for dawn 
By strech of limb or stir of lid, -An 
independent one. 
Was ever idleness like this? 
Within a hut of stone 
To bask the centuries away 
Nor once look up for noon? 
A Loss Of Something Ever Felt I 
 
A loss of something ever felt I&mdash; 
The first that I could recollect 
Bereft I was&mdash;of what I knew not 
Too young that any should suspect 
A Mourner walked among the children 
I notwithstanding went about 
As one bemoaning a Dominion 
Itself the only Prince cast out&mdash; 
Elder, Today, a session wiser 
And fainter, too, as Wiseness is&mdash; 
I find myself still softly searching 
For my Delinguent Palaces&mdash; 
And a Suspicion, like a Finger 
Touches my Forehead now and then 
That I am looking oppositely 
For the site of the Kingdom of Heaven&mdash; 
A Man May Make A Remark 
 
A Man may make a Remark&mdash; 
In itself&mdash;a quiet thing 
That may furnish the Fuse unto a Spark 
In dormant nature&mdash;lain&mdash; 
Let us deport&mdash;with skill&mdash; 
Let us discourse&mdash;with care&mdash; 
Powder exists in Charcoal&mdash; 
Before it exists in Fire. 
A Mien To Move A Queen 
 
A Mien to move a Queen&mdash; 
Half Child&mdash;Half Heroine&mdash; 
An Orleans in the Eye 
That puts its manner by 
For humbler Company 
When none are near 
Even a Tear&mdash; 
Its frequent Visitor&mdash; 
A Bonnet like a Duke&mdash; 
And yet a Wren's Peruke 
Were not so shy 
Of Goer by&mdash; 
And Hands&mdash;so slight&mdash; 
They would elate a Sprite 
With Merriment&mdash; 
A Voice that Alters&mdash;Low 
And on the Ear can go 
Like Let of Snow&mdash; 
Or shift supreme&mdash; 
As tone of Realm 
On Subjects Diadem&mdash; 
Too small&mdash;to fear&mdash; 
Too distant&mdash;to endear&mdash; 
And so Men Compromise 
And just&mdash;revere&mdash; 
A Moth The Hue Of This 
 
A Moth the hue of this 
Haunts Candles in Brazil. 
Nature's Experience would make 
Our Reddest Second pale. 
Nature is fond, I sometimes think, 
Of Trinkets, as a Girl. 
A Murmur In The Trees&Mdash;To Note 
 
A Murmur in the Trees&mdash;to note&mdash; 
Not loud enough&mdash;for Wind&mdash; 
A Star&mdash;not far enough to seek&mdash; 
Nor near enough&mdash;to find&mdash; 
A long&mdash;long Yellow&mdash;on the Lawn&mdash; 
A Hubbub&mdash;as of feet&mdash; 
Not audible&mdash;as Ours&mdash;to Us&mdash; 
But dapperer&mdash;More Sweet&mdash; 
A Hurrying Home of little Men 
To Houses unperceived&mdash; 
All this&mdash;and more&mdash;if I should tell&mdash; 
Would never be believed&mdash; 
Of Robins in the Trundle bed 
How many I espy 
Whose Nightgowns could not hide the Wings&mdash; 
Although I heard them try&mdash; 
But then I promised ne'er to tell&mdash; 
How could I break My Word? 
So go your Way&mdash;and I'll go Mine&mdash; 
No fear you'll miss the Road. 
A Narrow Fellow In The Grass 
A narrow fellow in the grass 
Occasionally rides; 
You may have met him,--did you not, 
His notice sudden is. 
The grass divides as with a comb, 
A spotted shaft is seen; 
And then it closes at your feet 
And opens further on. 
He likes a boggy acre, 
A floor too cool for corn. 
Yet when a child, and barefoot, 
I more than once, at morn, 
Have passed, I thought, a whip-lash 
Unbraiding in the sun,-When, 
stooping to secure it, 
It wrinkled, and was gone. 
Several of nature's people 
I know, and they know me; 
I feel for them a transport 
Of cordiality; 
But never met this fellow, 
Attended or alone, 
Without a tighter breathing, 
And zero at the bone.

Vicinity to Laws 
Contentment's quiet Suburb&mdash; 
Affliction cannot stay 
In Acres&mdash;Its Location 
Is Illocality&mdash;

A Night&mdash;there lay the Days between&mdash;

Too imperceptible to note&mdash; 
Till it be night&mdash;no more&mdash;

A Pang is more conspicuous in Spring

what they sung for is undone

Till they had moved a Stone

A Poor&Mdash;Torn Heart&Mdash;A Tattered Heart 
 
A poor&mdash;torn heart&mdash;a tattered heart&mdash; 
That sat it down to rest&mdash; 
Nor noticed that the Ebbing Day 
Flowed silver to the West&mdash; 
Nor noticed Night did soft descend&mdash; 
Nor Constellation burn&mdash; 
Intent upon the vision 
Of latitudes unknown. 
The angels&mdash;happening that way 
This dusty heart espied&mdash; 
Tenderly took it up from toil 
And carried it to God&mdash; 
There&mdash;sandals for the Barefoot&mdash; 
There&mdash;gathered from the gales&mdash; 
Do the blue havens by the hand 
Lead the wandering Sails. 
A Precious—mouldering Pleasure 
 
A precious—mouldering pleasure—'tis— 
To meet an Antique Book— 
In just the Dress his Century wore— 
A privilege—I think— 
His venerable Hand to take— 
And warming in our own— 
A passage back—or two—to make— 
To Times when he—was young— 
His quaint opinions—to inspect— 
His thought to ascertain 
On Themes concern our mutual mind— 
The Literature of Man— 
What interested Scholars—most— 
What Competitions ran— 
When Plato—was a Certainty— 
And Sophocles—a Man— 
When Sappho—was a living Girl— 
And Beatrice wore 
The Gown that Dante—deified— 
Facts Centuries before 
He traverses—familiar— 
As One should come to Town— 
And tell you all your Dreams—were true— 
He lived—where Dreams were born— 
His presence is Enchantment— 
You beg him not to go— 
Old Volume shake their Vellum Heads 
And tantalize—just so— 
A Prison Gets To Be A Friend 
 
A Prison gets to be a friend&mdash; 
Between its Ponderous face 
And Ours&mdash;a Kinsmanship express&mdash; 
And in its narrow Eyes&mdash; 
We come to look with gratitude 
For the appointed Beam 
It deal us&mdash;stated as our food&mdash; 
And hungered for&mdash;the same&mdash; 
We learn to know the Planks&mdash; 
That answer to Our feet&mdash; 
So miserable a sound&mdash;at first&mdash; 
Nor ever now&mdash;so sweet&mdash; 
As plashing in the Pools&mdash; 
When Memory was a Boy&mdash; 
But a Demurer Circuit&mdash; 
A Geometric Joy&mdash; 
The Posture of the Key 
That interrupt the Day 
To Our Endeavor&mdash;Not so real 
The Check of Liberty&mdash; 
As this Phantasm Steel&mdash; 
Whose features&mdash;Day and Night&mdash; 
Are present to us&mdash;as Our Own&mdash; 
And as escapeless&mdash;quite&mdash; 
The narrow Round&mdash;the Stint&mdash; 
The slow exchange of Hope&mdash; 
For something passiver&mdash;Content 
Too steep for lookinp up&mdash; 
The Liberty we knew 
Avoided&mdash;like a Dream&mdash; 
Too wide for any Night but Heaven&mdash; 
If That&mdash;indeed&mdash;redeem&mdash;

A Science&Mdash;So The Savants Say 
 
A science&mdash;so the Savants say, 
"Comparative Anatomy"&mdash; 
By which a single bone&mdash; 
Is made a secret to unfold 
Of some rare tenant of the mold, 
Else perished in the stone&mdash; 
So to the eye prospective led, 
This meekest flower of the mead 
Upon a winter's day, 
Stands representative in gold 
Of Rose and Lily, manifold, 
And countless Butterfly!

A Secret told&mdash; 
Ceases to be a Secret&mdash;then&mdash;

That&mdash;can appal but One&mdash; 
Better of it&mdash;continual be afraid&mdash; 
Than it&mdash; 
And Whom you told it to&mdash;beside&mdash; 
A Sepal, Petal, And A Thorn 
 
A sepal, petal, and a thorn 
Upon a common summer's morn&mdash; 
A flask of Dew&mdash;A Bee or two&mdash; 
A Breeze&mdash;a caper in the trees&mdash; 
And I'm a Rose!

As when on Noon 
A Cloud the mighty Sun encloses 
Remembering 
That some there be too numb to notice 
Oh God 
Why give if Thou must take away 
The Loved? 
A Shady Friend For Torrid Days 
A shady friend for torrid days 
Is easier to find 
Than one of higher temperature 
For frigid hour of mind. 
The vane a little to the east 
Scares muslin souls away; 
If broadcloth breasts are firmer 
Than those of organdy, 
Who is to blame? The weaver? 
Ah! the bewildering thread! 
The tapestries of paradise! 
So notelessly are made! 
A Sickness Of This World It Most Occasions 
A Sickness of this World it most occasions 
When Best Men die. 
A Wishfulness their far Condition 
To occupy. 
A Chief indifference, as Foreign 
A World must be 
Themselves forsake -contented, 
For Deity. 
A Single Screw Of Flesh 
 
Is all that pins the Soul 
That stands for Deity, to Mine, 
Upon my side the Veil&mdash; 
Once witnessed of the Gauze&mdash; 
Its name is put away 
As far from mine, as if no plight 
Had printed yesterday, 
In tender&mdash;solemn Alphabet, 
My eyes just turned to see, 
When it was smuggled by my sight 
Into Eternity&mdash; 
More Hands&mdash;to hold&mdash;These are but Two&mdash; 
One more new-mailed Nerve 
Just granted, for the Peril's sake&mdash; 
Some striding&mdash;Giant&mdash;Love&mdash; 
So greater than the Gods can show, 
They slink before the Clay, 
That not for all their Heaven can boast 
Will let its Keepsake&mdash;go 
A Slash Of Blue 
 
A slash of Blue&mdash; 
A sweep of Gray&mdash; 
Some scarlet patches on the way, 
Compose an Evening Sky&mdash; 
A little purple&mdash;slipped between&mdash; 
Some Ruby Trousers hurried on&mdash; 
A Wave of Gold&mdash; 
A Bank of Day&mdash; 
This just makes out the Morning Sky. 
A Sloop of Amber slips away 
A Sloop of Amber slips away 
Upon an Ether Sea, 
And wrecks in Peace a Purple Tar, 
The Son of Ecstasy 
A Solemn Thing Within The Soul 
 
A Solemn thing within the Soul 
To feel itself get ripe&mdash; 
And golden hang&mdash;while farther up&mdash; 
The Maker's Ladders stop&mdash; 
And in the Orchard far below&mdash; 
You hear a Being&mdash;drop&mdash; 
A Wonderful&mdash;to feel the Sun 
Still toiling at the Cheek 
You thought was finished&mdash; 
Cool of eye, and critical of Work&mdash; 
He shifts the stem&mdash;a little&mdash; 
To give your Core&mdash;a look&mdash; 
But solemnest&mdash;to know 
Your chance in Harvest moves 
A little nearer&mdash;Every Sun 
The Single&mdash;to some lives. 
A Solemn Thing&Mdash;It Was&Mdash;I Said 
 
A solemn thing&mdash;it was&mdash;I said&mdash; 
A woman&mdash;white&mdash;to be&mdash; 
And wear&mdash;if God should count me fit&mdash; 
Her blameless mystery&mdash; 
A hallowed thing&mdash;to drop a life 
Into the purple well&mdash; 
Too plummetless&mdash;that it return&mdash; 
Eternity&mdash;until&mdash; 
I pondered how the bliss would look&mdash; 
And would it feel as big&mdash; 
When I could take it in my hand&mdash; 
As hovering&mdash;seen&mdash;through fog&mdash; 
And then&mdash;the size of this "small" life&mdash; 
The Sages&mdash;call it small&mdash; 
Swelled&mdash;like Horizons&mdash;in my vest&mdash; 
And I sneered&mdash;softly&mdash;"small"! 
A Something In A Summer's Day 
 
A something in a summer's Day 
As slow her flambeaux burn away 
Which solemnizes me. 
A something in a summer's noon&mdash; 
A depth&mdash;an Azure&mdash;a perfume&mdash; 
Transcending ecstasy. 
And still within a summer's night 
A something so transporting bright 
I clap my hands to see&mdash; 
Then veil my too inspecting face 
Lets such a subtle&mdash;shimmering grace 
Flutter too far for me&mdash; 
The wizard fingers never rest&mdash; 
The purple brook within the breast 
Still chafes it narrow bed&mdash; 
Still rears the East her amber Flag&mdash; 
Guides still the sun along the Crag 
His Caravan of Red&mdash; 
So looking on&mdash;the night&mdash;the morn 
Conclude the wonder gay&mdash; 
And I meet, coming thro' the dews 
Another summer's Day! 
A South Wind&Mdash;Has A Pathos 
 
A South Wind&mdash;has a pathos 
Of individual Voice&mdash; 
As One detect on Landings 
An Emigrant's address. 
A Hint of Ports and Peoples&mdash; 
And much not understood&mdash; 
The fairer&mdash;for the farness&mdash; 
And for the foreignhood. 
A Spider sewed at Night 
A Spider sewed at Night 
Without a Light 
Upon an Arc of White. 
If Ruff it was of Dame 
Or Shroud of Gnome 
Himself himself inform. 
Of Immortality 
His Strategy 
Was Physiognomy. 
A Still—volcano—life 
 
A still—Volcano—Life— 
That flickered in the night— 
When it was dark enough to do 
Without erasing sight— 
A quiet—Earthquake Style— 
Too subtle to suspect 
By natures this side Naples— 
The North cannot detect 
The Solemn—Torrid—Symbol— 
The lips that never lie— 
Whose hissing Corals part—and shut— 
And Cities—ooze away— 
A Thought Went Up My Mind To-Day 
A thought went up my mind to-day 
That I have had before, 
But did not finish,--some way back, 
I could not fix the year, 
Nor where it went, nor why it came 
The second time to me, 
Nor definitely what it was, 
Have I the art to say. 
But somewhere in my soul, I know 
I've met the thing before; 
It just reminded me--'t was all-And 
came my way no more. 
A Throe Upon The Features 
 
A throe upon the features&mdash; 
A hurry in the breath&mdash; 
An ecstasy of parting 
Denominated "Death"&mdash; 
An anguish at the mention 
Which when to patience grown, 
I've known permission given 
To rejoin its own. 
A Toad Can Die Of Light! 
A toad can die of light!
 Death is the common right
 Of toads and men,-
Of earl and midge
 The privilege.
 Why swagger then?
 The gnat's supremacy
 Is large as thine. 
A Tongue—to Tell Him I Am True! 
 
A Tongue—to tell Him I am true! 
Its fee—to be of Gold— 
Had Nature—in Her monstrous House 
A single Ragged Child— 
To earn a Mine—would run 
That Interdicted Way, 
And tell Him—Charge thee speak it plain— 
That so far—Truth is True? 
And answer What I do— 
Beginning with the Day 
That Night—begun— 
Nay—Midnight—'twas— 
Since Midnight—happened—say— 
If once more—Pardon—Boy— 
The Magnitude thou may 
Enlarge my Message—If too vast 
Another Lad—help thee— 
Thy Pay—in Diamonds—be— 
And His—in solid Gold— 
Say Rubies—if He hesitate— 
My Message—must be told— 
Say—last I said—was This— 
That when the Hills—come down— 
And hold no higher than the Plain— 
My Bond—have just begun— 
And when the Heavens—disband— 
And Deity conclude— 
Then—look for me. Be sure you say— 
Least Figure—on the Road— 
A Tooth Upon Our Peace 
 
A Tooth upon Our Peace 
The Peace cannot deface&mdash; 
Then Wherefore be the Tooth? 
To vitalize the Grace&mdash; 
The Heaven hath a Hell&mdash; 
Itself to signalize&mdash; 
And every sign before the Place 
Is Gilt with Sacrifice&mdash; 
A train went through a burial gate 
A train went through a burial gate, 
A bird broke forth and sang, 
And trilled, and quivered, and shook his throat 
Till all the churchyard rang; 
And then adjusted his little notes, 
And bowed and sang again. 
Doubtless, he thought it meet of him 
To say good-by to men. 
A Transport One Cannot Contain 
 
A transport one cannot contain 
May yet a transport be&mdash; 
Though God forbid it lift the lid&mdash; 
Unto its Ecstasy! 
A Diagram&mdash;of Rapture! 
A sixpence at a Show&mdash; 
With Holy Ghosts in Cages! 
The Universe would go! 
A Visitor In Marl 
 
A Visitor in Marl&mdash; 
Who influences Flowers&mdash; 
Till they are orderly as Busts&mdash; 
And Elegant&mdash;as Glass&mdash; 
Who visits in the Night&mdash; 
And just before the Sun&mdash; 
Concludes his glistening interview&mdash; 
Caresses&mdash;and is gone&mdash; 
But whom his fingers touched&mdash; 
And where his feet have run&mdash; 
And whatsoever Mouth be kissed&mdash; 
Is as it had not been&mdash; 
A Weight With Needles On The Pounds 
 
A Weight with Needles on the pounds&mdash; 
To push, and pierce, besides&mdash; 
That if the Flesh resist the Heft&mdash; 
The puncture&mdash;coolly tries&mdash; 
That not a pore be overlooked 
Of all this Compound Frame&mdash; 
As manifold for Anguish&mdash; 
As Species&mdash;be&mdash;for name&mdash; 
A Wife&Mdash;At Daybreak I Shall Be 
 
A Wife&mdash;at daybreak I shall be&mdash; 
Sunrise&mdash;Hast thou a Flag for me? 
At Midnight, I am but a Maid, 
How short it takes to make a Bride&mdash; 
Then&mdash;Midnight, I have passed from thee 
Unto the East, and Victory&mdash; 
Midnight&mdash;Good Night! I hear them call, 
The Angels bustle in the Hall&mdash; 
Softly my Future climbs the Stair, 
I fumble at my Childhood's prayer 
So soon to be a Child no more&mdash; 
Eternity, I'm coming&mdash;Sire, 
Savior&mdash;I've seen the face&mdash;before! 
A Wind That Rose 
A Wind that rose 
Though not a Leaf 
In any Forest stirred 
But with itself did cold engage 
Beyond the Realm of Bird A 
Wind that woke a lone Delight 
Like Separation's Swell 
Restored in Arctic Confidence 
To the Invisible 
A Word dropped careless on a Page 
A Word dropped careless on a Page 
May stimulate an eye 
When folded in perpetual seam 
The Wrinkled Maker lie 
Infection in the sentence breeds 
We may inhale Despair 
At distances of Centuries 
From the Malaria 
A Wounded Deer&Mdash;Leaps Highest 
 
A Wounded Deer&mdash;leaps highest&mdash; 
I've heard the Hunter tell&mdash; 
'Tis but the Ecstasy of death&mdash; 
And then the Brake is still! 
The Smitten Rock that gushes! 
The trampled Steel that springs! 
A Cheek is always redder 
Just where the Hectic stings! 
Mirth is the Mail of Anguish 
In which it Cautious Arm, 
Lest anybody spy the blood 
And "you're hurt" exclaim! 
Abraham To Kill Him 
Abraham to kill him 
Was distinctly told— 
Isaac was an Urchin— 
Abraham was old— 
Not a hesitation— 
Abraham complied— 
Flattered by Obeisance 
Tyranny demurred— 
Isaac—to his children 
Lived to tell the tale— 
Moral—with a mastiff 
Manners may prevail. 
Absence Disembodies—so Does Death 
 
Absence disembodies—so does Death 
Hiding individuals from the Earth 
Superposition helps, as well as love— 
Tenderness decreases as we prove— 
Absent Place&Mdash;An April Day 
 
Absent Place&mdash;an April Day&mdash; 
Daffodils a-blow 
Homesick curiosity 
To the Souls that snow&mdash; 
Drift may block within it 
Deeper than without&mdash; 
Daffodil delight but 
Him it duplicate&mdash; 
Adrift! A Little Boat Adrift! 
 
Adrift! A little boat adrift! 
And night is coming down! 
Will no one guide a little boat 
Unto the nearest town? 
So Sailors say&mdash;on yesterday&mdash; 
Just as the dusk was brown 
One little boat gave up its strife 
And gurgled down and down. 
So angels say&mdash;on yesterday&mdash; 
Just as the dawn was red 
One little boat&mdash;o'erspent with gales&mdash; 
Retrimmed its masts&mdash;redecked its sails&mdash; 
And shot&mdash;exultant on! 
Afraid! Of Whom Am I Afraid? 
 
Afraid! Of whom am I afraid? 
Not Death&mdash;for who is He? 
The Porter of my Father's Lodge 
As much abasheth me! 
Of Life? 'Twere odd I fear [a] thing 
That comprehendeth me 
In one or two existences&mdash; 
As Deity decree&mdash; 
Of Resurrection? Is the East 
Afraid to trust the Morn 
With her fastidious forehead? 
As soon impeach my Crown! 
After A Hundred Years 
After a hundred years 
Nobody knows the place,-Agony, 
that enacted there, 
Motionless as peace. 
Weeds triumphant ranged, 
Strangers strolled and spelled 
At the lone orthography 
Of the elder dead. 
Winds of summer fields 
Recollect the way,-Instinct 
picking up the key 
Dropped by memory. 
After Great Pain, A Formal Feeling Comes 
After great pain, a formal feeling comes-The 
Nerves sit ceremonious, like Toombs-The 
stiff Heart questions was it He, that bore, 
And Yesterday, or Centuries before? 
The Feet, mechanical, go round-Of 
Ground, or Air, or Ought-A 
Wooden way 
Regardless grown, 
A Quartz contentment, like a stone-
This is the Hour of Lead-Remembered, 
if outlived, 
As Freezing persons recollect the Snow-First--
Chill--then Stupor--then the letting go-
Again&Mdash;His Voice Is At The Door 
 
Again&mdash;his voice is at the door&mdash; 
I feel the old Degree&mdash; 
I hear him ask the servant 
For such an one&mdash;as me&mdash; 
I take a flower&mdash;as I go&mdash; 
My face to justify&mdash; 
He never saw me&mdash;in this life&mdash; 
I might surprise his eye! 
I cross the Hall with mingled steps&mdash; 
I&mdash;silent&mdash;pass the door&mdash; 
I look on all this world contains&mdash; 
Just his face&mdash;nothing more! 
We talk in careless&mdash;and it toss&mdash; 
A kind of plummet strain&mdash; 
Each&mdash;sounding&mdash;shyly&mdash; 
Just&mdash;how&mdash;deep&mdash; 
The other's one&mdash;had been&mdash; 
We walk&mdash;I leave my Dog&mdash;at home&mdash; 
A tender&mdash;thoughtful Moon&mdash; 
Goes with us&mdash;just a little way&mdash; 
And&mdash;then&mdash;we are alone&mdash; 
Alone&mdash;if Angels are "alone"&mdash; 
First time they try the sky! 
Alone&mdash;if those "veiled faces"&mdash;be&mdash; 
We cannot count&mdash;on High! 
I'd give&mdash;to live that hour&mdash;again&mdash; 
The purple&mdash;in my Vein&mdash; 
But He must count the drops&mdash;himself&mdash; 
My price for every stain! 
Ah, Moon—and Star! 
 
Ah, Moon—and Star! 
You are very far— 
But were no one 
Farther than you— 
Do you think I'd stop 
For a Firmament— 
Or a Cubit—or so? 
I could borrow a Bonnet 
Of the Lark— 
And a Chamois' Silver Boot— 
And a stirrup of an Antelope— 
And be with you—Tonight! 
But, Moon, and Star, 
Though you're very far— 
There is one—farther than you— 
He—is more than a firmament—from Me— 
So I can never go! 
Ah, Teneriffe! 
 
Ah, Teneriffe! 
Retreating Mountain! 
Purples of Ages&mdash;pause for you&mdash; 
Sunset&mdash;reviews her Sapphire Regiment&mdash; 
Day&mdash;drops you her Red Adieu! 
Still&mdash;Clad in your Mail of ices&mdash; 
Thigh of Granite&mdash;and thew&mdash;of Steel&mdash; 
Heedless&mdash;alike&mdash;of pomp&mdash;or parting 
Ah, Teneriffe! 
I'm kneeling&mdash;still&mdash; 
Air has no Residence, no Neighbor 
Air has no Residence, no Neighbor, 
No Ear, no Door, 
No Apprehension of Another 
Oh, Happy Air! 
Ethereal Guest at e'en an Outcast's Pillow Essential 
Host, in Life's faint, wailing Inn, 
Later than Light thy Consciousness accost me 
Till it depart, persuading Mine 
All But Death, Can Be Adjusted 
 
All but Death, can be Adjusted&mdash; 
Dynasties repaired&mdash; 
Systems&mdash;settled in their Sockets&mdash; 
Citadels&mdash;dissolved&mdash; 
Wastes of Lives&mdash;resown with Colors 
By Succeeding Springs&mdash; 
Death&mdash;unto itself&mdash;Exception&mdash; 
Is exempt from Change&mdash; 
All Circumstances Are The Frame 
 
All Circumstances are the Frame 
In which His Face is set&mdash; 
All Latitudes exist for His 
Sufficient Continent&mdash; 
The Light His Action, and the Dark 
The Leisure of His Will&mdash; 
In Him Existence serve or set 
A Force illegible. 
All Forgot For Recollecting 
 
All forgot for recollecting 
Just a paltry One&mdash; 
All forsook, for just a Stranger's 
New Accompanying&mdash; 
Grace of Wealth, and Grace of Station 
Less accounted than 
An unknown Esteem possessing&mdash; 
Estimate&mdash;Who can&mdash; 
Home effaced&mdash;Her faces dwindled&mdash; 
Nature&mdash;altered small&mdash; 
Sun&mdash;if shone&mdash;or Storm&mdash;if shattered&mdash; 
Overlooked I all&mdash; 
Dropped&mdash;my fate&mdash;a timid Pebble&mdash; 
In thy bolder Sea&mdash; 
Prove&mdash;me&mdash;Sweet&mdash;if I regret it&mdash; 
Prove Myself&mdash;of Thee&mdash; 
All I May, If Small 
 
All I may, if small, 
Do it not display 
Larger for the Totalness&mdash; 
'Tis Economy 
To bestow a World 
And withhold a Star&mdash; 
Utmost, is Munificence&mdash; 
Less, tho' larger, poor. 
All Men For Honor Hardest Work 
All men for Honor hardest work 
But are not known to earn Paid 
after they have ceased to work 
In Infamy or Urn 
All Overgrown By Cunning Moss 
 
All overgrown by cunning moss, 
All interspersed with weed, 
The little cage of "Currer Bell" 
In quiet "Haworth" laid. 
Gathered from many wanderings&mdash; 
Gethsemane can tell 
Thro' what transporting anguish 
She reached the Asphodel! 
Soft falls the sounds of Eden 
Upon her puzzled ear&mdash; 
Oh what an afternoon for Heaven, 
When "Bronte" entered there! 
All The Letters I Can Write 
 
All the letters I can write 
Are not fair as this&mdash; 
Syllables of Velvet&mdash; 
Sentences of Plush, 
Depths of Ruby, undrained, 
Hid, Lip, for Thee&mdash; 
Play it were a Humming Bird&mdash; 
And just sipped&mdash;me&mdash; 
All These My Banners Be 
 
All these my banners be. 
I sow my pageantry 
In May&mdash; 
It rises train by train&mdash; 
Then sleeps in state again&mdash; 
My chancel&mdash;all the plain
 Today. 
To lose&mdash;if one can find again&mdash; 
To miss&mdash;if one shall meet&mdash; 
The Burglar cannot rob&mdash;then&mdash; 
The Broker cannot cheat. 
So build the hillocks gaily 
Thou little spade of mine 
Leaving nooks for Daisy 
And for Columbine&mdash; 
You and I the secret 
Of the Crocus know&mdash; 
Let us chant it softly&mdash; 
"There is no more snow!" 
To him who keeps an Orchis' heart&mdash; 
The swamps are pink with June. 
Alone, I Cannot Be 
 
Alone, I cannot be&mdash; 
For Hosts&mdash;do visit me&mdash; 
Recordless Company&mdash; 
Who baffle Key&mdash; 
They have no Robes, nor Names&mdash; 
No Almanacs&mdash;nor Climes&mdash; 
But general Homes 
Like Gnomes&mdash; 
Their Coming, may be known 
By Couriers within&mdash; 
Their going&mdash;is not&mdash; 
For they've never gone&mdash; 
Alter! When The Hills Do 
 
Alter! When the Hills do&mdash; 
Falter! When the Sun 
Question if His Glory 
Be the Perfect One&mdash; 
Surfeit! When the Daffodil 
Doth of the Dew&mdash; 
Even as Herself&mdash;Sir&mdash; 
I will&mdash;of You&mdash; 
Although I Put Away His Life 
 
Although I put away his life&mdash; 
An Ornament too grand 
For Forehead low as mine, to wear, 
This might have been the Hand 
That sowed the flower, he preferred&mdash; 
Or smoothed a homely pain, 
Or pushed the pebble from his path&mdash; 
Or played his chosen tune&mdash; 
On Lute the least&mdash;the latest&mdash; 
But just his Ear could know 
That whatsoe'er delighted it, 
I never would let go&mdash; 
The foot to bear his errand&mdash; 
A little Boot I know&mdash; 
Would leap abroad like Antelope&mdash; 
With just the grant to do&mdash; 
His weariest Commandment&mdash; 
A sweeter to obey, 
Than "Hide and Seek"&mdash; 
Or skip to Flutes&mdash; 
Or all Day, chase the Bee&mdash; 
Your Servant, Sir, will weary&mdash; 
The Surgeon, will not come&mdash; 
The World, will have its own&mdash;to do&mdash; 
The Dust, will vex your Fame&mdash; 
The Cold will force your tightest door 
Some February Day, 
But say my apron bring the sticks 
To make your Cottage gay&mdash; 
That I may take that promise 
To Paradise, with me&mdash; 
To teach the Angels, avarice, 
You, Sir, taught first&mdash;to me. 
Always Mine! 
 
Always Mine! 
No more Vacation! 
Term of Light this Day begun! 
Failless as the fair rotation 
Of the Seasons and the Sun. 
Old the Grace, but new the Subjects&mdash; 
Old, indeed, the East, 
Yet upon His Purple Programme 
Every Dawn, is first. 
Ambition Cannot Find Him 
 
Ambition cannot find him. 
Affection doesn't know 
How many leagues of nowhere 
Lie between them now. 
Yesterday, undistinguished! 
Eminent Today 
For our mutual hone, Immortality! 
Ample Make This Bed. 
Ample make this bed. 
Make this bed with awe; 
In it wait till judgment break 
Excellent and fair. 
Be its mattress straight, 
Be its pillow round; 
Let no sunrise' yellow noise 
Interrupt this ground. 
An Altered Look About The Hills 
 
An altered look about the hills&mdash; 
A Tyrian light the village fills&mdash; 
A wider sunrise in the morn&mdash; 
A deeper twilight on the lawn&mdash; 
A print of a vermillion foot&mdash; 
A purple finger on the slope&mdash; 
A flippant fly upon the pane&mdash; 
A spider at his trade again&mdash; 
An added strut in Chanticleer&mdash; 
A flower expected everywhere&mdash; 
An axe shrill singing in the woods&mdash; 
Fern odors on untravelled roads&mdash; 
All this and more I cannot tell&mdash; 
A furtive look you know as well&mdash; 
And Nicodemus' Mystery 
Receives its annual reply! 
An Antiquated Tree 
An Antiquated Tree 
Is cherished of the Crow 
Because that Junior Foliage is disrespectful now 
To venerable Birds 
Whose Corporation Coat 
Would decorate Oblivion's 
Remotest Consulate. 
An Awful Tempest Mashed The Air 
 
An awful Tempest mashed the air&mdash; 
The clouds were gaunt, and few&mdash; 
A Black&mdash;as of a Spectre's Cloak 
Hid Heaven and Earth from view. 
The creatures chuckled on the Roofs&mdash; 
And whistled in the air&mdash; 
And shook their fists&mdash; 
And gnashed their teeth&mdash; 
And swung their frenzied hair. 
The morning lit&mdash;the Birds arose&mdash; 
The Monster's faded eyes 
Turned slowly to his native coast&mdash; 
And peace&mdash;was Paradise! 
An English Breeze 
UP with the sun, the breeze arose, 
Across the talking corn she goes, 
And smooth she rustles far and wide 
Through all the voiceful countryside. 
Through all the land her tale she tells; 
She spins, she tosses, she compels 
The kites, the clouds, the windmill sails 
And all the trees in all the dales. 
God calls us, and the day prepares 
With nimble, gay and gracious airs: 
And from Penzance to Maidenhead 
The roads last night He watered. 
God calls us from inglorious ease, 
Forth and to travel with the breeze 
While, swift and singing, smooth and strong 
She gallops by the fields along. 
An Everywhere Of Silver 
An everywhere of silver, 
With ropes of sand 
To keep it from effacing 
The track called land. 
An Hour Is A Sea 
 
An Hour is a Sea 
Between a few, and me&mdash; 
With them would Harbor be&mdash; 
An Ignorance A Sunset 
 
An ignorance a Sunset 
Confer upon the Eye&mdash; 
Of Territory&mdash;Color&mdash; 
Circumference&mdash;Decay&mdash; 
Its Amber Revelation 
Exhilirate&mdash;Debase&mdash; 
Omnipotence' inspection 
Of Our inferior face&mdash; 
And when the solemn features 
Confirm&mdash;in Victory&mdash; 
We start&mdash;as if detected 
In Immortality&mdash;

Angels, In The Early Morning 
 
Angels, in the early morning 
May be seen the Dews among, 
Stooping&mdash;plucking&mdash;smiling&mdash;flying&mdash; 
Do the Buds to them belong? 
Angels, when the sun is hottest 
May be seen the sands among, 
Stooping&mdash;plucking&mdash;sighing&mdash;flying&mdash; 
Parched the flowers they bear along.

Answer July&mdash; 
Where is the Bee&mdash; 
Where is the Blush&mdash; 
Where is the Hay?

Where is the Seed&mdash;

Here&mdash;said the Year&mdash; 
Apology For Her 
 
Apology for Her 
Be rendered by the Bee&mdash; 
Herself, without a Parliament 
Apology for Me. 
Apparently With No Surprise 
Apparently with no surprise, 
To any happy flower, 
The frost beheads it at its play, 
In accidental power. 
The blond assassin passes on. 
The sun proceeds unmoved, 
To measure off another day, 
For an approving God. 
Arcturus 
"Arcturus" is his other name— 
I'd rather call him "Star." 
It's very mean of Science 
To go and interfere! 
I slew a worm the other day— 
A "Savant" passing by 
Murmured "Resurgam"—"Centipede"! 
"Oh Lord—how frail are we"! 
I pull a flower from the woods— 
A monster with a glass 
Computes the stamens in a breath— 
And has her in a "class"! 
Whereas I took the Butterfly 
Aforetime in my hat— 
He sits erect in "Cabinets"— 
The Clover bells forgot. 
What once was "Heaven" 
Is "Zenith" now— 
Where I proposed to go 
When Time's brief masquerade was done 
Is mapped and charted too. 
What if the poles should frisk about 
And stand upon their heads! 
I hope I'm ready for "the worst"— 
Whatever prank betides! 
Perhaps the "Kingdom of Heaven's" changed— 
I hope the "Children" there Won't be "new fashioned" when I come— 
And laugh at me—and stare— 
I hope the Father in the skies 
Will lift his little girl— 
Old fashioned—naught—everything— 
Over the stile of "Pearl."

Are Friends Delight Or Pain 
Are Friends Delight or Pain? 
Could Bounty but remain 
Riches were good 
But if they only stay 
Ampler to fly away 
Riches are sad. 
Artists Wrestled Here! 
 
Artists wrestled here! 
Lo, a tint Cashmere! 
Lo, a Rose! 
Student of the Year! 
For the easel here 
Say Repose! 
As By The Dead We Love To Sit 
 
As by the dead we love to sit, 
Become so wondrous dear&mdash; 
As for the lost we grapple 
Tho' all the rest are here&mdash; 
In broken mathematics 
We estimate our prize 
Vast&mdash;in its fading ration 
To our penurious eyes! 
As Children Bid The Guest "Good Night" 
 
As Children bid the Guest "Good Night" 
And then reluctant turn&mdash; 
My flowers raise their pretty lips&mdash; 
Then put their nightgowns on. 
As children caper when they wake 
Merry that it is Morn&mdash; 
My flowers from a hundred cribs 
Will peep, and prance again. 
As Everywhere Of Silver 
 
As Everywhere of Silver 
With Ropes of Sand 
To keep it from effacing 
The Track called Land. 
As Far From Pity, As Complaint 
 
As far from pity, as complaint&mdash; 
As cool to speech&mdash;as stone&mdash; 
As numb to Revelation 
As if my Trade were Bone&mdash; 
As far from time&mdash;as History&mdash; 
As near yourself&mdash;Today&mdash; 
As Children, to the Rainbow's scarf&mdash; 
Or Sunset's Yellow play 
To eyelids in the Sepulchre&mdash; 
How dumb the Dancer lies&mdash; 
While Color's Revelations break&mdash; 
And blaze&mdash;the Butterflies! 
As from the earth the light Balloon 
As from the earth the light Balloon 
Asks nothing but release Ascension 
that for which it was, 
Its soaring Residence. 
The spirit looks upon the Dust 
That fastened it so long 
With indignation, 
As a Bird 
Defrauded of its song. 
As Frost Is Best Conceived 
 
As Frost is best conceived 
By force of its Result&mdash; 
Affliction is inferred 
By subsequent effect&mdash; 
If when the sun reveal, 
The Garden keep the Gash&mdash; 
If as the Days resume 
The wilted countenance 
Cannot correct the crease 
Or counteract the stain&mdash; 
Presumption is Vitality 
Was somewhere put in twain. 
As If I Asked A Common Alms 
 
As if I asked a common Alms, 
And in my wondering hand 
A Stranger pressed a Kingdom, 
And I, bewildered, stand&mdash; 
As if I asked the Orient 
Had it for me a Morn&mdash; 
And it should lift its purple Dikes, 
And shatter me with Dawn! 
As If Some Little Arctic Flower 
 
As if some little Arctic flower 
Upon the polar hem&mdash; 
Went wandering down the Latitudes 
Until it puzzled came 
To continents of summer&mdash; 
To firmaments of sun&mdash; 
To strange, bright crowds of flowers&mdash; 
And birds, of foreign tongue! 
I say, As if this little flower 
To Eden, wandered in&mdash; 
What then? Why nothing, 
Only, your inference therefrom! 
As If The Sea Should Part 
 
As if the Sea should part 
And show a further Sea&mdash; 
And that&mdash;a further&mdash;and the Three 
But a presumption be&mdash; 
Of Periods of Seas&mdash; 
Unvisited of Shores&mdash; 
Themselves the Verge of Seas to be&mdash; 
Eternity&mdash;is Those&mdash; 
As Imperceptibly As Grief 
 
As imperceptibly as Grief 
The Summer lapsed away&mdash; 
Too imperceptible at last 
To seem like Perfidy&mdash; 
A Quietness distilled 
As Twilight long begun, 
Or Nature spending with herself 
Sequestered Afternoon&mdash; 
The Dusk drew earlier in&mdash; 
The Morning foreign shone&mdash; 
A courteous, yet harrowing Grace, 
As Guest, that would be gone&mdash; 
And thus, without a Wing 
Or service of a Keel 
Our Summer made her light escape 
Into the Beautiful. 
As old as Woe 
As old as Woe How 
old is that? 
Some eighteen thousand years As 
old as Bliss 
How old is that 
They are of equal years 
Together chiefest they ard found 
But seldom side by side 
From neither of them tho' he try 
Can Human nature hide 
As One Does Sickness Over 
 
As One does Sickness over 
In convalescent Mind, 
His scrutiny of Chances 
By blessed Health obscured&mdash; 
As One rewalks a Precipice 
And whittles at the Twig 
That held Him from Perdition 
Sown sidewise in the Crag 
A Custom of the Soul 
Far after suffering 
Identity to question 
For evidence't has been&mdash; 
As Plan For Noon And Plan For Night 
 
As plan for Noon and plan for Night 
So differ Life and Death 
In positive Prospective&mdash; 
The Foot upon the Earth 
At Distance, and Achievement, strains, 
The Foot upon the Grave 
Makes effort at conclusion 
Assisted faint of Love. 
As Sleigh Bells Seem In Summer 
 
As Sleigh Bells seem in summer 
Or Bees, at Christmas show&mdash; 
So fairy&mdash;so fictitious 
The individuals do 
Repealed from observation&mdash; 
A Party that we knew&mdash; 
More distant in an instant 
Than Dawn in Timbuctoo. 
As subtle as tomorrow 
As subtle as tomorrow 
That never came, 
A warrant, a conviction, 
Yet but a name. 
As The Starved Maelstrom Laps The Navies 
 
As the Starved Maelstrom laps the Navies 
As the Vulture teased 
Forces the Broods in lonely Valleys 
As the Tiger eased 
By but a Crumb of Blood, fasts Scarlet 
Till he meet a Man 
Dainty adorned with Veins and Tissues 
And partakes&mdash;his Tongue 
Cooled by the Morsel for a moment 
Grows a fiercer thing 
Till he esteem his Dates and Cocoa 
A Nutrition mean 
I, of a finer Famine 
Deem my Supper dry 
For but a Berry of Domingo 
And a Torrid Eye. 
As Watchers Hang Upon The East 
 
As Watchers hang upon the East, 
As Beggars revel at a feast 
By savory Fancy spread&mdash; 
As brooks in deserts babble sweet 
On ear too far for the delight, 
Heaven beguiles the tired. 
As that same watcher, when the East 
Opens the lid of Amethyst 
And lets the morning go&mdash; 
That Beggar, when an honored Guest, 
Those thirsty lips to flagons pressed, 
Heaven to us, if true. 
At Last, To Be Identified! 
 
At last, to be identified! 
At last, the lamps upon thy side 
The rest of Life to see! 
Past Midnight! Past the Morning Star! 
Past Sunrise! 
Ah, What leagues there were 
Between our feet, and Day! 
At Least—to Pray—is Left—is Left 
 
At least—to pray—is left—is left— 
Oh Jesus—in the Air— 
I know not which thy chamber is— 
I'm knocking—everywhere— 
Thou settest Earthquake in the South— 
And Maelstrom, in the Sea— 
Say, Jesus Christ of Nazareth— 
Hast thou no Arm for Me? 
Autumn&Mdash;Overlooked My Knitting 
 
Autumn&mdash;overlooked my Knitting&mdash; 
Dyes&mdash;said He&mdash;have I&mdash; 
Could disparage a Flamingo&mdash; 
Show Me them&mdash;said I&mdash; 
Cochineal&mdash;I chose&mdash;for deeming 
It resemble Thee&mdash; 
And the little Border&mdash;Dusker&mdash; 
For resembling Me&mdash; 
Awake Ye Muses Nine, Sing Me A Strain Divine 
 
Awake ye muses nine, sing me a strain divine, 
Unwind the solemn twine, and tie my Valentine! 
Oh the Earth was made for lovers, for damsel, and hopeless swain, 
For sighing, and gentle whispering, and unity made of twain. 
All things do go a courting, in earth, or sea, or air, 
God hath made nothing single but thee in His world so fair! 
The bride, and then the bridegroom, the two, and then the one, 
Adam, and Eve, his consort, the moon, and then the sun; 
The life doth prove the precept, who obey shall happy be, 
Who will not serve the sovereign, be hanged on fatal tree. 
The high do seek the lowly, the great do seek the small, 
None cannot find who seeketh, on this terrestrial ball; 
The bee doth court the flower, the flower his suit receives, 
And they make merry wedding, whose guests are hundred leaves; 
The wind doth woo the branches, the branches they are won, 
And the father fond demandeth the maiden for his son. 
The storm doth walk the seashore humming a mournful tune, 
The wave with eye so pensive, looketh to see the moon, 
Their spirits meet together, they make their solemn vows, 
No more he singeth mournful, her sadness she doth lose. 
The worm doth woo the mortal, death claims a living bride, 
Night unto day is married, morn unto eventide; 
Earth is a merry damsel, and heaven a knight so true, 
And Earth is quite coquettish, and beseemeth in vain to sue. 
Now to the application, to the reading of the roll, 
To bringing thee to justice, and marshalling thy soul: 
Thou art a human solo, a being cold, and lone, 
Wilt have no kind companion, thou reap'st what thou hast sown. 
Hast never silent hours, and minutes all too long, 
And a deal of sad reflection, and wailing instead of song? 
There's Sarah, and Eliza, and Emeline so fair, 
And Harriet, and Susan, and she with curling hair! 
Thine eyes are sadly blinded, but yet thou mayest see 
Six true, and comely maidens sitting upon the tree; 
Approach that tree with caution, then up it boldly climb, 
And seize the one thou lovest, nor care for space, or time! 
Then bear her to the greenwood, and build for her a bower, 
And give her what she asketh, jewel, or bird, or flower&mdash; 
And bring the fife, and trumpet, and beat upon the drum&mdash; 
And bid the world Goodmorrow, and go to glory home! 
Away From Home Are Some And I— 
 
Away from Home are some and I— 
An Emigrant to be 
In a Metropolis of Homes 
Is easy, possibly— 
The Habit of a Foreign Sky 
We—difficult—acquire 
As Children, who remain in Face 
The more their Feet retire. 
Baffled For Just A Day Or Two 
 
Baffled for just a day or two&mdash; 
Embarrassed&mdash;not afraid&mdash; 
Encounter in my garden 
An unexpected Maid. 
She beckons, and the woods start&mdash; 
She nods, and all begin&mdash; 
Surely, such a country 
I was never in! 
Banish Air From Air&Mdash; 
 
Banish Air from Air&mdash; 
Divide Light if you dare&mdash; 
They'll meet 
While Cubes in a Drop 
Or Pellets of Shape 
Fit 
Films cannot annul 
Odors return whole 
Force Flame 
And with a Blonde push 
Over your impotence 
Flits Steam. 
Be Mine The Doom&Mdash; 
 
Be Mine the Doom&mdash; 
Sufficient Fame&mdash; 
To perish in Her Hand! 
Beauty&Mdash;Be Not Caused&Mdash;It Is 
 
Beauty&mdash;be not caused&mdash;It Is&mdash; 
Chase it, and it ceases&mdash; 
Chase it not, and it abides&mdash; 
Overtake the Creases 
In the Meadow&mdash;when the Wind 
Runs his fingers thro' it&mdash; 
Deity will see to it 
That You never do it&mdash; 
Because I Could Not Stop For Death 
Because I could not stop for Death-
He kindly stopped for me-
The Carriage held but just Ourselves-
And Immortality. 
We slowly drove- He knew no haste 
And I had put away 
My labor and my leisure too, 
For His Civility-
We passed the School, where Children strove 
At Recess- in the Ring-
We passed the Fields of Gazing Grain-
We passed the Setting Sun-
Or rather- He passed us-
The Dews drew quivering and chill-
For only Gossamer, my Gown-
My Tippet- only Tulle-
We paused before a House that seemed 
A Swelling of the Ground-
The Roof was scarcely visible-
The Cornice- in the Ground-
Since then- 'tis Centuries- and yet 
Feels shorter than the Day 
I first surmised the Horses' Heads 
Were toward Eternity-
Because The Bee May Blameless Hum 
 
Because the Bee may blameless hum 
For Thee a Bee do I become 
List even unto Me. 
Because the Flowers unafraid 
May lift a look on thine, a Maid 
Alway a Flower would be. 
Nor Robins, Robins need not hide 
When Thou upon their Crypts intrude 
So Wings bestow on Me 
Or Petals, or a Dower of Buzz 
That Bee to ride, or Flower of Furze 
I that way worship Thee. 
Beclouded 
The sky is low, the clouds are mean, 
A travelling flake of snow 
Across a barn or through a rut 
Debates if it will go. 
A narrow wind complains all day 
How some one treated him; 
Nature, like us, is sometimes caught 
Without her diadem. 
Bee! I'M Expecting You! 
 
Bee! I'm expecting you! 
Was saying Yesterday 
To Somebody you know 
That you were due&mdash; 
The Frogs got Home last Week&mdash; 
Are settled, and at work&mdash; 
Birds, mostly back&mdash; 
The Clover warm and thick&mdash; 
You'll get my Letter by 
The seventeenth; Reply 
Or better, be with me&mdash; 
Yours, Fly. 
Before He Comes We Weigh The Time! 
 
Before He comes we weigh the Time! 
'Tis Heavy and 'tis Light. 
When He depart, an Emptiness 
Is the prevailing Freight. 
Before I Got My Eye Put Out 
 
Before I got my eye put out 
I liked as well to see&mdash; 
As other Creatures, that have Eyes 
And know no other way&mdash; 
But were it told to me&mdash;Today&mdash; 
That I might have the sky 
For mine&mdash;I tell you that my Heart 
Would split, for size of me&mdash; 
The Meadows&mdash;mine&mdash; 
The Mountains&mdash;mine&mdash; 
All Forests&mdash;Stintless Stars&mdash; 
As much of Noon as I could take 
Between my finite eyes&mdash; 
The Motions of the Dipping Birds&mdash; 
The Morning's Amber Road&mdash; 
For mine&mdash;to look at when I liked&mdash; 
The News would strike me dead&mdash; 
So safer&mdash;guess&mdash;with just my soul 
Upon the Window pane&mdash; 
Where other Creatures put their eyes&mdash; 
Incautious&mdash;of the Sun&mdash; 
Before The Ice Is In The Pools 
 
Before the ice is in the pools&mdash; 
Before the skaters go, 
Or any check at nightfall 
Is tarnished by the snow&mdash; 
Before the fields have finished, 
Before the Christmas tree, 
Wonder upon wonder 
Will arrive to me! 
What we touch the hems of 
On a summer's day&mdash; 
What is only walking 
Just a bridge away&mdash; 
That which sings so&mdash;speaks so&mdash; 
When there's no one here&mdash; 
Will the frock I wept in 
Answer me to wear? 
Before You Thought Of Spring, 
Before you thought of spring, 
Except as a surmise, 
You see, God bless his suddenness, 
A fellow in the skies 
Of independent hues, 
A little weather-worn, 
Inspiriting habiliments 
Of indigo and brown. 
With specimens of song, 
As if for you to choose, 
Discretion in the interval, 
With gay delays he goes 
To some superior tree 
Without a single leaf, 
And shouts for joy to nobody 
But his seraphic self! 
Behind Me Dips Eternity 
 
Behind Me—dips Eternity— 
Before Me—Immortality— 
Myself—the Term between— 
Death but the Drift of Eastern Gray, 
Dissolving into Dawn away, 
Before the West begin— 
'Tis Kingdoms—afterward—they say— 
In perfect—pauseless Monarchy— 
Whose Prince—is Son of None— 
Himself—His Dateless Dynasty— 
Himself—Himself diversify— 
In Duplicate divine— 
'Tis Miracle before Me—then— 
'Tis Miracle behind—between— 
A Crescent in the Sea— 
With Midnight to the North of Her— 
And Midnight to the South of Her— 
And Maelstrom—in the Sky— 
Bereaved Of All, I Went Abroad 
 
Bereaved of all, I went abroad&mdash; 
No less bereaved was I 
Upon a New Peninsula&mdash; 
The Grave preceded me&mdash; 
Obtained my Lodgings, ere myself&mdash; 
And when I sought my Bed&mdash; 
The Grave it was reposed upon 
The Pillow for my Head&mdash; 
I waked to find it first awake&mdash; 
I rose&mdash;It followed me&mdash; 
I tried to drop it in the Crowd&mdash; 
To lose it in the Sea&mdash; 
In Cups of artificial Drowse 
To steep its shape away&mdash; 
The Grave&mdash;was finished&mdash;but the Spade 
Remained in Memory&mdash; 
Bereavement In Their Death To Feel 
 
Bereavement in their death to feel 
Whom We have never seen&mdash; 
A Vital Kinsmanship import 
Our Soul and theirs&mdash;between&mdash; 
For Stranger&mdash;Strangers do not mourn&mdash; 
There be Immortal friends 
Whom Death see first&mdash;'tis news of this 
That paralyze Ourselves&mdash; 
Who, vital only to Our Thought&mdash; 
Such Presence bear away 
In dying&mdash;'tis as if Our Souls 
Absconded&mdash;suddenly&mdash; 
Besides The Autumn Poets Sing 
 
Besides the Autumn poets sing 
A few prosaic days

Mesmeric fingers softly touch 
The Eyes of many Elves&mdash; 
Perhaps a squirrel may remain&mdash; 
My sentiments to share&mdash; 
Grant me, Oh Lord, a sunny mind&mdash; 
Thy windy will to bear!

Best Witchcraft is Geometry 
To the magician's mind His 
ordinary acts are feats 
To thinking of mankind. 
Better—than Music! For I—who Heard It 
 
Better—than Music! For I—who heard it— 
I was used—to the Birds—before— 
This—was different—'Twas Translation— 
Of all tunes I knew—and more— 
'Twasn't contained—like other stanza— 
No one could play it—the second time— 
But the Composer—perfect Mozart— 
Perish with him—that Keyless Rhyme! 
So—Children—told how Brooks in Eden— 
Bubbled a better—Melody— 
Quaintly infer—Eve's great surrender— 
Urging the feet—that would—not—fly— 
Children—matured—are wiser—mostly— 
Eden—a legend—dimly told— 
Eve—and the Anguish—Grandame's story— 
But—I was telling a tune—I heard— 
Not such a strain—the Church—baptizes— 
When the last Saint—goes up the Aisles— 
Not such a stanza splits the silence— 
When the Redemption strikes her Bells— 
Let me not spill—its smallest cadence— 
Humming—for promise—when alone— 
Humming—until my faint Rehearsal— 
Drop into tune—around the Throne— 
Between My Country—and The Others 
Between My Country—and the Others— 
There is a Sea— 
But Flowers—negotiate between us— 
As Ministry. 
Bird 
A bird came down the walk: 
He did not know I saw; 
He bit an angle-worm in halves 
And ate the fellow, raw. 
And then he drank a dew 
From a convenient grass, 
And the hopped sideways to the wall 
To let a beetle pass. 
He glanced with rapid eyes 
That hurried all abroad, They 
looked like frightened beads, I thought 
He stirred his velvet head. 
Like one in danger; cautious, 
I offered him a crumb, 
And he unrolled his feathers 
And rolled him softer home 
Then oars divide the ocean, 
Too silver for a seam, 
Or butterflies, off banks of noon, 
Leap, plashless, as they swim. 
Blazing In Gold And Quenching In Purple 
 
Blazing in Gold and quenching in Purple 
Leaping like Leopards to the Sky 
Then at the feet of the old Horizon 
Laying her spotted Face to die 
Stooping as low as the Otter's Window 
Touching the Roof and tinting the Barn 
Kissing her Bonnet to the Meadow 
And the Juggler of Day is gone 
Bless God, He Went As Soldiers 
 
Bless God, he went as soldiers, 
His musket on his breast&mdash; 
Grant God, he charge the bravest 
Of all the martial blest! 
Please God, might I behold him 
In epauletted white&mdash; 
I should not fear the foe then&mdash; 
I should not fear the fight! 
Bloom Upon The Mountain—stated 
 
Bloom upon the Mountain—stated— 
Blameless of a Name— 
Efflorescence of a Sunset— 
Reproduced—the same— 
Seed, had I, my Purple Sowing 
Should endow the Day— 
Not a Topic of a Twilight— 
Show itself away— 
Who for tilling—to the Mountain 
Come, and disappear— 
Whose be Her Renown, or fading, 
Witness, is not here— 
While I state—the Solemn Petals, 
Far as North—and East, 
Far as South and West—expanding— 
Culminate—in Rest— 
And the Mountain to the Evening 
Fit His Countenance— 
Indicating, by no Muscle— 
The Experience— 
Bound&Mdash;A Trouble 
 
Bound&mdash;a trouble&mdash; 
And lives can bear it! 
Limit&mdash;how deep a bleeding go! 
So&mdash;many&mdash;drops&mdash;of vital scarlet&mdash; 
Deal with the soul 
As with Algebra! 
Tell it the Ages&mdash;to a cypher&mdash; 
And it will ache&mdash;contented&mdash;on&mdash; 
Sing&mdash;at its pain&mdash;as any Workman&mdash; 
Notching the fall of the Even Sun! 
Bring Me The Sunset In A Cup 
 
Bring me the sunset in a cup, 
Reckon the morning's flagons up 
And say how many Dew, 
Tell me how far the morning leaps&mdash; 
Tell me what time the weaver sleeps 
Who spun the breadth of blue! 
Write me how many notes there be 
In the new Robin's ecstasy 
Among astonished boughs&mdash; 
How many trips the Tortoise makes&mdash; 
How many cups the Bee partakes, 
The Debauchee of Dews! 
Also, who laid the Rainbow's piers, 
Also, who leads the docile spheres 
By withes of supple blue? 
Whose fingers string the stalactite&mdash; 
Who counts the wampum of the night 
To see that none is due? 
Who built this little Alban House 
And shut the windows down so close 
My spirit cannot see? 
Who'll let me out some gala day 
With implements to fly away, 
Passing Pomposity? 
But Little Carmine Hath Her Face 
 
But little Carmine hath her face&mdash; 
Of Emerald scant&mdash;her Gown&mdash; 
Her Beauty&mdash;is the love she doth&mdash; 
Itself&mdash;exhibit&mdash;Mine&mdash; 
By A Flower—by A Letter 
 
By a flower—By a letter— 
By a nimble love— 
If I weld the Rivet faster— 
Final fast—above— 
Never mind my breathless Anvil! 
Never mind Repose! 
Never mind the sooty faces 
Tugging at the Forge! 
By Chivalries As Tiny 
 
By Chivalries as tiny, 
A Blossom, or a Book, 
The seeds of smiles are planted&mdash; 
Which blossom in the dark. 
By homely gift and hindered Words 
By homely gift and hindered Words 
The human heart is told 
Of Nothing '
Nothing' is the force 
That renovates the World 
By My Window Have I For Scenery 
 
By my Window have I for Scenery 
Just a Sea&mdash;with a Stem&mdash; 
If the Bird and the Farmer&mdash;deem it a "Pine"&mdash; 
The Opinion will serve&mdash;for them&mdash; 
It has no Port, nor a "Line"&mdash;but the Jays&mdash; 
That split their route to the Sky&mdash; 
Or a Squirrel, whose giddy Peninsula 
May be easier reached&mdash;this way&mdash; 
For Inlands&mdash;the Earth is the under side&mdash; 
And the upper side&mdash;is the Sun&mdash; 
And its Commerce&mdash;if Commerce it have&mdash; 
Of Spice&mdash;I infer from the Odors borne&mdash; 
Of its Voice&mdash;to affirm&mdash;when the Wind is within&mdash;

By The Sea 
I started early, took my dog, 
And visited the sea; 
The mermaids in the basement 
Came out to look at me. 
And frigates in the upper floor 
Extended hempen hands, 
Presuming me to be a mouse 
Aground, upon the sands. 
But no man moved me till the tide 
Went past my simple shoe, 
And past my apron and my belt, 
And past my bodice too, 
And made as he would eat me up 
As wholly as a dew 
Upon a dandelion's sleeve And 
then I started too. 
And he - he followed close behind; 
I felt his silver heel 
Upon my ankle, - then my shoes 
Would overflow with pearl. 
Until we met the solid town, 
No man he seemed to know; 
And bowing with a mighty look 
At me, the sea withdrew. 
Chartless 
I never saw a moor, 
I never saw the sea; 
Yet now I know how the heather looks, 
And what a wave must be. 
I never spoke with God, 
Nor visited in Heaven; 
Yet certain am I of the spot 
As if the chart were given.

Nor suppressed&mdash;with Balm&mdash;

Dare you see a Soul at the White Heat?

Dear March - Come in 
DEAR March, come in!	 
How glad I am!	 
I looked for you before.	 
Put down your hat—	 
You must have walked—	
How out of breath you are!	 
Dear March, how are you?	 
And the rest?	 
Did you leave Nature well?	 
Oh, March, come right upstairs with me,	
I have so much to tell!	 
I got your letter, and the bird's;	 
The maples never knew	 
That you were coming,—I declare,	 
How red their faces grew!	
But, March, forgive me—	 
And all those hills	 
You left for me to hue;	 
There was no purple suitable,	 
You took it all with you.	
Who knocks? That April!	 
Lock the door!	 
I will not be pursued!	 
He stayed away a year, to call	 
When I am occupied.	
But trifles look so trivial	 
As soon as you have come,	 
That blame is just as dear as praise	 
And praise as mere as blame.

Death is like the insect

the tree and leave it, 
'Tis the vermin's will.

For interrupting tears 
Obliterate the etchings 
Too costly for repairs.
