And shape my Hands&mdash; 
Petition's way, 
Tho' ignorant of a word 
That Ordination&mdash;utters&mdash; 
My Business, with the Cloud, 
If any Power behind it, be, 
Not subject to Despair&mdash; 
It care, in some remoter way, 
For so minute affair 
As Misery&mdash; 
Itself, too vast, for interrupting&mdash;more&mdash; 
I Had A Guinea Golden 
 
I had a guinea golden&mdash; 
I lost it in the sand&mdash; 
And tho' the sum was simple 
And pounds were in the land&mdash; 
Still, had it such a value 
Unto my frugal eye&mdash; 
That when I could not find it&mdash; 
I sat me down to sigh. 
I had a crimson Robin&mdash; 
Who sang full many a day 
But when the woods were painted, 
He, too, did fly away&mdash; 
Time brought me other Robins&mdash; 
Their ballads were the same&mdash; 
Still, for my missing Troubador 
I kept the "house at hame." 
I had a star in heaven&mdash; 
One "Pleiad" was its name&mdash; 
And when I was not heeding, 
It wandered from the same. 
And tho' the skies are crowded&mdash; 
And all the night ashine&mdash; 
I do not care about it&mdash; 
Since none of them are mine. 
My story has a moral&mdash; 
I have a missing friend&mdash; 
"Pleiad" its name, and Robin, 
And guinea in the sand. 
And when this mournful ditty 
Accompanied with tear&mdash; 
Shall meet the eye of traitor 
In country far from here&mdash; 
Grant that repentance solemn 
May seize upon his mind&mdash; 
And he no consolation 
Beneath the sun may find. 
I Had Been Hungry All The Years-
I had been hungry all the years-
My noon had come, to dine-
I, trembling, drew the table near 
And touched the curious wine. 
'T was this on tables I had seen 
When turning, hungry, lone, 
I looked in windows, for the wealth 
I could not hope to own. 
I did not know the ample bread, 
'T was so unlike the crumb 
The birds and I had often shared 
In Nature's dining-room. 
The plenty hurt me, 't was so new,-Myself 
felt ill and odd, 
As berry of a mountain bush 
Transplanted to the road. 
Nor was I hungry; so I found 
That hunger was a way 
Of persons outside windows, 
The entering takes away. 
I Had No Cause To Be Awake 
 
I had no Cause to be awake&mdash; 
My Best&mdash;was gone to sleep&mdash; 
And Morn a new politeness took&mdash; 
And failed to wake them up&mdash; 
But called the others&mdash;clear&mdash; 
And passed their Curtains by&mdash; 
Sweet Morning&mdash;when I oversleep&mdash; 
Knock&mdash;Recollect&mdash;to Me&mdash; 
I looked at Sunrise&mdash;Once&mdash; 
And then I looked at Them&mdash; 
And wishfulness in me arose&mdash; 
For Circumstance the same&mdash; 
'Twas such an Ample Peace&mdash; 
It could not hold a Sigh&mdash; 
'Twas Sabbath&mdash;with the Bells divorced&mdash; 
'Twas Sunset&mdash;all the Day&mdash; 
So choosing but a Gown&mdash; 
And taking but a Prayer&mdash; 
The only Raiment I should need&mdash; 
I struggled&mdash;and was There&mdash; 
I Had No Time To Hate, Because 
I had no time to hate, because 
The grave would hinder me, 
And life was not so ample I 
Could finish enmity. 
Nor had I time to love, but since 
Some industry must be, 
The little toil of love, I thought, 
Was large enough for me. 
I Had Not Minded—walls 
 
I had not minded—Walls— 
Were Universe—one Rock— 
And fr I heard his silver Call 
The other side the Block— 
I'd tunnel—till my Groove 
Pushed sudden thro' to his— 
Then my face take her Recompense— 
The looking in his Eyes— 
But 'tis a single Hair— 
A filament—a law— 
A Cobweb—wove in Adamant— 
A Battlement—of Straw— 
A limit like the Veil 
Unto the Lady's face— 
But every Mesh—a Citadel— 
And Dragons—in the Crease— 
I Had Some Things That I Called Mine 
 
I had some things that I called mine&mdash; 
And God, that he called his, 
Till, recently a rival Claim 
Disturbed these amities. 
The property, my garden, 
Which having sown with care, 
He claims the pretty acre, 
And sends a Bailiff there. 
The station of the parties 
Forbids publicity, 
But Justice is sublimer 
Than arms, or pedigree. 
I'll institute an "Action"&mdash; 
I'll vindicate the law&mdash; 
Jove! Choose your counsel&mdash; 
I retain "Shaw"! 
I Had The Glory—that Will Do 
 
I had the Glory—that will do— 
An Honor, Thought can turn her to 
When lesser Fames invite— 
With one long "Nay"— 
Bliss' early shape 
Deforming—Dwindling—Gulfing up— 
Time's possibility. 
I Have A Bird In Spring 
 
I have a Bird in spring 
Which for myself doth sing&mdash; 
The spring decoys. 
And as the summer nears&mdash; 
And as the Rose appears, 
Robin is gone. 
Yet do I not repine 
Knowing that Bird of mine 
Though flown&mdash; 
Learneth beyond the sea 
Melody new for me 
And will return. 
Fast is a safer hand 
Held in a truer Land 
Are mine&mdash; 
And though they now depart, 
Tell I my doubting heart 
They're thine. 
In a serener Bright, 
In a more golden light 
I see 
Each little doubt and fear, 
Each little discord here 
Removed. 
Then will I not repine, 
Knowing that Bird of mine 
Though flown 
Shall in a distant tree 
Bright melody for me 
Return. 
I Have A King, Who Does Not Speak 
 
I have a King, who does not speak&mdash; 
So&mdash;wondering&mdash;thro' the hours meek 
I trudge the day away&mdash; 
Half glad when it is night, and sleep, 
If, haply, thro' a dream, to peep 
In parlors, shut by day. 
And if I do&mdash;when morning comes&mdash; 
It is as if a hundred drums 
Did round my pillow roll, 
And shouts fill all my Childish sky, 
And Bells keep saying "Victory" 
From steeples in my soul! 
And if I don't&mdash;the little Bird 
Within the Orchard, is not heard, 
And I omit to pray 
"Father, thy will be done" today 
For my will goes the other way, 
And it were perjury! 
I Have Never Seen "Volcanoes" 
 
I have never seen "Volcanoes"&mdash; 
But, when Travellers tell 
How those old&mdash;phlegmatic mountains 
Usually so still&mdash; 
Bear within&mdash;appalling Ordnance, 
Fire, and smoke, and gun, 
Taking Villages for breakfast, 
And appalling Men&mdash; 
If the stillness is Volcanic 
In the human face 
When upon a pain Titanic 
Features keep their place&mdash; 
If at length the smouldering anguish 
Will not overcome&mdash; 
And the palpitating Vineyard 
In the dust, be thrown? 
If some loving Antiquary, 
On Resumption Morn, 
Will not cry with joy "Pompeii"! 
To the Hills return! 
I Have No Life But This 
I have no life but this, 
To lead it here; 
Nor any death, but lest 
Dispelled from there; 
Nor tie to earths to come, 
Nor action new, 
Except through this extent, 
The Realm of You! 
I Haven'T Told My Garden Yet 
 
I haven't told my garden yet&mdash; 
Lest that should conquer me. 
I haven't quite the strength now 
To break it to the Bee&mdash; 
I will not name it in the street 
For shops would stare at me&mdash; 
That one so shy&mdash;so ignorant 
Should have the face to die. 
The hillsides must not know it&mdash; 
Where I have rambled so&mdash; 
Nor tell the loving forests 
The day that I shall go&mdash; 
Nor lisp it at the table&mdash; 
Nor heedless by the way 
Hint that within the Riddle 
One will walk today&mdash; 
I Heard A Fly Buzz When I Died; 
I heard a fly buzz when I died; 
The stillness round my form 
Was like the stillness in the air 
Between the heaves of storm. 
The eyes beside had wrung them dry, 
And breaths were gathering sure 
For that last onset, when the king 
Be witnessed in his power. 
I willed my keepsakes, signed away 
What portion of me I 
Could make assignable,--and then 
There interposed a fly, 
With blue, uncertain, stumbling buzz, 
Between the light and me; 
And then the windows failed, and then 
I could not see to see. 
I Held A Jewel In My Fingers 
I held a Jewel in my fingers— 
And went to sleep— 
The day was warm, and winds were prosy— 
I said ''Twill keep'— 
I woke—and chid my honest fingers, 
The Gem was gone— 
And now, an Amethyst remembrance 
Is all I own— 
I Hide Myself Within My Flower 
 
I hide myself within my flower, 
That fading from your Vase, 
You, unsuspecting, feel for me&mdash; 
Almost a loneliness. 
I Keep My Pledge 
 
I keep my pledge. 
I was not called&mdash; 
Death did not notice me. 
I bring my Rose. 
I plight again, 
By every sainted Bee&mdash; 
By Daisy called from hillside&mdash; 
by Bobolink from lane. 
Blossom and I&mdash; 
Her oath, and mine&mdash; 
Will surely come again. 
I Know A Place Where Summer Strives 
I know a place where summer strives 
With such a practised frost, 
She each year leads her daisies back, 
Recording briefly, 'Lost.' 
But when the south wind stirs the pools 
And struggles in the lanes, 
Her heart misgives her for her vow, 
And she pours soft refrains 
Into the lap of adamant, 
And spices, and the dew, 
That stiffens quietly to quartz 
Upon her amber shoe. 
I Know Lives, I Could Miss 
 
I know lives, I could miss 
Without a Misery&mdash; 
Others&mdash;whose instant's wanting&mdash; 
Would be Eternity&mdash; 
The last&mdash;a scanty Number&mdash; 
'Twould scarcely fill a Two&mdash; 
The first&mdash;a Gnat's Horizon 
Could easily outgrow&mdash; 
I Know Some Lonely Houses Off The Road 
 
I know some lonely Houses off the Road 
A Robber'd like the look of&mdash; 
Wooden barred, 
And Windows hanging low, 
Inviting to&mdash; 
A Portico, 
Where two could creep&mdash; 
One&mdash;hand the Tools&mdash; 
The other peep&mdash; 
To make sure All's Asleep&mdash; 
Old fashioned eyes&mdash; 
Not easy to surprise! 
How orderly the Kitchen'd look, by night, 
With just a Clock&mdash; 
But they could gag the Tick&mdash; 
And Mice won't bark&mdash; 
And so the Walls&mdash;don't tell&mdash; 
None&mdash;will&mdash; 
A pair of Spectacles ajar just stir&mdash; 
An Almanac's aware&mdash; 
Was it the Mat&mdash;winked, 
Or a Nervous Star? 
The Moon&mdash;slides down the stair, 
To see who's there! 
There's plunder&mdash;where&mdash; 
Tankard, or Spoon&mdash; 
Earring&mdash;or Stone&mdash; 
A Watch&mdash;Some Ancient Brooch 
To match the Grandmama&mdash; 
Staid sleeping&mdash;there&mdash; 
Day&mdash;rattles&mdash;too 
Stealth's&mdash;slow&mdash; 
The Sun has got as far 
As the third Sycamore&mdash; 
Screams Chanticleer 
"Who's there"? 
And Echoes&mdash;Trains away, 
Sneer&mdash;"Where"! 
While the old Couple, just astir, 
Fancy the Sunrise&mdash;left the door ajar! 
I Know That He Exists 
 
I know that He exists. 
Somewhere&mdash;in Silence&mdash; 
He has hid his rare life 
From our gross eyes. 
'Tis an instant's play. 
'Tis a fond Ambush&mdash; 
Just to make Bliss 
Earn her own surprise! 
But&mdash;should the play 
Prove piercing earnest&mdash; 
Should the glee&mdash;glaze&mdash; 
In Death's&mdash;stiff&mdash;stare&mdash; 
Would not the fun 
Look too expensive! 
Would not the jest&mdash; 
Have crawled too far! 
I Know Where Wells Grow—droughtless Wells 
 
I know where Wells grow—Droughtless Wells— 
Deep dug—for Summer days— 
Where Mosses go no more away— 
And Pebble—safely plays— 
It's made of Fathoms—and a Belt— 
A Belt of jagged Stone— 
Inlaid with Emerald—half way down— 
And Diamonds—jumbled on— 
It has no Bucket—Were I rich 
A Bucket I would buy— 
I'm often thirsty—but my lips 
Are so high up—You see— 
I read in an Old fashioned Book 
That People "thirst no more"— 
The Wells have Buckets to them there— 
It must mean that—I'm sure— 
Shall We remember Parching—then? 
Those Waters sound so grand— 
I think a little Well—like Mine— 
Dearer to understand— 
I Learned—at Least—what Home Could Be 
 
I learned—at least—what Home could be— 
How ignorant I had been 
Of pretty ways of Covenant— 
How awkward at the Hymn 
Round our new Fireside—but for this— 
This pattern—of the Way— 
Whose Memory drowns me, like the Dip 
Of a Celestial Sea— 
What Mornings in our Garden—guessed— 
What Bees—for us—to hum— 
With only Birds to interrupt 
The Ripple of our Theme— 
And Task for Both— 
When Play be done— 
Your Problem—of the Brain— 
And mine—some foolisher effect— 
A Ruffle—or a Tune— 
The Afternoons—Together spent— 
And Twilight—in the Lanes— 
Some ministry to poorer lives— 
Seen poorest—thro' our gains— 
And then Return—and Night—and Home— 
And then away to You to pass— 
A new—diviner—care— 
Till Sunrise take us back to Scene— 
Transmuted—Vivider— 
This seems a Home— 
And Home is not— 
But what that Place could be— 
Afflicts me—as a Setting Sun— 
Where Dawn—knows how to be— 
I Like A Look Of Agony 
 
I like a look of Agony, 
Because I know it's true&mdash; 
Men do not sham Convulsion, 
Nor simulate, a Throe&mdash; 
The Eyes glaze once&mdash;and that is Death&mdash; 
Impossible to feign 
The Beads upon the Forehead 
By homely Anguish strung. 
I Like To See It Lap The Miles, 
I like to see it lap the miles, 
And lick the valleys up, 
And stop to feed itself at tanks; 
And then, prodigious, step 
Around a pile of mountains, 
And, supercilious, peer 
In shanties by the sides of roads; 
And then a quarry pare 
To fit its sides, and crawl between, 
Complaining all the while 
In horrid, hooting stanza; 
Then chase itself down hill 
And neigh like Boanerges; 
Then, punctual as a star, 
Stop--docile and omnipotent-At 
its own stable door. 
I Live With Him—i See His Face 
 
I live with Him—I see His face— 
I go no more away 
For Visitor—or Sundown— 
Death's single privacy 
The Only One—forestalling Mine— 
And that—by Right that He 
Presents a Claim invisible— 
No wedlock—granted Me— 
I live with Him—I hear His Voice— 
I stand alive—Today— 
To witness to the Certainty 
Of Immortality— 
Taught Me—by Time—the lower Way— 
Conviction—Every day— 
That Life like This—is stopless— 
Be Judgment—what it may— 
I Lived On Dread 
 
I lived on Dread&mdash; 
To Those who know 
The Stimulus there is 
In Danger&mdash;Other impetus 
Is numb&mdash;and Vitalless&mdash; 
As 'twere a Spur&mdash;upon the Soul&mdash; 
A Fear will urge it where 
To go without the Sceptre's aid 
Were Challenging Despair. 
I Lived On Dread; To Those Who Know 
I lived on dread; to those who know 
The stimulus there is 
In danger, other impetus 
Is numb and vital-less. 
As't were a spur upon the soul, 
A fear will urge it where 
To go without the spectre's aid 
Were challenging despair. 
I Lost A World - The Other Day! 
 
I lost a World - the other day! 
Has Anybody found? 
You'll know it by the Row of Stars 
Around its forehead bound. 
A Rich man&mdash;might not notice it&mdash; 
Yet&mdash;to my frugal Eye, 
Of more Esteem than Ducats&mdash; 
Oh find it&mdash;Sir&mdash;for me! 
I Made Slow Riches But My Gain 
 
I made slow Riches but my Gain 
Was steady as the Sun 
And every Night, it numbered more 
Than the preceding One 
All Days, I did not earn the same 
But my perceiveless Gain 
Inferred the less by Growing than 
The Sum that it had grown. 
I Make His Crescent Fill Or Lack 
 
I make His Crescent fill or lack&mdash; 
His Nature is at Full 
Or Quarter&mdash;as I signify&mdash; 
His Tides&mdash;do I control&mdash; 
He holds superior in the Sky 
Or gropes, at my Command 
Behind inferior Clouds&mdash;or round 
A Mist's slow Colonnade&mdash; 
But since We hold a Mutual Disc&mdash; 
And front a Mutual Day&mdash; 
Which is the Despot, neither knows&mdash; 
Nor Whose&mdash;the Tyranny&mdash; 
I Many Times Thought Peace Had Come 
I many times thought Peace had come 
When Peace was far away— 
As Wrecked Men—deem they sight the Land— 
At Centre of the Sea— 
And struggle slacker—but to prove 
As hopelessly as I— 
How many the fictitious Shores— 
Before the Harbor be— 
I Meant To Find Her When I Came 
 
I meant to find Her when I came&mdash; 
Death&mdash;had the same design&mdash; 
But the Success&mdash;was His&mdash;it seems&mdash; 
And the Surrender&mdash;Mine&mdash; 
I meant to tell Her how I longed 
For just this single time&mdash; 
But Death had told Her so the first&mdash; 
And she had past, with Him&mdash; 
To wander&mdash;now&mdash;is my Repose&mdash; 
To rest&mdash;To rest would be 
A privilege of Hurricane 
To Memory&mdash;and Me. 
I Meant To Have But Modest Needs 
 
I meant to have but modest needs&mdash; 
Such as Content&mdash;and Heaven&mdash; 
Within my income&mdash;these could lie 
And Life and I&mdash;keep even&mdash; 
But since the last&mdash;included both&mdash; 
It would suffice my Prayer 
But just for One&mdash;to stipulate&mdash; 
And Grace would grant the Pair&mdash; 
And so&mdash;upon this wise&mdash;I prayed&mdash; 
Great Spirit&mdash;Give to me 
A Heaven not so large as Yours, 
But large enough&mdash;for me&mdash; 
A Smile suffused Jehovah's face&mdash; 
The Cherubim&mdash;withdrew&mdash; 
Grave Saints stole out to look at me&mdash; 
And showed their dimples&mdash;too&mdash; 
I left the Place, with all my might&mdash; 
I threw my Prayer away&mdash; 
The Quiet Ages picked it up&mdash; 
And Judgment&mdash;twinkled&mdash;too&mdash; 
Tat one so honest&mdash;be extant&mdash; 
It take the Tale for true&mdash; 
That "Whatsoever Ye shall ask&mdash; 
Itself be given You"&mdash; 
But I, grown shrewder&mdash;scan the Skies 
With a suspicious Air&mdash; 
As Children&mdash;swindled for the first 
All Swindlers&mdash;be&mdash;infer&mdash; 
I Measure Every Grief I Meet (561) 
I measure every Grief I meet 
With narrow, probing, Eyes-I 
wonder if It weighs like Mine-Or 
has an Easier size. 
I wonder if They bore it long-Or 
did it just begin-I 
could not tell the Date of Mine-It 
feels so old a pain-
I wonder if it hurts to live-And 
if They have to try-And 
whether--could They choose between-It 
would not be--to die-
I note that Some--gone patient long-At 
length, renew their smile-An 
imitation of a Light 
That has so little Oil-
I wonder if when Years have piled-Some 
Thousands--on the Harm-That 
hurt them early--such a lapse 
Could give them any Balm-
Or would they go on aching still 
Through Centuries of Nerve-Enlightened 
to a larger Pain-In 
Contrast with the Love-
The Grieved--are many--I am told-There 
is the various Cause-Death--
is but one--and comes but once-And 
only nails the eyes-
There's Grief of Want--and grief of Cold-A 
sort they call &quot;Despair&quot;-There's 
Banishment from native Eyes-In 
Sight of Native Air-
And though I may not guess the kind-Correctly--
yet to me 
A piercing Comfort it affords 
In passing Calvary-
To note the fashions--of the Cross-And 
how they're mostly worn-Still 
fascinated to presume 
That Some--are like My Own-
I Ment To Find Her When I Came; 
I meant to find her when I came; 
Death had the same design; 
But the success was his, it seems, 
And the discomfit mine. 
I meant to tell her how I longed 
For just this single time; 
But Death had told her so the first, 
And she had hearkened him. 
To wander now is my abode; 
To rest,--to rest would be 
A privilege of hurricane 
To memory and me. 
I Met A King This Afternoon! 
 
I met a King this afternoon! 
He had not on a Crown indeed, 
A little Palmleaf Hat was all, 
And he was barefoot, I'm afraid! 
But sure I am he Ermine wore 
Beneath his faded Jacket's blue&mdash; 
And sure I am, the crest he bore 
Within that Jacket's pocket too! 
For 'twas too stately for an Earl&mdash; 
A Marquis would not go so grand! 
'Twas possibly a Czar petite&mdash; 
A Pope, or something of that kind! 
If I must tell you, of a Horse 
My freckled Monarch held the rein&mdash; 
Doubtless an estimable Beast, 
But not at all disposed to run! 
And such a wagon! While I live 
Dare I presume to see 
Another such a vehicle 
As then transported me! 
Two other ragged Princes 
His royal state partook! 
Doubtless the first excursion 
These sovereigns ever took! 
I question if the Royal Coach 
Round which the Footmen wait 
Has the significance, on high, 
Of this Barefoot Estate! 
I Never Felt At Home—below 
 
I never felt at Home—Below—And 
in the Handsome Skies 
I shall not feel at Home—I know— 
I don't like Paradise— 
Because it's Sunday—all the time— 
And Recess—never comes— 
And Eden'll be so lonesome 
Bright Wednesday Afternoons— 
If God could make a visit— 
Or ever took a Nap— 
So not to see us—but they say 
Himself—a Telescope 
Perennial beholds us— 
Myself would run away 
From Him—and Holy Ghost—and All— 
But there's the "Judgement Day"! 
I Never Hear The Word 'Escape' 
I never hear the word 'escape' 
Without a quicker blood, 
A sudden expectation, 
A flying attitude. 
I never hear of prisons broad 
By soldiers battered down, 
But I tug childish at my bars, -Only 
to fail again! 
I Never Lost As Much But Twice 
 
I never lost as much but twice, 
And that was in the sod. 
Twice have I stood a beggar 
Before the door of God! 
Angels&mdash;twice descending 
Reimbursed my store&mdash; 
Burglar! Banker&mdash;Father! 
I am poor once more! 
I Never Saw A Moor 
I never saw a moor; 
I never saw the sea, 
Yet know I how the heather looks 
And what a billow be. 
I never spoke with God, 
Nor visited in heaven. 
Yet certain am I of the spot 
As if the checks were given. 
I Never Told The Buried Gold 
 
I never told the buried gold 
Upon the hill&mdash;that lies&mdash; 
I saw the sun&mdash;his plunder done 
Crouch low to guard his prize. 
He stood as near 
As stood you here&mdash; 
A pace had been between&mdash; 
Did but a snake bisect the brake 
My life had forfeit been. 
That was a wondrous booty&mdash; 
I hope 'twas honest gained. 
Those were the fairest ingots 
That ever kissed the spade! 
Whether to keep the secret&mdash; 
Whether to reveal&mdash; 
Whether as I ponder 
Kidd will sudden sail&mdash; 
Could a shrewd advise me 
We might e'en divide&mdash; 
Should a shrewd betray me&mdash; 
Atropos decide! 
I Noticed People Disappeared 
I noticed People disappeared 
When but a little child Supposed 
they visited remote 
Or settled Regions wild But 
did because they died 
A Fact withheld the little child 
I Often Passed The Village 
 
I often passed the village 
When going home from school&mdash; 
And wondered what they did there&mdash; 
And why it was so still&mdash; 
I did not know the year then&mdash; 
In which my call would come&mdash; 
Earlier, by the Dial, 
Than the rest have gone. 
It's stiller than the sundown. 
It's cooler than the dawn&mdash; 
The Daisies dare to come here&mdash; 
And birds can flutter down&mdash; 
So when you are tired&mdash; 
Or perplexed&mdash;or cold&mdash; 
Trust the loving promise 
Underneath the mould, 
Cry "it's I," "take Dollie," 
And I will enfold! 
I Pay—in Satin Cash 
 
I pay—in Satin Cash— 
You did not state—your price— 
A Petal, for a Paragraph 
It near as I can guess— 
I Play At Riches—to Appease 
 
I play at Riches—to appease 
The Clamoring for Gold— 
It kept me from a Thief, I think, 
For often, overbold 
With Want, and Opportunity— 
I could have done a Sin 
And been Myself that easy Thing 
An independent Man— 
But often as my lot displays 
Too hungry to be borne 
I deem Myself what I would be— 
And novel Comforting 
My Poverty and I derive— 
We question if the Man— 
Who own—Esteem the Opulence— 
As We—Who never Can— 
Should ever these exploring Hands 
Chance Sovereign on a Mine— 
Or in the long—uneven term 
To win, become their turn— 
How fitter they will be—for Want— 
Enlightening so well— 
I know not which, Desire, or Grant— 
Be wholly beautiful— 
I Prayed, At First, A Little Girl 
 
I prayed, at first, a little Girl, 
Because they told me to&mdash; 
But stopped, when qualified to guess 
How prayer would feel&mdash;to me&mdash; 
If I believed God looked around, 
Each time my Childish eye 
Fixed full, and steady, on his own 
In Childish honesty&mdash; 
And told him what I'd like, today, 
And parts of his far plan 
That baffled me&mdash; 
The mingled side 
Of his Divinity&mdash; 
And often since, in Danger, 
I count the force 'twould be 
To have a God so strong as that 
To hold my life for me 
Till I could take the Balance 
That tips so frequent, now, 
It takes me all the while to poise&mdash; 
And then&mdash;it doesn't stay&mdash; 
I Read My Sentence—steadily 
 
I read my sentence—steadily— 
Reviewed it with my eyes, 
To see that I made no mistake 
In its extremest clause— 
The Date, and manner, of the shame— 
And then the Pious Form 
That "God have mercy" on the Soul 
The Jury voted Him— 
I made my soul familiar—with her extremity— 
That at the last, it should not be a novel Agony— 
But she, and Death, acquainted— 
Meet tranquilly, as friends— 
Salute, and pass, without a Hint— 
And there, the Matter ends— 
I Reason, Earth Is Short 
 
I reason, Earth is short&mdash; 
And Anguish&mdash;absolute&mdash; 
And many hurt, 
But, what of that? 
I reason, we could die&mdash; 
The best Vitality 
Cannot excel Decay, 
But, what of that? 
I reason, that in Heaven&mdash; 
Somehow, it will be even&mdash; 
Some new Equation, given&mdash; 
But, what of that? 
I Reckon—when I Count It All 
 
I reckon—when I count it all— 
First—Poets—Then the Sun— 
Then Summer—Then the Heaven of God— 
And then—the List is done— 
But, looking back—the First so seems 
To Comprehend the Whole— 
The Others look a needless Show— 
So I write—Poets—All— 
Their Summer—lasts a Solid Year— 
They can afford a Sun 
The East—would deem extravagant— 
And if the Further Heaven— 
Be Beautiful as they prepare 
For Those who worship Them— 
It is too difficult a Grace— 
To justify the Dream— 
I Robbed The Woods 
 
I robbed the Woods&mdash; 
The trusting Woods. 
The unsuspecting Trees 
Brought out their Burs and mosses 
My fantasy to please. 
I scanned their trinkets curious&mdash;I grasped&mdash;I bore away&mdash; 
What will the solemn Hemlock&mdash; 
What will the Oak tree say? 
I Rose—because He Sank 
 
I rose—because He sank— 
I thought it would be opposite— 
But when his power dropped— 
My Soul grew straight. 
I cheered my fainting Prince— 
I sang firm—even—Chants— 
I helped his Film—with Hymn— 
And when the Dews drew off 
That held his Forehead stiff— 
I met him— 
Balm to Balm— 
I told him Best—must pass 
Through this low Arch of Flesh— 
No Casque so brave 
It spurn the Grave— 
I told him Worlds I knew 
Where Emperors grew— 
Who recollected us 
If we were true— 
And so with Thews of Hymn— 
And Sinew from within— 
And ways I knew not that I knew—till then— 
I lifted Him— 
I Saw No Way—the Heavens Were Stitched 
 
I saw no Way—The Heavens were stitched— 
I felt the Columns close— 
The Earth reversed her Hemispheres— 
I touched the Universe— 
And back it slid—and I alone— 
A Speck upon a Ball— 
Went out upon Circumference— 
Beyond the Dip of Bell— 
I Saw The Wind Within Her 
I saw the wind within her 
I knew it blew for me — 
But she must buy my shelter 
I asked Humility 
I See Thee Better—in The Dark 
I see thee better—in the Dark— 
I do not need a Light— 
The Love of Thee—a Prism be— 
Excelling Violet— 
I see thee better for the Years 
That hunch themselves between— 
The Miner's Lamp—sufficient be— 
To nullify the Mine— 
And in the Grave—I see Thee best— 
Its little Panels be 
Aglow—All ruddy—with the Light 
I held so high, for Thee— 
What need of Day— 
To Those whose Dark—hath so—surpassing Sun— 
It deem it be—Continually— 
At the Meridian? 
I Send Two Sunsets 
 
I send Two Sunsets&mdash; 
Day and I&mdash;in competition ran&mdash; 
I finished Two&mdash;and several Stars&mdash; 
While He&mdash;was making One&mdash; 
His own was ampler&mdash;but as I 
Was saying to a friend&mdash; 
Mine&mdash;is the more convenient 
To Carry in the Hand&mdash; 
I Shall Keep Singing! 
 
I shall keep singing! 
Birds will pass me 
On their way to Yellower Climes&mdash; 
Each&mdash;with a Robin's expectation&mdash; 
I&mdash;with my Redbreast&mdash; 
And my Rhymes&mdash; 
Late&mdash;when I take my place in summer&mdash; 
But&mdash;I shall bring a fuller tune&mdash; 
Vespers&mdash;are sweeter than Matins&mdash;Signor&mdash; 
Morning&mdash;only the seed of Noon&mdash; 
I Shall Know Why—when Time Is Over 
 
I shall know why—when Time is over— 
And I have ceased to wonder why— 
Christ will explain each separate anguish 
In the fair schoolroom of the sky— 
He will tell me what "Peter" promised— 
And I—for wonder at his woe— 
I shall forget the drop of Anguish 
That scalds me now—that scalds me now! 
I Should Have Been Too Glad, I See 
 
I should have been too glad, I see&mdash; 
Too lifted&mdash;for the scant degree 
Of Life's penurious Round&mdash; 
My little Circuit would have shamed 
This new Circumference&mdash;have blamed&mdash; 
The homelier time behind. 
I should have been too saved&mdash;I see&mdash; 
Too rescued&mdash;Fear too dim to me 
That I could spell the Prayer 
I knew so perfect&mdash;yesterday&mdash; 
That Scalding One&mdash;Sabachthani&mdash; 
Recited fluent&mdash;here&mdash; 
Earth would have been too much&mdash;I see&mdash; 
And Heaven&mdash;not enough for me&mdash; 
I should have had the Joy 
Without the Fear&mdash;to justify&mdash; 
The Palm&mdash;without the Calvary&mdash; 
So Savior&mdash;Crucify&mdash; 
Defeat&mdash;whets Victory&mdash;they say&mdash; 
The Reefs&mdash;in old Gethsemane&mdash; 
Endear the Coast&mdash;beyond! 
'Tis Beggars&mdash;Banquets&mdash;can define&mdash; 
'Tis Parching&mdash;vitalizes Wine&mdash; 
"Faith" bleats&mdash;to understand! 
I Should Not Dare To Leave My Friend 
 
I should not dare to leave my friend, 
Because&mdash;because if he should die 
While I was gone&mdash;and I&mdash;too late&mdash; 
Should reach the Heart that wanted me&mdash; 
If I should disappoint the eyes 
That hunted&mdash;hunted so&mdash;to see&mdash; 
And could not bear to shut until 
They "noticed" me&mdash;they noticed me&mdash; 
If I should stab the patient faith 
So sure I'd come&mdash;so sure I'd come&mdash; 
It listening&mdash;listening&mdash;went to sleep&mdash; 
Telling my tardy name&mdash; 
My Heart would wish it broke before&mdash; 
Since breaking then&mdash;since breaking then&mdash; 
Were useless as next morning's sun&mdash; 
Where midnight frosts&mdash;had lain! 
I Showed Her Heights She Never Saw 
 
I showed her Heights she never saw&mdash; 
"Would'st Climb," I said? 
She said&mdash;"Not so"&mdash; 
"With me&mdash;" I said&mdash;With me? 
I showed her Secrets&mdash;Morning's Nest&mdash; 
The Rope the Nights were put across&mdash; 
And now&mdash;"Would'st have me for a Guest?" 
She could not find her Yes&mdash; 
And then, I brake my life&mdash;And Lo, 
A Light, for her, did solemn glow, 
The larger, as her face withdrew&mdash; 
And could she, further, "No"? 
I Sing To Use The Waiting 
 
I sing to use the Waiting 
My Bonnet but to tie 
And shut the Door unto my House 
No more to do have I 
Till His best step approaching 
We journey to the Day 
And tell each other how We sung 
To Keep the Dark away. 
I Sometimes Drop It, For A Quick 
 
I sometimes drop it, for a Quick&mdash; 
The Thought to be alive&mdash; 
Anonymous Delight to know&mdash; 
And Madder&mdash;to conceive&mdash; 
Consoles a Woe so monstrous 
That did it tear all Day, 
Without an instant's Respite&mdash; 
'Twould look too far&mdash;to Die&mdash; 
I Started Early - Took My Dog 
I started Early - Took my Dog And 
visited the Sea The 
Mermaids in the Basement 
Came out to look at me 
And Frigates - in the Upper Floor 
Extended Hempen Hands Presuming 
Me to be a Mouse Aground 
- upon the Sands 
But no Man moved Me - till the Tide 
Went past my simple Shoe And 
past my Apron - and my Belt 
And past my Bodice - too 
And made as He would eat me up As 
wholly as a Dew 
Upon a Dandelion's Sleeve And 
then - I started - too 
And He - He followed - close behind I 
felt His Silver Heel 
Upon my Ankle - Then my Shoes 
Would overflow with Pearl 
Until We met the Solid Town No 
One He seemed to know And 
bowing - with a Mighty look At 
me - The Sea withdrew 
I Stepped From Plank To Plank 
I stepped from plank to plank 
So slow and cautiously; 
The stars about my head I felt, 
About my feet the sea. 
I knew not but the next 
Would be my final inch,-
This gave me that precarious gait 
Some call experience. 
I Stole Them From A Bee 
 
I stole them from a Bee&mdash; 
Because&mdash;Thee&mdash; 
Sweet plea&mdash; 
He pardoned me! 
I Taste A Liquor Never Brewed 
I taste a liquor never brewed, 
From tankards scooped in pearl; 
Not all the vats upon the Rhine 
Yield such an alcohol! 
Inebriate of air am I, 
And debauchee of dew, 
Reeling, through endless summer days, 
From inns of molten blue. 
When the landlord turn the drunken bee 
Out of the foxglove's door, 
When butterflies renounce their drams, 
I shall but drink the more! 
Till seraphs swing their snowy hats, 
And saints to windows run, 
To see the little tippler 
Leaning against the sun! 
I Tend My Flowers For Thee 
 
I tend my flowers for thee&mdash; 
Bright Absentee! 
My Fuchsia's Coral Seams 
Rip&mdash;while the Sower&mdash;dreams&mdash; 
Geraniums&mdash;tint&mdash;and spot&mdash; 
Low Daisies&mdash;dot&mdash; 
My Cactus&mdash;splits her Beard 
To show her throat&mdash; 
Carnations&mdash;tip their spice&mdash; 
And Bees&mdash;pick up&mdash; 
A Hyacinth&mdash;I hid&mdash; 
Puts out a Ruffled Head&mdash; 
And odors fall 
From flasks&mdash;so small&mdash; 
You marvel how they held&mdash; 
Globe Roses&mdash;break their satin glake&mdash; 
Upon my Garden floor&mdash; 
Yet&mdash;thou&mdash;not there&mdash; 
I had as lief they bore 
No Crimson&mdash;more&mdash; 
Thy flower&mdash;be gay&mdash; 
Her Lord&mdash;away! 
It ill becometh me&mdash; 
I'll dwell in Calyx&mdash;Gray&mdash; 
How modestly&mdash;alway&mdash; 
Thy Daisy&mdash; 
Draped for thee! 
I Think I Was Enchanted 
 
I think I was enchanted 
When first a sombre Girl&mdash; 
I read that Foreign Lady&mdash; 
The Dark&mdash;felt beautiful&mdash; 
And whether it was noon at night&mdash; 
Or only Heaven&mdash;at Noon&mdash; 
For very Lunacy of Light 
I had not power to tell&mdash; 
The Bees&mdash;became as Butterflies&mdash; 
The Butterflies&mdash;as Swans&mdash; 
Approached&mdash;and spurned the narrow Grass&mdash; 
And just the meanest Tunes 
That Nature murmured to herself 
To keep herself in Cheer&mdash; 
I took for Giants&mdash;practising 
Titanic Opera&mdash; 
The Days&mdash;to Mighty Metres stept&mdash; 
The Homeliest&mdash;adorned 
As if unto a Jubilee 
'Twere suddenly confirmed&mdash; 
I could not have defined the change&mdash; 
Conversion of the Mind 
Like Sanctifying in the Soul&mdash; 
Is witnessed&mdash;not explained&mdash; 
'Twas a Divine Insanity&mdash; 
The Danger to be Sane 
Should I again experience&mdash; 
'Tis Antidote to turn&mdash; 
To Tomes of solid Witchcraft&mdash; 
Magicians be asleep&mdash; 
But Magic&mdash;hath an Element 
Like Deity&mdash;to keep&mdash; 
I Think Just How My Shape Will Rise 
 
I think just how my shape will rise&mdash; 
When I shall be "forgiven"&mdash; 
Till Hair&mdash;and Eyes&mdash;and timid Head&mdash; 
Are out of sight&mdash;in Heaven&mdash; 
I think just how my lips will weigh&mdash; 
With shapeless&mdash;quivering&mdash;prayer&mdash; 
That you&mdash;so late&mdash;"Consider" me&mdash; 
The "Sparrow" of your Care&mdash; 
I mind me that of Anguish&mdash;sent&mdash; 
Some drifts were moved away&mdash; 
Before my simple bosom&mdash;broke&mdash; 
And why not this&mdash;if they? 
And so I con that thing&mdash;"forgiven"&mdash; 
Until&mdash;delirious&mdash;borne&mdash; 
By my long bright&mdash;and longer&mdash;trust&mdash; 
I drop my Heart&mdash;unshriven! 
I Think The Hemlock Likes To Stand 
 
I think the Hemlock likes to stand 
Upon a Marge of Snow&mdash; 
It suits his own Austerity&mdash; 
And satisfies an awe 
That men, must slake in Wilderness&mdash; 
And in the Desert&mdash;cloy&mdash; 
An instinct for the Hoar, the Bald&mdash; 
Lapland's&mdash;necessity&mdash; 
The Hemlock's nature thrives&mdash;on cold&mdash; 
The Gnash of Northern winds 
Is sweetest nutriment&mdash;to him&mdash; 
His best Norwegian Wines&mdash; 
To satin Races&mdash;he is nought&mdash; 
But Children on the Don, 
Beneath his Tabernacles, play, 
And Dnieper Wrestlers, run. 
I Think The Longest Hour Of All 
 
I think the longest Hour of all 
Is when the Cars have come&mdash; 
And we are waiting for the Coach&mdash; 
It seems as though the Time 
Indignant&mdash;that the Joy was come&mdash; 
Did block the Gilded Hands&mdash; 
And would not let the Seconds by&mdash; 
But slowest instant&mdash;ends&mdash; 
The Pendulum begins to count&mdash; 
Like little Scholars&mdash;loud&mdash; 
The steps grow thicker&mdash;in the Hall&mdash; 
The Heart begins to crowd&mdash; 
Then I&mdash;my timid service done&mdash; 
Tho' service 'twas, of Love&mdash; 
Take up my little Violin&mdash; 
And further North&mdash;remove. 
I Think To Live—may Be A Bliss 
 
I think to Live—may be a Bliss 
To those who dare to try— 
Beyond my limit to conceive— 
My lip—to testify— 
I think the Heart I former wore 
Could widen—till to me 
The Other, like the little Bank 
Appear—unto the Sea— 
I think the Days—could every one 
In Ordination stand— 
And Majesty—be easier— 
Than an inferior kind— 
No numb alarm—lest Difference come— 
No Goblin—on the Bloom— 
No start in Apprehension's Ear, 
No Bankruptcy—no Doom— 
But Certainties of Sun— 
Midsummer—in the Mind— 
A steadfast South—upon the Soul— 
Her Polar time—behind— 
The Vision—pondered long— 
So plausible becomes 
That I esteem the fiction—real— 
The Real—fictitious seems— 
How bountiful the Dream— 
What Plenty—it would be— 
Had all my Life but been Mistake 
Just rectified—in Thee 
I thought the Train would never come 
I thought the Train would never come How 
slow the whistle sang I 
don't believe a peevish Bird 
So whimpered for the Spring I 
taught my Heart a hundred times 
Precisely what to say Provoking 
Lover, when you came 
Its Treatise flew away 
To hide my strategy too late 
To wiser be too soon For 
miseries so halcyon 
The happiness atone 
I Tie My Hat—i Crease My Shawl 
 
I tie my Hat—I crease my Shawl— 
Life's little duties do—precisely— 
As the very least 
Were infinite—to me— 
I put new Blossoms in the Glass— 
And throw the old—away— 
I push a petal from my gown 
That anchored there—I weigh 
The time 'twill be till six o'clock 
I have so much to do— 
And yet—Existence—some way back— 
Stopped—struck—my tickling—through— 
We cannot put Ourself away 
As a completed Man 
Or Woman—When the Errand's done 
We came to Flesh—upon— 
There may be—Miles on Miles of Nought— 
Of Action—sicker far— 
To simulate—is stinging work— 
To cover what we are 
From Science—and from Surgery— 
Too Telescopic Eyes 
To bear on us unshaded— 
For their—sake—not for Ours— 
'Twould start them— 
We—could tremble— 
But since we got a Bomb— 
And held it in our Bosom— 
Nay—Hold it—it is calm— 
Therefore—we do life's labor— 
Though life's Reward—be done— 
With scrupulous exactness— 
To hold our Senses—on— 
I Took My Power In My Hand 
 
I took my Power in my Hand&mdash; 
And went against the World&mdash; 
'Twas not so much as David&mdash;had&mdash; 
But I&mdash;was twice as bold&mdash; 
I aimed by Pebble&mdash;but Myself 
Was all the one that fell&mdash; 
Was it Goliath&mdash;was too large&mdash; 
Or was myself&mdash;too small? 
I Tried To Think A Lonelier Thing 
 
I tried to think a lonelier Thing 
Than any I had seen&mdash; 
Some Polar Expiation&mdash;An Omen in the Bone 
Of Death's tremendous nearness&mdash; 
I probed Retrieverless things 
My Duplicate&mdash;to borrow&mdash; 
A Haggard Comfort springs 
From the belief that Somewhere&mdash; 
Within the Clutch of Thought&mdash; 
There dwells one other Creature 
Of Heavenly Love&mdash;forgot&mdash; 
I plucked at our Partition 
As One should pry the Walls&mdash; 
Between Himself&mdash;and Horror's Twin&mdash; 
Within Opposing Cells&mdash; 
I almost strove to clasp his Hand, 
Such Luxury&mdash;it grew&mdash; 
That as Myself&mdash;could pity Him&mdash; 
Perhaps he&mdash;pitied me&mdash; 
I Want—it Pleaded—all Its Life— 
"I want"—it pleaded—All its life— 
I want—was chief it said 
When Skill entreated it—the last— 
And when so newly dead— 
I could not deem it late—to hear 
That single—steadfast sigh— 
The lips had placed as with a "Please" 
Toward Eternity— 
I Was The Slightest In The House 
 
I was the slightest in the House&mdash; 
I took the smallest Room&mdash; 
At night, my little Lamp, and Book&mdash; 
And one Geranium&mdash; 
So stationed I could catch the Mint 
That never ceased to fall&mdash; 
And just my Basket&mdash; 
Let me think&mdash;I'm sure&mdash; 
That this was all&mdash; 
I never spoke&mdash;unless addressed&mdash; 
And then, 'twas brief and low&mdash; 
I could not bear to live&mdash;aloud&mdash; 
The Racket shamed me so&mdash; 
And if it had not been so far&mdash; 
And any one I knew 
Were going&mdash;I had often thought 
How noteless&mdash;I could die&mdash; 
I Watched The Moon Around The House (629) 
I watched the Moon around the House 
Until upon a Pane -She 
stopped -- a Traveller's privilege -- for Rest -And 
there upon 
I gazed -- as at a stranger -The 
Lady in the Town 
Doth think no incivility 
To lift her Glass -- upon -
But never Stranger justified 
The Curiosity 
Like Mine -- for not a Foot -- nor Hand -Nor 
Formula -- had she -
But like a Head -- a Guillotine 
Slid carelessly away -Did 
independent, Amber -Sustain 
her in the sky -

in rolling Air

bind Philosopher -

too far below

its advantage -- Blue -
I Went To Heaven,-
I went to heaven,-'
T was a small town, 
Lit with a ruby, 
Lathed with down. 
Stiller than the fields 
At the full dew, 
Beautiful as pictures 
No man drew. 
People like the moth, 
Of mechlin, frames, 
Duties of gossamer, 
And eider names. 
Almost contented 
I could be 
'Mong such unique 
Society. 
I Went To Thank Her 
 
I went to thank Her&mdash; 
But She Slept&mdash; 
Her Bed&mdash;a funneled Stone&mdash; 
With Nosegays at the Head and Foot&mdash; 
That Travellers&mdash;had thrown&mdash; 
Who went to thank Her&mdash; 
But She Slept&mdash; 
'Twas Short&mdash;to cross the Sea&mdash; 
To look upon Her like&mdash;alive&mdash; 
But turning back&mdash;'twas slow&mdash; 
I Would Distil A Cup 
 
I would distil a cup, 
And bear to all my friends, 
Drinking to her no more astir, 
By beck, or burn, or moor! 
I Would Not Paint—a Picture 
 
I would not paint—a picture— 
I'd rather be the One 
Its bright impossibility 
To dwell—delicious—on— 
And wonder how the fingers feel 
Whose rare—celestial—stir— 
Evokes so sweet a Torment— 
Such sumptuous—Despair— 
I would not talk, like Cornets— 
I'd rather be the One 
Raised softly to the Ceilings— 
And out, and easy on— 
Through Villages of Ether— 
Myself endued Balloon 
By but a lip of Metal— 
The pier to my Pontoon— 
Nor would I be a Poet— 
It's finer—own the Ear— 
Enamored—impotent—content— 
The License to revere, 
A privilege so awful 
What would the Dower be, 
Had I the Art to stun myself 
With Bolts of Melody! 
I Years Had Been From Home, 
I years had been from home, 
And now, before the door, 
I dared not open, lest a face 
I never saw before 
Stare vacant into mine 
And ask my business there. 
My business,--just a life I left, 
Was such still dwelling there? 
I fumbled at my nerve, 
I scanned the windows near; 
The silence like an ocean rolled, 
And broke against my ear. 
I laughed a wooden laugh 
That I could fear a door, 
Who danger and the dead had faced, 
But never quaked before. 
I fitted to the latch 
My hand, with trembling care, 
Lest back the awful door should spring, 
And leave me standing there. 
I moved my fingers off 
As cautiously as glass, 
And held my ears, and like a thief 
Fled gasping from the house. 
I’ll Tell You How The Sun Rose 
I’ll tell you how the sun rose, A 
ribbon at a time. 
The steeples swam in amethyst, 
The news like squirrels ran. 
The hills untied their bonnets, 
The bobolinks begun. 
Then I said softly to myself, 
"That must have been the sun!" 
But how he set, I know not. 
There seemed a purple stile. 
Which little yellow boys and girls 
Were climbing all the while 
Till when they reached the other side, 
A dominie in gray 
Put gently up the evening bars, 
And led the flock away. 
Ideals Are The Fairly Oil 
 
Ideals are the Fairly Oil 
With which we help the Wheel 
But when the Vital Axle turns 
The Eye rejects the Oil. 
If all the griefs I am to have 
If all the griefs I am to have 
Would only come today, 
I am so happy I believe 
They'd laugh and run away. 
If all the joys I am to have 
Would only come today, 
They could not be so big as this 
That happens to me now. 
If Any Sink, Assure That This, Now Standing 
 
If any sink, assure that this, now standing&mdash; 
Failed like Themselves&mdash;and conscious that it rose&mdash; 
Grew by the Fact, and not the Understanding 
How Weakness passed&mdash;or Force&mdash;arose&mdash; 
Tell that the Worst, is easy in a Moment&mdash; 
Dread, but the Whizzing, before the Ball&mdash; 
When the Ball enters, enters Silence&mdash; 
Dying&mdash;annuls the power to kill. 
If Anybody's Friend Be Dead 
 
If anybody's friend be dead 
It's sharpest of the theme 
The thinking how they walked alive&mdash; 
At such and such a time&mdash; 
Their costume, of a Sunday, 
Some manner of the Hair&mdash; 
A prank nobody knew but them 
Lost, in the Sepulchre&mdash; 
How warm, they were, on such a day, 
You almost feel the date&mdash; 
So short way off it seems&mdash; 
And now&mdash;they're Centuries from that&mdash; 
How pleased they were, at what you said&mdash; 
You try to touch the smile 
And dip your fingers in the frost&mdash; 
When was it&mdash;Can you tell&mdash; 
You asked the Company to tea&mdash; 
Acquaintance&mdash;just a few&mdash; 
And chatted close with this Grand Thing 
That don't remember you&mdash; 
Past Bows, and Invitations&mdash; 
Past Interview, and Vow&mdash; 
Past what Ourself can estimate&mdash; 
That&mdash;makes the Quick of Woe! 
If Blame Be My Side—forfeit Me 
 
If Blame be my side—forfeit Me— 
But doom me not to forfeit Thee— 
To forfeit Thee? The very name 
Is sentence from Belief—and House— 
If Ever The Lid Gets Off My Head 
If ever the lid gets off my head 
And lets the brain away 
The fellow will go where he belonged Without 
a hint from me, 
And the world -if the world be looking on Will 
see how far from home 
It is possible for sense to live 
The soul there -all the time. 
If He Dissolve—then—there Is Nothing 
 
If He dissolve—then—there is nothing—more— 
Eclipse—at Midnight— 
It was dark—before— 
Sunset—at Easter— 
Blindness—on the Dawn— 
Faint Star of Bethlehem— 
Gone down! 
Would but some God—inform Him— 
Or it be too late! 
Say—that the pulse just lisps— 
The Chariots wait— 
Say—that a little life—for His— 
Is leaking—red— 
His little Spaniel—tell Him! 
Will He heed? 
If He Were Living—dare I Ask 
 
If He were living—dare I ask— 
And how if He be dead— 
And so around the Words I went— 
Of meeting them—afraid— 
I hinted Changes—Lapse of Time— 
The Surfaces of Years— 
I touched with Caution—lest they crack— 
And show me to my fears— 
Reverted to adjoining Lives— 
Adroitly turning out 
Wherever I suspected Graves— 
'Twas prudenter—I thought— 
And He—I pushed—with sudden force— 
In face of the Suspense— 
"Was buried"—"Buried"! "He!" 
My Life just holds the Trench— 
If I Can Stop One Heart From Breaking, 
If I can stop one heart from breaking, 
I shall not live in vain; 
If I can ease one life the aching, 
Or cool one pain, 
Or help one fainting robin 
Unto his nest again, 
I shall not live in vain. 
If I Could Bribe Them By A Rose 
 
If I could bribe them by a Rose 
I'd bring them every flower that grows 
From Amherst to Cashmere! 
I would not stop for night, or storm&mdash; 
Or frost, or death, or anyone&mdash; 
My business were so dear! 
If they would linger for a Bird 
My Tambourin were soonest heard 
Among the April Woods! 
Unwearied, all the summer long, 
Only to break in wilder song 
When Winter shook the boughs! 
What if they hear me! 
Who shall say 
That such an importunity 
May not at last avail? 
That, weary of this Beggar's face&mdash; 
They may not finally say, Yes&mdash; 
To drive her from the Hall? 
If I May Have It, When It's Dead 
 
If I may have it, when it's dead, 
I'll be contented&mdash;so&mdash; 
If just as soon as Breath is out 
It shall belong to me&mdash; 
Until they lock it in the Grave, 
'Tis Bliss I cannot weigh&mdash; 
For tho' they lock Thee in the Grave, 
Myself&mdash;can own the key&mdash; 
Think of it Lover! I and Thee 
Permitted&mdash;face to face to be&mdash; 
After a Life&mdash;a Death&mdash;We'll say&mdash; 
For Death was That&mdash; 
And this&mdash;is Thee&mdash; 
I'll tell Thee All&mdash;how Bald it grew&mdash; 
How Midnight felt, at first&mdash;to me&mdash; 
How all the Clocks stopped in the World&mdash; 
And Sunshine pinched me&mdash;'Twas so cold&mdash; 
Then how the Grief got sleepy&mdash;some&mdash; 
As if my Soul were deaf and dumb&mdash; 
Just making signs&mdash;across&mdash;to Thee&mdash; 
That this way&mdash;thou could'st notice me&mdash; 
I'll tell you how I tried to keep 
A smile, to show you, when this Deep 
All Waded&mdash;We look back for Play, 
At those Old Times&mdash;in Calvary, 
Forgive me, if the Grave come slow&mdash; 
For Coveting to look at Thee&mdash; 
Forgive me, if to stroke thy frost 
Outvisions Paradise! 
If I Should Cease To Bring A Rose 
 
If I should cease to bring a Rose 
Upon a festal day, 
'Twill be because beyond the Rose 
I have been called away&mdash; 
If I should cease to take the names 
My buds commemorate&mdash; 
'Twill be because Death's finger 
Claps my murmuring lip! 
If I Should Die 
 
If I should die, 
And you should live&mdash; 
And time should gurgle on&mdash; 
And morn should beam&mdash; 
And noon should burn&mdash; 
As it has usual done&mdash; 
If Birds should build as early 
And Bees as bustling go&mdash; 
One might depart at option 
From enterprise below! 
'Tis sweet to know that stocks will stand 
When we with Daisies lie&mdash; 
That Commerce will continue&mdash; 
And Trades as briskly fly&mdash; 
It makes the parting tranquil 
And keeps the soul serene&mdash; 
That gentlemen so sprightly 
Conduct the pleasing scene! 
If I Shouldn'T Be Alive 
 
If I shouldn't be alive 
When the Robins come, 
Give the one in Red Cravat, 
A Memorial crumb. 
If I couldn't thank you, 
Being fast asleep, 
You will know I'm trying 
Why my Granite lip! 
If I'M Lost&Mdash;Now 
 
If I'm lost&mdash;now 
That I was found&mdash; 
Shall still my transport be&mdash; 
That once&mdash;on me&mdash;those Jasper Gates 
Blazed open&mdash;suddenly&mdash; 
That in my awkward&mdash;gazing&mdash;face&mdash; 
The Angels&mdash;softly peered&mdash; 
And touched me with their fleeces, 
Almost as if they cared&mdash; 
I'm banished&mdash;now&mdash;you know it&mdash; 
How foreign that can be&mdash; 
You'll know&mdash;Sir&mdash;when the Savior's face 
Turns so&mdash;away from you&mdash; 
If It Had No Pencil 
 
If it had no pencil 
Would it try mine&mdash; 
Worn&mdash;now&mdash;and dull&mdash;sweet, 
Writing much to thee. 
If it had no word, 
Would it make the Daisy, 
Most as big as I was, 
When it plucked me? 
If Nature Smiles -The Mother Must 
If Nature smiles -the Mother must 
I'm sure, at many a whim 
Of Her eccentric Family Is 
She so much to blame? 
If Pain For Peace Prepares 
 
If pain for peace prepares 
Lo, what "Augustan" years 
Our feet await! 
If springs from winter rise, 
Can the Anemones 
Be reckoned up? 
If night stands fast&mdash;then noon 
To gird us for the sun, 
What gaze! 
When from a thousand skies 
On our developed eyes 
Noons blaze! 
If Recollecting Were Forgetting 
 
If recollecting were forgetting, 
Then I remember not. 
And if forgetting, recollecting, 
How near I had forgot. 
And if to miss, were merry, 
And to mourn, were gay, 
How very blithe the fingers 
That gathered this, Today! 
If She Had Been The Mistletoe 
 
If she had been the Mistletoe 
And I had been the Rose&mdash; 
How gay upon your table 
My velvet life to close&mdash; 
Since I am of the Druid, 
And she is of the dew&mdash; 
I'll deck Tradition's buttonhole&mdash; 
And send the Rose to you. 
If The Foolish, Call Them "Flowers" 
 
If the foolish, call them "flowers"&mdash; 
Need the wiser, tell? 
If the Savants "Classify" them 
It is just as well! 
Those who read the "Revelations" 
Must not criticize 
Those who read the same Edition&mdash; 
With beclouded Eyes! 
Could we stand with that Old "Moses"&mdash; 
"Canaan" denied&mdash; 
Scan like him, the stately landscape 
On the other side&mdash; 
Doubtless, we should deem superfluous 
Many Sciences, 
Not pursued by learned Angels 
In scholastic skies! 
Low amid that glad Belles lettres 
Grant that we may stand, 
Stars, amid profound Galaxies&mdash; 
At that grand "Right hand"! 
If This Is "Fading" 
 
If this is "fading" 
Oh let me immediately "fade"! 
If this is "dying" 
Bury me, in such a shroud of red! 
If this is "sleep," 
On such a night 
How proud to shut the eye! 
Good Evening, gentle Fellow men! 
Peacock presumes to die! 
If Those I Loved Were Lost 
 
If those I loved were lost 
The Crier's voice would tell me&mdash; 
If those I loved were found 
The bells of Ghent would ring&mdash; 
Did those I loved repose 
The Daisy would impel me. 
Philip&mdash;when bewildered 
Bore his riddle in! 
If What We Could&Mdash;Were What We Would 
 
If What we could&mdash;were what we would&mdash; 
Criterion&mdash;be small&mdash; 
It is the Ultimate of Talk&mdash; 
The Impotence to Tell&mdash; 
If You Were Coming In The Fall, 
If you were coming in the fall, 
I'd brush the summer by 
With half a smile and half a spum, 
As housewives do a fly. 
If I could see you in a year, 
I'd wind the months in balls, 
And put them each in separate drawers, 
Until their time befalls. 
If only centuries delayed, 
I'd count them on my hand, 
Subtracting till my fingers dropped 
Into Van Diemen's land. 
If certain, when this life was out, 
That yours and mine should be, 
I'd toss it yonder like a rind, 
And taste eternity. 
But now, all ignorant of the length 
Of time's uncertain wing, 
It goads me, like the goblin bee, 
That will not state its sting. 
If Your Nerve, Deny You 
 
If your Nerve, deny you&mdash; 
Go above your Nerve&mdash; 
He can lean against the Grave, 
If he fear to swerve&mdash; 
That's a steady posture&mdash; 
Never any bend 
Held of those Brass arms&mdash; 
Best Giant made&mdash; 
If your Soul seesaw&mdash; 
Lift the Flesh door&mdash; 
The Poltroon wants Oxygen&mdash; 
Nothing more&mdash; 
I'Ll Clutch—and Clutch 
 
I'll clutch—and clutch— 
Next—One—Might be the golden touch— 
Could take it— 
Diamonds—Wait— 
I'm diving—just a little late— 
But stars—go slow—for night— 
I'll string you—in fine Necklace— 
Tiaras—make—of some— 
Wear you on Hem— 
Loop up a Countess—with you— 
Make—a Diadem—and mend my old One— 
Count—Hoard—then lose— 
And doubt that you are mine— 
To have the joy of feeling it—again— 
I'll show you at the Court— 
Bear you—for Ornament 
Where Women breathe— 
That every sigh—may lift you 
Just as high—as I— 
And—when I die— 
In meek array—display you— 
Still to show—how rich I go— 
Lest Skies impeach a wealth so wonderful— 
And banish me— 
I'Ll Send The Feather From My Hat! 
 
I'll send the feather from my Hat! 
Who knows&mdash;but at the sight of that 
My Sovereign will relent? 
As trinket&mdash;worn by faded Child&mdash; 
Confronting eyes long&mdash;comforted&mdash; 
Blisters the Adamant! 
I'M 
 
I'm "wife"—I've finished that— 
That other state— 
I'm Czar—I'm "Woman" now— 
It's safer so— 
How odd the Girl's life looks 
Behind this soft Eclipse— 
I think that Earth feels so 
To folks in Heaven—now— 
This being comfort—then 
That other kind—was pain— 
But why compare? 
I'm "Wife"! Stop there!

I'M Ceded—i'Ve Stopped Being Theirs 
 
I'm ceded—I've stopped being Theirs— 
The name They dropped upon my face 
With water, in the country church 
Is finished using, now, 
And They can put it with my Dolls, 
My childhood, and the string of spools, 
I've finished threading—too— 
Baptized, before, without the choice, 
But this time, consciously, of Grace— 
Unto supremest name— 
Called to my Full—The Crescent dropped— 
Existence's whole Arc, filled up, 
With one small Diadem. 
My second Rank—too small the first— 
Crowned—Crowing—on my Father's breast— 
A half unconscious Queen— 
But this time—Adequate—Erect, 
With Will to choose, or to reject, 
And I choose, just a Crown— 
I'M Nobody! Who Are You? 
I'm nobody! Who are you? 
Are you nobody, too? 
Then there's a pair of us -- don't tell! 
They'd banish -- you know! 
How dreary to be somebody! 
How public like a frog 
To tell one's name the livelong day 
To an admiring bog! 
I'M Saying Every Day 
 
I'm saying every day 
"If I should be a Queen, tomorrow"&mdash; 
I'd do this way&mdash; 
And so I deck, a little, 
If it be, I wake a Bourbon, 
None on me, bend supercilious&mdash; 
With "This was she&mdash; 
Begged in the Market place&mdash; 
Yesterday." 
Court is a stately place&mdash; 
I've heard men say&mdash; 
So I loop my apron, against the Majesty 
With bright Pins of Buttercup&mdash; 
That not too plain&mdash; 
Rank&mdash;overtake me&mdash; 
And perch my Tongue 
On Twigs of singing&mdash;rather high&mdash; 
But this, might be my brief Term 
To qualify&mdash; 
Put from my simple speech all plain word&mdash; 
Take other accents, as such I heard 
Though but for the Cricket&mdash;just, 
And but for the Bee&mdash; 
Not in all the Meadow&mdash; 
One accost me&mdash; 
Better to be ready&mdash; 
Than did next morn 
Meet me in Aragon&mdash; 
My old Gown&mdash;on&mdash; 
And the surprised Air 
Rustics&mdash;wear&mdash; 
Summoned&mdash;unexpectedly&mdash; 
To Exeter&mdash; 
I'M Sorry For The Dead—today 
 
I'm sorry for the Dead—Today— 
It's such congenial times 
Old Neighbors have at fences— 
It's time o' year for Hay. 
And Broad—Sunburned Acquaintance 
Discourse between the Toil— 
And laugh, a homely species 
That makes the Fences smile— 
It seems so straight to lie away 
From all of the noise of Fields— 
The Busy Carts—the fragrant Cocks— 
The Mower's Metre—Steals— 
A Trouble lest they're homesick— 
Those Farmers—and their Wives— 
Set separate from the Farming— 
And all the Neighbors' lives— 
A Wonder if the Sepulchre 
Don't feel a lonesome way— 
When Men—and Boys—and Carts—and June, 
Go down the Fields to "Hay"— 
I'M The Little 
 
I'm the little "Heart's Ease"! 
I don't care for pouting skies! 
If the Butterfly delay 
Can I, therefore, stay away? 
If the Coward Bumble Bee 
In his chimney corner stay, 
I, must resoluter be! 
Who'll apologize for me? 
Dear, Old fashioned, little flower! 
Eden is old fashioned, too! 
Birds are antiquated fellows! 
Heaven does not change her blue. 
Nor will I, the little Heart's Ease— 
Ever be induced to do!

Immured in Heaven! 
What a Cell!

Impossibility, Like Wine 
 
Impossibility, like Wine 
Exhilarates the Man 
Who tastes it; Possibility 
Is flavorless&mdash;Combine 
A Chance's faintest Tincture 
And in the former Dram 
Enchantment makes ingredient 
As certainly as Doom&mdash; 
In Ebon Box, When Years Have Flown 
 
In Ebon Box, when years have flown 
To reverently peer, 
Wiping away the velvet dust 
Summers have sprinkled there! 
To hold a letter to the light&mdash; 
Grown Tawny now, with time&mdash; 
To con the faded syllables 
That quickened us like Wine! 
Perhaps a Flower's shrivelled check 
Among its stores to find&mdash; 
Plucked far away, some morning&mdash; 
By gallant&mdash;mouldering hand! 
A curl, perhaps, from foreheads 
Our Constancy forgot&mdash; 
Perhaps, an Antique trinket&mdash; 
In vanished fashions set! 
And then to lay them quiet back&mdash; 
And go about its care&mdash; 
As if the little Ebon Box 
Were none of our affair! 
In Falling Timbers Buried 
 
In falling Timbers buried&mdash; 
There breathed a Man&mdash; 
Outside&mdash;the spades&mdash;were plying&mdash; 
The Lungs&mdash;within&mdash; 
Could He&mdash;know&mdash;they sought Him&mdash; 
Could They&mdash;know&mdash;He breathed&mdash; 
Horrid Sand Partition&mdash; 
Neither&mdash;could be heard&mdash; 
Never slacked the Diggers&mdash; 
But when Spades had done&mdash; 
Oh, Reward of Anguish, 
It was dying&mdash;Then&mdash; 
Many Things&mdash;are fruitless&mdash; 
'Tis a Baffling Earth&mdash; 
But there is no Gratitude 
Like the Grace&mdash;of Death&mdash; 
In Lands I Never Saw—they Say 
 
In lands I never saw—they say 
Immortal Alps look down— 
Whose Bonnets touch the firmament— 
Whose Sandals touch the town— 
Meek at whose everlasting feet 
A Myriad Daisy play— 
Which, Sir, are you and which am I 
Upon an August day? 
In Rags Mysterious As These 
 
In rags mysterious as these 
The shining Courtiers go&mdash; 
Veiling the purple, and the plumes&mdash; 
Veiling the ermine so. 
Smiling, as they request an alms&mdash; 
At some imposing door! 
Smiling when we walk barefoot 
Upon their golden floor! 
In Snow Thou Comest 
In snow thou comest Thou 
shalt go with the resuming ground, 
The sweet derision of the crow, 
And Glee's advancing sound. 
In fear thou comest Thou 
shalt go at such a gait of joy 
That man anew embark to live 
Upon the depth of thee. 
In This Short Life 
That only lasts an hour 
How much — how little — is 
Within our power 
In Winter In My Room 
 
In Winter in my Room 
I came upon a Worm&mdash; 
Pink, lank and warm&mdash; 
But as he was a worm 
And worms presume 
Not quite with him at home&mdash; 
Secured him by a string 
To something neighboring 
And went along. 
A Trifle afterward 
A thing occurred 
I'd not believe it if I heard 
But state with creeping blood&mdash; 
A snake with mottles rare 
Surveyed my chamber floor 
In feature as the worm before 
But ringed with power&mdash; 
The very string with which 
I tied him&mdash;too 
When he was mean and new 
That string was there&mdash; 
I shrank&mdash;"How fair you are"! 
Propitiation's claw&mdash; 
"Afraid," he hissed 
"Of me"? 
"No cordiality"&mdash; 
He fathomed me&mdash; 
Then to a Rhythm Slim 
Secreted in his Form 
As Patterns swim 
Projected him. 
That time I flew 
Both eyes his way 
Lest he pursue 
Nor ever ceased to run 
Till in a distant Town 
Towns on from mine 
I set me down 
This was a dream. 
Inconceivably Solemn! 
 
Inconceivably solemn! 
Things go gay 
Pierce&mdash;by the very Press 
Of Imagery&mdash; 
Their far Parades&mdash;order on the eye 
With a mute Pomp&mdash; 
A pleading Pageantry&mdash; 
Flags, are a brave sight&mdash; 
But no true Eye 
Ever went by One&mdash; 
Steadily&mdash; 
Music's triumphant&mdash; 
But the fine Ear 
Winces with delight 
Are Drums too near&mdash; 
Is Bliss Then, Such Abyss 
 
Is Bliss then, such Abyss, 
I must not put my foot amiss 
For fear I spoil my shoe? 
I'd rather suit my foot 
Than save my Boot&mdash; 
For yet to buy another Pair 
Is possible, 
At any store&mdash; 
But Bliss, is sold just once. 
The Patent lost 
None buy it any more&mdash; 
Say, Foot, decide the point&mdash; 
The Lady cross, or not? 
Verdict for Boot!

Is it dead—Find it—

You, or the Wind?

Of the low Ground?

Even through them—This

It Always Felt To Me—a Wrong 
 
It always felt to me—a wrong 
To that Old Moses—done— 
To let him see—the Canaan— 
Without the entering— 
And tho' in soberer moments— 
No Moses there can be 
I'm satisfied—the Romance 
In point of injury— 
Surpasses sharper stated— 
Of Stephen—or of Paul— 
For these—were only put to death— 
While God's adroiter will 
On Moses—seemed to fasten 
With tantalizing Play 
As Boy—should deal with lesser Boy— 
To prove ability. 
The fault—was doubtless Israel's— 
Myself—had banned the Tribes— 
And ushered Grand Old Moses 
In Pentateuchal Robes 
Upon the Broad Possession 
'Twas little—But titled Him—to see— 
Old Man on Nebo! Late as this— 
My justice bleeds—for Thee! 
It Bloomed And Dropt, A Single Noon 
 
It bloomed and dropt, a Single Noon&mdash; 
The Flower&mdash;distinct and Red&mdash; 
I, passing, thought another Noon 
Another in its stead 
Will equal glow, and thought no More 
But came another Day 
To find the Species disappeared&mdash; 
The Same Locality&mdash; 
The Sun in place&mdash;no other fraud 
On Nature's perfect Sum&mdash; 
Had I but lingered Yesterday&mdash; 
Was my retrieveless blame&mdash; 
Much Flowers of this and further Zones 
Have perished in my Hands 
For seeking its Resemblance&mdash; 
But unapproached it stands&mdash; 
The single Flower of the Earth 
That I, in passing by 
Unconscious was&mdash;Great Nature's Face 
Passed infinite by Me&mdash; 
It Can'T Be "Summer"! 
 
It can't be "Summer"! 
That&mdash;got through!

Before the Blackbirds sing! 
It can't be "Dying"! 
It's too Rouge&mdash; 
The Dead shall go in White&mdash; 
So Sunset shuts my question down 
With Cuffs of Chrysolite! 
It Ceased To Hurt Me, Though So Slow 
 
It ceased to hurt me, though so slow 
I could not feel the Anguish go&mdash; 
But only knew by looking back&mdash; 
That something&mdash;had benumbed the Track&mdash; 
Nor when it altered, I could say, 
For I had worn it, every day, 
As constant as the Childish frock&mdash; 
I hung upon the Peg, at night. 
But not the Grief&mdash;that nestled close 
As needles&mdash;ladies softly press 
To Cushions Cheeks&mdash; 
To keep their place&mdash; 
Nor what consoled it, I could trace&mdash; 
Except, whereas 'twas Wilderness&mdash; 
It's better&mdash;almost Peace&mdash;

It did not surprise me&mdash;

What and if it be

Had departed me? 
This was but a story&mdash; 
What and if indeed 
There were just such coffin

It Don'T Sound So Terrible—quite—as It Did 
 
It don't sound so terrible—quite—as it did— 
I run it over—"Dead", Brain, "Dead." 
Put it in Latin—left of my school— 
Seems it don't shriek so—under rule. 
Turn it, a little—full in the face 
A Trouble looks bitterest— 
Shift it—just— 
Say "When Tomorrow comes this way— 
I shall have waded down one Day." 
I suppose it will interrupt me some 
Till I get accustomed—but then the Tomb 
Like other new Things—shows largest—then— 
And smaller, by Habit— 
It's shrewder then 
Put the Thought in advance—a Year— 
How like "a fit"—then— 
Murder—wear!

It dropped so low in my regard 
I heard it hit the ground,

At bottom of my mind; 
Yet blamed the fate that fractured, less 
Than I reviled myself

It Feels A Shame To Be Alive 
 
It feels a shame to be Alive&mdash; 
When Men so brave&mdash;are dead&mdash; 
One envies the Distinguished Dust&mdash; 
Permitted&mdash;such a Head&mdash; 
The Stone&mdash;that tells defending Whom 
This Spartan put away 
What little of Him we&mdash;possessed 
In Pawn for Liberty&mdash; 
The price is great&mdash;Sublimely paid&mdash; 
Do we deserve&mdash;a Thing&mdash; 
That lives&mdash;like Dollars&mdash;must be piled 
Before we may obtain? 
Are we that wait&mdash;sufficient worth&mdash; 
That such Enormous Pearl 
As life&mdash;dissolved be&mdash;for Us&mdash; 
In Battle's&mdash;horrid Bowl? 
It may be&mdash;a Renown to live&mdash; 
I think the Man who die&mdash; 
Those unsustained&mdash;Saviors&mdash; 
Present Divinity&mdash;

It is a lonesome Glee&mdash;

With fair association&mdash; 
Afar upon the Wind 
A Bird to overhear

Arrestless as invisible&mdash; 
A matter of the Skies. 
It Is An Honorable Thought, 
It is an honorable thought, 
And makes one lift one's hat, 
As one encountered gentlefolk 
Upon a daily street, 
That we've immortal place, 
Though pyramids decay, 
And kingdoms, like the orchard, 
Flit russetly away.

It Knew No Medicine 
 
It knew no Medicine&mdash; 
It was not Sickness&mdash;then&mdash; 
Nor any need of Surgery&mdash; 
And therefore&mdash;'twas not Pain&mdash; 
It moved away the Cheeks&mdash; 
A Dimple at a time&mdash; 
And left the Profile&mdash;plainer&mdash; 
And in the place of Bloom

If momently ajar&mdash; 
Temerity&mdash;drew near&mdash; 
And sickened&mdash;ever afterward

It Makes No Difference Abroad 
 
It makes no difference abroad&mdash; 
The Seasons&mdash;fit&mdash;the same&mdash;

It might be lonelier

It Sifts From Leaden Sieves 
 
It sifts from Leaden Sieves&mdash; 
It powders all the Wood. 
It fills with Alabaster Wool 
The Wrinkles of the Road&mdash; 
It makes an Even Face 
Of Mountain, and of Plain&mdash; 
Unbroken Forehead from the East 
Unto the East again&mdash; 
It reaches to the Fence&mdash; 
It wraps it Rail by Rail 
Till it is lost in Fleeces&mdash; 
It deals Celestial Vail 
To Stump, and Stack&mdash;and Stem&mdash; 
A Summer's empty Room&mdash; 
Acres of Joints, where Harvests were, 
Recordless, but for them-
It Ruffles Wrists of Posts 
As Ankles of a Queen&mdash; 
Then stills its Artisans&mdash;like Ghosts&mdash; 
Denying they have been&mdash; 
It sounded as if the Streets were running 
It sounded as if the Streets were running

-was all we could see at the Window 
And Awe -was all we could feel. 
By and by -the boldest stole out of his Covert 
To see if Time was there Nature 
was in an Opal Apron, 
Mixing fresher Air. 
It stole along so stealthy 
It stole along so stealthy 
Suspicion it was done 
Was dim as to the wealthy 
Beginning not to own 
It Struck Me Every Day 
It struck me every day 
The lightning was as new 
As if the cloud that instant slit 
And let the fire through. 
It burned me in the night, 
It blistered in my dream; 
It sickened fresh upon my sight 
With every morning's beam. 
I thought that storm was brief,-The 
maddest, quickest by; 
But Nature lost the date of this, 
And left it in the sky. 
It Tossed—and Tossed 
 
It tossed—and tossed— 
A little Brig I knew—o'ertook by Blast— 
It spun—and spun— 
And groped delirious, for Morn— 
It slipped—and slipped— 
As One that drunken—stept— 
Its white foot tripped— 
Then dropped from sight— 
Ah, Brig—Good Night 
To Crew and You— 
The Ocean's Heart too smooth—too Blue— 
To break for You— 
It Troubled Me As Once I Was 
 
It troubled me as once I was&mdash; 
For I was once a Child&mdash; 
Concluding how an Atom&mdash;fell&mdash; 
And yet the Heavens&mdash;held&mdash; 
The Heavens weighed the most&mdash;by far&mdash; 
Yet Blue&mdash;and solid&mdash;stood&mdash; 
Without a Bolt&mdash;that I could prove&mdash; 
Would Giants&mdash;understand? 
Life set me larger&mdash;problems&mdash; 
Some I shall keep&mdash;to solve 
Till Algebra is easier&mdash; 
Or simpler proved&mdash;above&mdash; 
Then&mdash;too&mdash;be comprehended&mdash; 
What sorer&mdash;puzzled me&mdash; 
Why Heaven did not break away&mdash; 
And tumble&mdash;Blue&mdash;on me&mdash; 
It Was A Grave, Yet Bore No Stone 
 
It was a Grave, yet bore no Stone 
Enclosed 'twas not of Rail 
A Consciousness its Acre, and 
It held a Human Soul. 
Entombed by whom, for what offence 
If Home or Foreign born&mdash; 
Had I the curiosity 
'Twere not appeased of men 
Till Resurrection, I must guess 
Denied the small desire 
A Rose upon its Ridge to sow 
Or take away a Briar. 
It Was Given To Me By The Gods 
 
It was given to me by the Gods&mdash; 
When I was a little Girl&mdash; 
They given us Presents most&mdash;you know&mdash; 
When we are new&mdash;and small. 
I kept it in my Hand&mdash; 
I never put it down&mdash; 
I did not dare to eat&mdash;or sleep&mdash; 
For fear it would be gone&mdash; 
I heard such words as "Rich"&mdash; 
When hurrying to school&mdash; 
From lips at Corners of the Streets&mdash; 
And wrestled with a smile. 
Rich! 'Twas Myself&mdash;was rich&mdash; 
To take the name of Gold&mdash; 
And Gold to own&mdash;in solid Bars&mdash; 
The Difference&mdash;made me bold&mdash; 
It Was Not Death, For I Stood Up, 
It was not death, for I stood up, 
And all the dead lie down; 
It was not night, for all the bells 
Put out their tongues, for noon. 
It was not frost, for on my flesh 
I felt siroccos crawl,-Nor 
fire, for just my marble feet 
Could keep a chancel cool. 
And yet it tasted like them all; 
The figures I have seen 
Set orderly, for burial, 
Reminded me of mine, 
As if my life were shaven 
And fitted to a frame, 
And could not breathe without a key; 
And 't was like midnight, some, 
When everything that ticked has stopped, 
And space stares, all around, 
Or grisly frosts, first autumn morns, 
Repeal the beating ground. 
But most like chaos,--stopless, cool,-Without 
a chance or spar,-Or 
even a report of land 
To justify despair.

It will be Summer—eventually.

And Dowered—all the World—

A Goblin—drank my Dew— 
My Palaces—dropped tenantless— 
Myself—was beggared—too— 
I clutched at sounds— 
I groped at shapes— 
I touched the tops of Films— 
I felt the Wilderness roll back 
Along my Golden lines— 
The Sackcloth—hangs upon the nail— 
The Frock I used to wear— 
But where my moment of Brocade— 
My—drop—of India?

Morns Like These—we Parted 
 
Morns like these—we parted— 
Noons like these—she rose—

To her fair repose.

It was not for me— 
She—was mute from transport— 
I—from agony— 
Till—the evening nearing 
One the curtains drew— 
Quick! A Sharper rustling! 
And this linnet flew! 
Most She Touched Me By Her Muteness 
 
Most she touched me by her muteness&mdash; 
Most she won me by the way

Plea itself&mdash;for Charity&mdash;

Were there famine in the land&mdash; 
Were it my resource from starving&mdash;

I supposed&mdash;when sudden

Musicians Wrestle Everywhere 
 
Musicians wrestle everywhere&mdash; 
All day&mdash;among the crowded air 
I hear the silver strife&mdash; 
And&mdash;walking&mdash;long before the morn&mdash; 
Such transport breaks upon the town 
I think it that "New Life"! 
If is not Bird&mdash;it has no nest&mdash; 
Nor "Band"&mdash;in brass and scarlet&mdash;drest&mdash; 
Nor Tamborin&mdash;nor Man&mdash;

The "Morning Stars" the Treble led 
On Time's first Afternoon! 
Some&mdash;say&mdash;it is "the Spheres"&mdash;at play! 
Some say that bright Majority 
Of vanished Dames&mdash;and Men! 
Some&mdash;think it service in the place 
Where we&mdash;with late&mdash;celestial face&mdash; 
Please God&mdash;shall Ascertain!

MY cocoon tightens, colors tease,

My Faith Is Larger Than The Hills 
 
My Faith is larger than the Hills&mdash; 
So when the Hills decay&mdash; 
My Faith must take the Purple Wheel 
To show the Sun the way&mdash; 
'Tis first He steps upon the Vane&mdash; 
And then&mdash;upon the Hill&mdash; 
And then abroad the World He go 
To do His Golden Will&mdash;

The Bird would not arise&mdash;

No Bells have Paradise&mdash; 
How dare I, therefore, stint a faith 
On which so vast depends&mdash; 
Lest Firmament should fail for me&mdash;

My First Well Day—since Many Ill 
 
My first well Day—since many ill— 
I asked to go abroad, 
And take the Sunshine in my hands, 
And see the things in Pod— 
A 'blossom just when I went in 
To take my Chance with pain— 
Uncertain if myself, or He, 
Should prove the strongest One. 
The Summer deepened, while we strove— 
She put some flowers away— 
And Redder cheeked Ones—in their stead— 
A fond—illusive way— 
To cheat Herself, it seemed she tried— 
As if before a child 
To fade—Tomorrow—Rainbows held 
The Sepulchre, could hide. 
She dealt a fashion to the Nut— 
She tied the Hoods to Seeds— 
She dropped bright scraps of Tint, about— 
And left Brazilian Threads 
On every shoulder that she met— 
Then both her Hands of Haze 
Put up—to hide her parting Grace 
From our unfitted eyes. 
My loss, by sickness—Was it Loss? 
Or that Ethereal Gain 
One earns by measuring the Grave— 
Then—measuring the Sun— 
My Friend Attacks My Friend! 
 
My friend attacks my friend! 
Oh Battle picturesque! 
Then I turn Soldier too, 
And he turns Satirist! 
How martial is this place! 
Had I a mighty gun 
I think I'd shoot the human race 
And then to glory run!

My Life Closed Twice 
My life closed twice before its close-It 
yet remains to see 
If Immortality unveil 
A third event to me 
So huge, so hopeless to conceive 
As these that twice befell. 
Parting is all we know of heaven, 
And all we need of hell. 
My Life Had Stood 
My life had stood--a Loaded Gun-In 
Corners--till a Day 
The Owner passed--identified-And 
carried Me away-
And now We roam in Sovereign Woods-And 
now We hunt the Doe-And 
every time I speak for Him-The 
Mountains straight reply-
And do I smile, such cordial light 
Upon the Valley glow-It 
is as a Vesuvian face 
Had let its pleasure through-
And when at Night--Our good Day done-I 
guard My Master's Head-'
Tis better than the Eider-Duck's 
Deep Pillow--to have shared-
To foe of His--I'm deadly foe-None 
stir the second time-On 
whom I lay a Yellow Eye-Or 
an emphatic Thumb-
Though I than He--may longer live 
He longer must--than I-For 
I have but the power to kill, 
Without--the power to die-

My period had come for Prayer&mdash;

My Portion Is Defeat—today 
 
My Portion is Defeat—today— 
A paler luck than Victory— 
Less Paeans—fewer Bells— 
The Drums don't follow Me—with tunes— 
Defeat—a somewhat slower—means— 
More Arduous than Balls—

How different Victory

Who to have had it, would have been 
Contender—to die—

My wheel is in the dark!

Nature Rarer Uses Yellow 
Nature rarer uses yellow 
Than another hue; 
Saves she all of that for sunsets,-Prodigal 
of blue,

Like a lover's words. 
Nature The Gentlest Mother Is 
Nature the gentlest mother is, 
Impatient of no child, 
The feeblest of the waywardest. 
Her admonition mild 
In forest and the hill 
By traveller be heard, 
Restraining rampant squirrel 
Or too impetuous bird. 
How fair her conversation 
A summer afternoon, 
Her household her assembly; 
And when the sun go down, 
Her voice among the aisles 
Incite the timid prayer 
Of the minutest cricket, 
The most unworthy flower. 
When all the children sleep, 
She turns as long away 
As will suffice tolight her lamps, 
Then bending from the sky 
With infinite affection 
An infiniter care, 
Her golden finger on her lip, 
Wills silence everywhere.

Of All The Souls That Stand Create 
Of all the souls that stand create 
I have elected one. 
When sense from spirit files away, 
And subterfuge is done; 
When that which is and that which was 
Apart, intrinsic, stand, 
And this brief tragedy of flesh 
Is shifted like a sand; 
When figures show their royal front 
And mists are carved sway,-Behold 
the atom I Feferred 
To all the lists of clay! 
Of All The Sounds Despatched Abroad 
 
Of all the Sounds despatched abroad, 
There's not a Charge to me 
Like that old measure in the Boughs&mdash; 
That phraseless Melody&mdash; 
The Wind does&mdash;working like a Hand, 
Whose fingers Comb the Sky&mdash; 
Then quiver down&mdash;with tufts of Tune&mdash; 
Permitted Gods, and me&mdash; 
Inheritance, it is, to us&mdash; 
Beyond the Art to Earn&mdash; 
Beyond the trait to take away 
By Robber, since the Gain 
Is gotten not of fingers&mdash; 
And inner than the Bone&mdash; 
Hid golden, for the whole of Days, 
And even in the Urn, 
I cannot vouch the merry Dust 
Do not arise and play 
In some odd fashion of its own, 
Some quainter Holiday, 
When Winds go round and round in Bands&mdash; 
And thrum upon the door, 
And Birds take places, overhead, 
To bear them Orchestra. 
I crave Him grace of Summer Boughs, 
If such an Outcast be&mdash; 
Who never heard that fleshless Chant&mdash; 
Rise&mdash;solemn&mdash;on the Tree, 
As if some Caravan of Sound 
Off Deserts, in the Sky, 
Had parted Rank, 
Then knit, and swept&mdash; 
In Seamless Company&mdash; 
Of Being Is A Bird 
 
Of Being is a Bird 
The likest to the Down 
An Easy Breeze do put afloat 
The General Heavens&mdash;upon&mdash; 
It soars&mdash;and shifts&mdash;and whirls&mdash; 
And measures with the Clouds 
In easy&mdash;even&mdash;dazzling pace&mdash; 
No different the Birds&mdash; 
Except a Wake of Music 
Accompany their feet&mdash; 
As did the Down emit a Tune&mdash; 
For Ecstasy&mdash;of it 
Of Bronze—and Blaze 
 
Of Bronze—and Blaze— 
The North—Tonight— 
So adequate—it forms— 
So preconcerted with itself— 
So distant—to alarms— 
And Unconcern so sovereign 
To Universe, or me— 
Infects my simple spirit 
With Taints of Majesty— 
Till I take vaster attitudes— 
And strut upon my stem— 
Disdaining Men, and Oxygen, 
For Arrogance of them— 
My Splendors, are Menagerie— 
But their Completeless Show 
Will entertain the Centuries 
When I, am long ago, 
An Island in dishonored Grass— 
Whom none but Beetles—know. 
Of Brussels—it Was Not 
Of Brussels—it was not—

In hue—a mellow Dun—

But, principally—of Sun—
