And spread it on the Ground— 
Upholsterer of the Pines—is He— 
Upholsterer—of the Pond— 
Of Consciousness, Her Awful Mate 
 
Of Consciousness, her awful Mate 
The Soul cannot be rid&mdash; 
As easy the secreting her 
Behind the Eyes of God. 
The deepest hid is sighted first 
And scant to Him the Crowd&mdash; 
What triple Lenses burn upon 
The Escapade from God&mdash; 
Of Course—i Prayed 
 
Of Course—I prayed— 
And did God Care? 
He cared as much as on the Air 
A Bird—had stamped her foot— 
And cried "Give Me"— 
My Reason—Life— 
I had not had—but for Yourself— 
'Twere better Charity 
To leave me in the Atom's Tomb— 
Merry, and Nought, and gay, and numb— 
Than this smart Misery. 
Of Nearness To Her Sundered Things 
 
Of nearness to her sundered Things 
The Soul has special times&mdash; 
When Dimness&mdash;looks the Oddity&mdash; 
Distinctness&mdash;easy&mdash;seems&mdash; 
The Shapes we buried, dwell about, 
Familiar, in the Rooms&mdash; 
Untarnished by the Sepulchre, 
The Mouldering Playmate comes&mdash; 
In just the Jacket that he wore&mdash; 
Long buttoned in the Mold 
Since we&mdash;old mornings, Children&mdash;played&mdash; 
Divided&mdash;by a world&mdash; 
The Grave yields back her Robberies&mdash; 
The Years, our pilfered Things&mdash; 
Bright Knots of Apparitions 
Salute us, with their wings&mdash; 
As we&mdash;it were&mdash;that perished&mdash; 
Themself&mdash;had just remained till we rejoin them&mdash; 
And 'twas they, and not ourself 
That mourned. 
Of Silken Speech And Specious Shoe 
 
Of Silken Speech and Specious Shoe 
A Traitor is the Bee 
His service to the newest Grace 
Present continually 
His Suit a chance 
His Troth a Term 
Protracted as the Breeze 
Continual Ban propoundeth He 
Continual Divorce. 
Of so divine a Loss 
Of so divine a Loss 
We enter but the Gain, 
Indemnity for Loneliness 
That such a Bliss has been. 
Of Tolling Bell I Ask The Cause? 
 
Of Tolling Bell I ask the cause? 
"A Soul has gone to Heaven" 
I'm answered in a lonesome tone&mdash; 
Is Heaven then a Prison? 
That Bells should ring till all should know 
A Soul had gone to Heaven 
Would seem to me the more the way 
A Good News should be given. 
Of Tribulation, These Are They 
 
Of Tribulation, these are They, 
Denoted by the White&mdash; 
The Spangled Gowns, a lesser Rank 
Of Victors&mdash;designate&mdash; 
All these&mdash;did conquer&mdash; 
But the ones who overcame most times&mdash; 
Wear nothing commoner than Snow&mdash; 
No Ornament, but Palms&mdash; 
Surrender&mdash;is a sort unknown&mdash; 
On this superior soil&mdash; 
Defeat&mdash;an outgrown Anguish&mdash; 
Remembered, as the Mile 
Our panting Ankle barely passed&mdash; 
When Night devoured the Road&mdash; 
But we&mdash;stood whispering in the House&mdash; 
And all we said&mdash;was "Saved"! 
Of Yellow was the outer Sky 
Nature rarer uses Yellow 
Than another Hue. 
Saves she all of that for Sunsets 
Prodigal of Blue 
Spending Scarlet, like a Woman 
Yellow she affords 
Only scantly and selectly 
Like a Lover's Words. 
Oh Shadow on the Grass 
Oh Shadow on the Grass, 
Art thou a Step or not? 
Go make thee fair my Candidate 
My nominated Heart Oh 
Shadow on the Grass 
While I delay to guess 
Some other thou wilt consecrate Oh 
Unelected Face 
On A Columnar Self 
 
On a Columnar Self&mdash; 
How ample to rely 
In Tumult&mdash;or Extremity&mdash; 
How good the Certainty 
That Lever cannot pry&mdash; 
And Wedge cannot divide 
Conviction&mdash;That Granitic Base&mdash; 
Though None be on our Side&mdash; 
Suffice Us&mdash;for a Crowd&mdash; 
Ourself&mdash;and Rectitude&mdash; 
And that Assembly&mdash;not far off 
From furthest Spirit&mdash;God&mdash; 
On my volcano grows the Grass 
On my volcano grows the Grass 
A meditative spot An 
acre for a Bird to choose 
Would be the General thought 
How red the Fire rocks below How 
insecure the sod 
Did I disclose 
Would populate with awe my solitude. 
On Such A Night, Or Such A Night 
 
On such a night, or such a night, 
Would anybody care 
If such a little figure 
Slipped quiet from its chair&mdash; 
So quiet&mdash;Oh how quiet, 
That nobody might know 
But that the little figure 
Rocked softer&mdash;to and fro&mdash; 
On such a dawn, or such a dawn&mdash; 
Would anybody sigh 
That such a little figure 
Too sound asleep did lie 
For Chanticleer to wake it&mdash; 
Or stirring house below&mdash; 
Or giddy bird in orchard&mdash; 
Or early task to do? 
There was a little figure plump 
For every little knoll&mdash; 
Busy needles, and spools of thread&mdash; 
And trudging feet from school&mdash; 
Playmates, and holidays, and nuts&mdash; 
And visions vast and small&mdash; 
Strange that the feet so precious charged 
Should reach so small a goal! 
On That Dear Frame The Years Had Worn 
 
On that dear Frame the Years had worn 
Yet precious as the House 
In which We first experienced Light 
The Witnessing, to Us&mdash; 
Precious! It was conceiveless fair 
As Hands the Grave had grimed 
Should softly place within our own 
Denying that they died. 
On This Long Storm The Rainbow Rose 
 
On this long storm the Rainbow rose&mdash; 
On this late Morn&mdash;the Sun&mdash; 
The clouds&mdash;like listless Elephants&mdash; 
Horizons&mdash;straggled down&mdash; 
The Birds rose smiling, in their nests&mdash; 
The gales&mdash;indeed&mdash;were done&mdash; 
Alas, how heedless were the eyes&mdash; 
On whom the summer shone! 
The quiet nonchalance of death&mdash; 
No Daybreak&mdash;can bestir&mdash; 
The slow&mdash;Archangel's syllables 
Must awaken her! 
On This Wondrous Sea 
 
On this wondrous sea 
Sailing silently, 
Ho! Pilot, ho! 
Knowest thou the shore 
Where no breakers roar&mdash; 
Where the storm is o'er? 
In the peaceful west 
Many the sails at rest&mdash; 
The anchors fast&mdash; 
Thither I pilot thee&mdash; 
Land Ho! Eternity! 
Ashore at last! 
Once More, My Now Bewildered Dove 
 
Once more, my now bewildered Dove 
Bestirs her puzzled wings 
Once more her mistress, on the deep 
Her troubled question flings&mdash; 
Thrice to the floating casement 
The Patriarch's bird returned, 
Courage! My brave Columba! 
There may yet be Land! 
One And One—are One 
 
One and One—are One— 
Two—be finished using— 
Well enough for Schools— 
But for Minor Choosing— 
Life—just—or Death— 
Or the Everlasting— 
More—would be too vast 
For the Soul's Comprising— 
One Anguish—in A Crowd 
 
One Anguish—in a Crowd— 
A Minor thing—it sounds— 
And yet, unto the single Doe 
Attempted of the Hounds 
'Tis Terror as consummate 
As Legions of Alarm 
Did leap, full flanked, upon the Host— 
'Tis Units—make the Swarm— 
A Small Leech—on the Vitals— 
The sliver, in the Lung— 
The Bung out—of an Artery— 
Are scarce accounted—Harms— 
Yet might—by relation 
To that Repealless thing— 
A Being—impotent to end— 
When once it has begun— 
One Blessing Had I Than The Rest 
 
One Blessing had I than the rest 
So larger to my Eyes 
That I stopped gauging&mdash;satisfied&mdash; 
For this enchanted size&mdash; 
It was the limit of my Dream&mdash; 
The focus of my Prayer&mdash; 
A perfect&mdash;paralyzing Bliss&mdash; 
Contented as Despair&mdash; 
I knew no more of Want&mdash;or Cold&mdash; 
Phantasms both become 
For this new Value in the Soul&mdash; 
Supremest Earthly Sum&mdash; 
The Heaven below the Heaven above&mdash; 
Obscured with ruddier Blue&mdash; 
Life's Latitudes leant over&mdash;full&mdash; 
The Judgment perished&mdash;too&mdash; 
Why Bliss so scantily disburse&mdash; 
Why Paradise defer&mdash; 
Why Floods be served to Us&mdash;in Bowls&mdash; 
I speculate no more&mdash; 
One Crucifixion Is Recorded—only 
 
One Crucifixion is recorded—only— 
How many be 
Is not affirmed of Mathematics— 
Or History— 
One Calvary—exhibited to Stranger— 
As many be 
As persons—or Peninsulas— 
Gethsemane— 
Is but a Province—in the Being's Centre— 
Judea— 
For Journey—or Crusade's Achieving— 
Too near— 
Our Lord—indeed—made Compound Witness— 
And yet— 
There's newer—nearer Crucifixion 
Than That— 
One Day Is There Of The Series 
 
One Day is there of the Series 
Termed Thanksgiving Day. 
Celebrated part at Table 
Part in Memory. 
Neither Patriarch nor Pussy 
I dissect the Play 
Seems it to my Hooded thinking 
Reflex Holiday. 
Had there been no sharp Subtraction 
From the early Sum&mdash; 
Not an Acre or a Caption 
Where was once a Room&mdash; 
Not a Mention, whose small Pebble 
Wrinkled any Sea, 
Unto Such, were such Assembly 
'Twere Thanksgiving Day. 
One Dignity Delays For All 
 
One dignity delays for all&mdash; 
One mitred Afternoon&mdash; 
None can avoid this purple&mdash; 
None evade this Crown! 
Coach, it insures, and footmen&mdash; 
Chamber, and state, and throng&mdash; 
Bells, also, in the village 
As we ride grand along! 
What dignified Attendants! 
What service when we pause! 
How loyally at parting 
Their hundred hats they raise! 
Her pomp surpassing ermine 
When simple You, and I, 
Present our meek escutheon 
And claim the rank to die! 
One Life Of So Much Consequence! 
 
One Life of so much Consequence! 
Yet I&mdash;for it&mdash;would pay&mdash; 
My Soul's entire income&mdash; 
In ceaseless&mdash;salary&mdash; 
One Pearl&mdash;to me&mdash;so signal&mdash; 
That I would instant dive&mdash; 
Although&mdash;I knew&mdash;to take it&mdash; 
Would cost me&mdash;just a life! 
The Sea is full&mdash;I know it! 
That&mdash;does not blur my Gem! 
It burns&mdash;distinct from all the row&mdash; 
Intact&mdash;in Diadem! 
The life is thick&mdash;I know it! 
Yet&mdash;not so dense a crowd&mdash; 
But Monarchs&mdash;are perceptible&mdash; 
Far down the dustiest Road! 
One Need Not Be A Chamber To Be Haunted, 
One need not be a chamber to be haunted, 
One need not be a house; 
The brain has corridors surpassing 
Material place. 
Far safer, of a midnight meeting 
External ghost, 
Than an interior confronting 
That whiter host. 
Far safer through an Abbey gallop, 
The stones achase, 
Than, moonless, one's own self encounter 
In lonesome place. 
Ourself, behind ourself concealed, 
Should startle most; 
Assassin, hid in our apartment, 
Be horror's least. 
The prudent carries a revolver, 
He bolts the door, 
O'erlooking a superior spectre 
More near. 
One Sister Have I In Our House 
 
One Sister have I in our house, 
And one, a hedge away. 
There's only one recorded, 
But both belong to me. 
One came the road that I came&mdash; 
And wore my last year's gown&mdash; 
The other, as a bird her nest, 
Builded our hearts among. 
She did not sing as we did&mdash; 
It was a different tune&mdash; 
Herself to her a music 
As Bumble bee of June. 
Today is far from Childhood&mdash; 
But up and down the hills 
I held her hand the tighter&mdash; 
Which shortened all the miles&mdash; 
And still her hum 
The years among, 
Deceives the Butterfly; 
Still in her Eye 
The Violets lie 
Mouldered this many May. 
I spilt the dew&mdash; 
But took the morn&mdash; 
I chose this single star 
From out the wide night's numbers&mdash; 
Sue - forevermore! 
One Year Ago—jots What? 
 
One Year ago—jots what? 
God—spell the word! I—can't— 
Was't Grace? Not that— 
Was't Glory? That—will do— 
Spell slower—Glory— 
Such Anniversary shall be— 
Sometimes—not often—in Eternity— 
When farther Parted, than the Common Woe— 
Look—feed upon each other's faces—so— 
In doubtful meal, if it be possible 
Their Banquet's true— 
I tasted—careless—then— 
I did not know the Wine 
Came once a World—Did you? 
Oh, had you told me so— 
This Thirst would blister—easier—now— 
You said it hurt you—most— 
Mine—was an Acorn's Breast— 
And could not know how fondness grew 
In Shaggier Vest— 
Perhaps—I couldn't— 
But, had you looked in— 
A Giant—eye to eye with you, had been— 
No Acorn—then— 
So—Twelve months ago— 
We breathed— 
Then dropped the Air— 
Which bore it best? 
Was this—the patientest— 
Because it was a Child, you know— 
And could not value—Air? 
If to be "Elder"—mean most pain— 
I'm old enough, today, I'm certain—then— 
As old as thee—how soon? 
One—Birthday more—or Ten? 
Let me—choose! 
Ah, Sir, None! 
Only A Shrine, But Mine 
 
Only a Shrine, but Mine&mdash; 
I made the Taper shine&mdash; 
Madonna dim, to whom all Feet may come, 
Regard a Nun&mdash; 
Thou knowest every Woe&mdash; 
Needless to tell thee&mdash;so&mdash; 
But can'st thou do 
The Grace next to it&mdash;heal? 
That looks a harder skill to us&mdash; 
Still&mdash;just as easy, if it be thy Will 
To thee&mdash;Grant me&mdash; 
Thou knowest, though, so Why tell thee? 
Only God—detect The Sorrow 
 
Only God—detect the Sorrow— 
Only God— 
The Jehovahs—are no Babblers— 
Unto God— 
God the Son—Confide it— 
Still secure— 
God the Spirit's Honor— 
Just as sure— 
Our Journey Had Advanced; 
Our journey had advanced; 
Our feet were almost come 
To that odd fork in Being's road, 
Eternity by term. 
Our pace took sudden awe, 
Our feet reluctant led. 
Before were cities, but between, 
The forest of the dead. 
Retreat was out of hope,-Behind, 
a sealed route, 
Eternity's white flag before, 
And God at every gate. 
Our Little Kinsmen—after Rain 
 
Our little Kinsmen—after Rain 
In plenty may be seen, 
A Pink and Pulpy multitude 
The tepid Ground upon. 
A needless life, it seemed to me 
Until a little Bird 
As to a Hospitality 
Advanced and breakfasted. 
As I of He, so God of Me 
I pondered, may have judged, 
And left the little Angle Worm 
With Modesties enlarged. 
Our Lives Are Swiss 
Our lives are Swiss -So 
still -- so Cool -Till 
some odd afternoon 
The Alps neglect their Curtains 
And we look farther on! 
Italy stands the other side! 
While like a guard between -The 
solemn Alps -The 
siren Alps 
Forever intervene! 
Our Share Of Night To Bear 
 
Our share of night to bear&mdash; 
Our share of morning&mdash; 
Our blank in bliss to fill 
Our blank in scorning&mdash; 
Here a star, and there a star, 
Some lose their way! 
Here a mist, and there a mist, 
Afterwards&mdash;Day! 
Ourselves Were Wed One Summer—dear 
 
Ourselves were wed one summer—dear— 
Your Vision—was in June— 
And when Your little Lifetime failed, 
I wearied—too—of mine— 
And overtaken in the Dark— 
Where You had put me down— 
By Some one carrying a Light— 
I—too—received the Sign. 
'Tis true—Our Futures different lay— 
Your Cottage—faced the sun— 
While Oceans—and the North must be— 
On every side of mine 
'Tis true, Your Garden led the Bloom, 
For mine—in Frosts—was sown— 
And yet, one Summer, we were Queens— 
But You—were crowned in June— 
Out Of Sight? What Of That? 
 
Out of sight? What of that? 
See the Bird&mdash;reach it! 
Curve by Curve&mdash;Sweep by Sweep&mdash; 
Round the Steep Air&mdash; 
Danger! What is that to Her? 
Better 'tis to fail&mdash;there&mdash; 
Than debate&mdash;here&mdash; 
Blue is Blue&mdash;the World through&mdash; 
Amber&mdash;Amber&mdash;Dew&mdash;Dew&mdash; 
Seek&mdash;Friend&mdash;and see&mdash; 
Heaven is shy of Earth&mdash;that's all&mdash; 
Bashful Heaven&mdash;thy Lovers small&mdash; 
Hide&mdash;too&mdash;from thee&mdash; 
Over And Over, Like A Tune 
 
Over and over, like a Tune&mdash; 
The Recollection plays&mdash; 
Drums off the Phantom Battlements 
Cornets of Paradise&mdash; 
Snatches, from Baptized Generations&mdash; 
Cadences too grand 
But for the Justified Processions 
At the Lord's Right hand. 
Over The Fence 
 
Over the fence&mdash; 
Strawberries&mdash;grow&mdash; 
Over the fence&mdash; 
I could climb&mdash;if I tried, I know&mdash; 
Berries are nice! 
But&mdash;if I stained my Apron&mdash; 
God would certainly scold! 
Oh, dear,&mdash;I guess if He were a Boy&mdash; 
He'd&mdash;climb&mdash;if He could! 
Pain 
Pain--has an Element of Blank-It 
cannot recollect 
When it begun--or if there were 
A time when it was not-
It has no Future--but itself-Its 
Infinite Contain 
Its Past--enlightened to perceive 
New Periods--of Pain. 
Pain Has An Element 
Pain has an element of blank; 
It cannot recollect 
When it began, or if there were 
A day when it was not. 
It has no future but itself, 
Its infinite realms contain 
Its past, enlightened to perceive 
New periods of pain. 
Pain Has An Element Of Blank; 
Pain has an element of blank; 
It cannot recollect 
When it began, or if there were 
A day when it was not. 
It has no future but itself, 
Its infinite realms contain 
Its past, enlightened to perceive 
New periods of pain. 
Pain&Mdash;Expands The Time 
 
Pain&mdash;expands the Time&mdash; 
Ages coil within 
The minute Circumference 
Of a single Brain&mdash; 
Pain contracts&mdash;the Time&mdash; 
Occupied with Shot 
Gamuts of Eternities 
Are as they were not&mdash; 
Papa Above! 
 
Papa above! 
Regard a Mouse 
O'erpowered by the Cat! 
Reserve within thy kingdom 
A "Mansion" for the Rat! 
Snug in seraphic Cupboards 
To nibble all the day 
While unsuspecting Cycles 
Wheel solemnly away! 
Part Five: The Single Hound 
THE LARGEST fire ever known	 
Occurs each afternoon,	 
Discovered is without surprise,	 
Proceeds without concern:	 
Consumes, and no report to men,	
An Occidental town,	 
Rebuilt another morning	 
To be again burned down. 
Partake As Doth The Bee 
 
Partake as doth the Bee, 
Abstemiously. 
The Rose is an Estate&mdash; 
In Sicily. 
Patience—has A Quiet Outer 
 
Patience—has a quiet Outer— 
Patience—Look within— 
Is an Insect's futile forces 
Infinites—between— 
'Scaping one—against the other 
Fruitlesser to fling— 
Patience—is the Smile's exertion 
Through the quivering— 
Peace Is A Fiction Of Our Faith 
 
Peace is a fiction of our Faith&mdash; 
The Bells a Winter Night 
Bearing the Neighbor out of Sound 
That never did alight. 
Perhaps I Asked Too Large 
Perhaps I asked too large -I 
take -- no less than skies -For 
Earths, grow thick as 
Berries, in my native town -
My Basked holds -- just -- Firmaments -Those 
-- dangle easy -- on my arm, 
But smaller bundles -- Cram. 
Perhaps You Think Me Stooping 
 
Perhaps you think me stooping 
I'm not ashamed of that 
Christ&mdash;stooped until He touched the Grave&mdash; 
Do those at Sacrament 
Commemorative Dishonor 
Or love annealed of love 
Until it bend as low as Death 
Redignified, above? 
Perhaps You'D Like To Buy A Flower 
 
Perhaps you'd like to buy a flower, 
But I could never sell&mdash; 
If you would like to borrow, 
Until the Daffodil 
Unties her yellow Bonnet 
Beneath the village door, 
Until the Bees, from Clover rows 
Their Hock, and Sherry, draw, 
Why, I will lend until just then, 
But not an hour more! 
Pigmy Seraphs—gone Astray 
 
Pigmy seraphs—gone astray— 
Velvet people from Vevay— 
Balles from some lost summer day— 
Bees exclusive Coterie— 
Paris could not lay the fold 
Belted down with Emerald— 
Venice could not show a check 
Of a tint so lustrous meek— 
Never such an Ambuscade 
As of briar and leaf displayed 
For my little damask maid— 
I had rather wear her grace 
Than an Earl's distinguished face— 
I had rather dwell like her 
Than be "Duke of Exeter"— 
Royalty enough for me 
To subdue the Bumblebee. 
Poor Little Heart! 
 
Poor little Heart! 
Did they forget thee? 
Then dinna care! Then dinna care! 
Proud little Heart! 
Did they forsake thee? 
Be debonnaire! Be debonnaire! 
Frail little Heart! 
I would not break thee&mdash; 
Could'st credit me? Could'st credit me? 
Gay little Heart&mdash; 
Like Morning Glory! 
Wind and Sun&mdash;wilt thee array! 
Portraits Are To Daily Faces 
 
Portraits are to daily faces 
As an Evening West, 
To a fine, pedantic sunshine&mdash; 
In a satin Vest! 
Praise it -'tis dead 
Praise it -'tis dead It 
cannot glow Warm 
this inclement Ear 
With the encomium it earned 
Since it was gathered here Invest 
this alabaster Zest 
In the Delights of Dust Remitted 
-since it flitted it 
In recusance august. 
Prayer Is The Little Implement 
 
Prayer is the little implement 
Through which Men reach 
Where Presence&mdash;is denied them. 
They fling their Speech 
By means of it&mdash;in God's Ear&mdash; 
If then He hear&mdash; 
This sums the Apparatus 
Comprised in Prayer&mdash; 
Precious To Me—she Still Shall Be 
 
Precious to Me—She still shall be— 
Though She forget the name I bear— 
The fashion of the Gown I wear— 
The very Color of My Hair— 
So like the Meadows—now— 
I dared to show a Tress of Theirs 
If haply—She might not despise 
A Buttercup's Array— 
I know the Whole—obscures the Part— 
The fraction—that appeased the Heart 
Till Number's Empery— 
Remembered—as the Millner's flower 
When Summer's Everlasting Dower— 
Confronts the dazzled Bee. 
Presentiment Is That Long Shadow On The Lawn 
Presentiment is that long shadow on the lawn 
Indicative that suns go down; 
The notice to the startled grass 
That darkness is about to pass. 
Promise This—when You Be Dying 
 
Promise This—When You be Dying— 
Some shall summon Me— 
Mine belong Your latest Sighing— 
Mine—to Belt Your Eye— 
Not with Coins—though they be Minted 
From an Emperor's Hand— 
Be my lips—the only Buckle 
Your low Eyes—demand— 
Mine to stay—when all have wandered— 
To devise once more 
If the Life be too surrendered— 
Life of Mine—restore— 
Poured like this—My Whole Libation— 
Just that You should see 
Bliss of Death—Life's Bliss extol thro' 
Imitating You— 
Mine—to guard Your Narrow Precinct— 
To seduce the Sun 
Longest on Your South, to linger, 
Largest Dews of Morn 
To demand, in Your low favor 
Lest the Jealous Grass 
Greener lean—Or fonder cluster 
Round some other face— 
Mine to supplicate Madonna— 
If Madonna be 
Could behold so far a Creature— 
Christ—omitted—Me— 
Just to follow Your dear future— 
Ne'er so far behind— 
For My Heaven— 
Had I not been 
Most enough—denied? 
Proud Of My Broken Heart 
Proud of my broken heart, since thou didst break it. 
Proud of the pain, I did not feel? till thee. 
Proud of my night, since thou, with moons, dos't shake it. 
Not to partake thy passion, -my humility 
Thou can'st not boast, like Jesus, drunken without companion 
Was the strong cup of anguish brewed for the Nazarene 
Thou can'st not pierce tradition with the peerless puncture, 
See! I usurped thy crucifix to honor mine!

Purple—is Fashionable Twice 
 
Purple—is fashionable twice— 
This season of the year, 
And when a soul perceives itself 
To be an Emperor. 
Put Up My Lute! 
 
Put up my lute! 
What of&mdash;my Music! 
Since the sole ear I cared to charm&mdash; 
Passive&mdash;as Granite&mdash;laps My Music&mdash; 
Sobbing&mdash;will suit&mdash;as well as psalm! 
Would but the "Memnon" of the Desert&mdash; 
Teach me the strain 
That vanquished Him&mdash; 
When He&mdash;surrendered to the Sunrise&mdash; 
Maybe&mdash;that&mdash;would awaken&mdash;them! 
Read—sweet—how Others—strove 
 
Read—Sweet—how others—strove— 
Till we—are stouter— 
What they—renounced— 
Till we—are less afraid— 
How many times they—bore the faithful witness— 
Till we—are helped— 
As if a Kingdom—cared! 
Read then—of faith— 
That shone above the fagot— 
Clear strains of Hymn 
The River could not drown— 
Brave names of Men— 
And Celestial Women— 
Passed out—of Record 
Into—Renown! 
Rearrange a 'Wife's' affection! 
Rearrange a 'Wife's' affection! 
When they dislocate my Brain! 
Amputate my freckled Bosom! 
Make me bearded like a man! 
Blush, my spirit, in thy Fastness Blush, 
my unacknowledged clay Seven 
years of troth have taught thee 
More than Wifehood every may! 
Love that never leaped its socket Trust 
entrenched in narrow pain Constancy 
thro' fire -awarded Anguish 
-bare of anodyne! 
Burden -borne so far triumphant None 
suspect me of the crown, 
For I wear the 'Thorns' till Sunset Then 
-my Diadem put on. 
Big my Secret but it's bandaged It 
will never get away 
Till the Day its Weary Keeper 
Leads it through the Grave to thee.

Revolution is the Pod

Robbed By Death—but That Was Easy 
 
Robbed by Death—but that was easy— 
To the failing Eye 
I could hold the latest Glowing— 
Robbed by Liberty 
For Her Jugular Defences— 
This, too, I endured— 
Hint of Glory—it afforded— 
For the Brave Beloved— 
Fraud of Distance—Fraud of Danger, 
Fraud of Death—to bear— 
It is Bounty—to Suspense's 
Vague Calamity— 
Stalking our entire Possession 
On a Hair's result— 
Then—seesawing—coolly—on it— 
Trying if it split— 
Safe In Their Alabaster Chambers, 
Safe in their alabaster chambers, 
Untouched by morning and untouched by noon, 
Sleep the meek members of the resurrection, 
Rafter of satin, and roof of stone. 
Light laughs the breeze in her castle of sunshine; 
Babbles the bee in a stolid ear; 
Pipe the sweet birds in ignorant cadences, -Ah, 
what sagacity perished here! 
Grand go the years in the crescent above them; 
Worlds scoop their arcs, and firmaments row, 
Diadems drop and Doges surrender, 
Soundless as dots on a disk of snow. 
Said Death To Passion 
Said Death to Passion 
'Give of thine an Acre unto me.' 
Said Passion, through contracting Breaths 
'A Thousand Times Thee Nay.' 
Bore Death from Passion 
All His East 
He -sovereign as the Sun 
Resituated in the West 
And the Debate was done.

That were the little load&mdash;

The Heart I carried in my own&mdash; 
Till mine too heavy grew&mdash; 
Yet&mdash;strangest&mdash;heavier since it went&mdash; 
Is it too large for you?

I&mdash;hastened to demand

She Bore It Till The Simple Veins 
 
She bore it till the simple veins 
Traced azure on her hand&mdash; 
Til pleading, round her quiet eyes 
The purple Crayons stand. 
Till Daffodils had come and gone 
I cannot tell the sum, 
And then she ceased to bear it&mdash; 
And with the Saints sat down. 
No more her patient figure 
At twilight soft to meet&mdash; 
No more her timid bonnet 
Upon the village street&mdash; 
But Crowns instead, and Courtiers&mdash; 
And in the midst so fair, 
Whose but her shy&mdash;immortal face 
Of whom we're whispering here? 
She could not live upon the Past 
She could not live upon the Past 
The Present did not know her 
And so she sought this sweet at last 
And nature gently owned her 
The mother that has not a knell 
for either Duke or Robin 
She Dealt Her Pretty Words Like Blades 
 
She dealt her pretty words like Blades&mdash; 
How glittering they shone&mdash; 
And every One unbared a Nerve 
Or wantoned with a Bone&mdash; 
She never deemed&mdash;she hurt&mdash; 
That&mdash;is not Steel's Affair&mdash; 
A vulgar grimace in the Flesh&mdash; 
How ill the Creatures bear&mdash; 
To Ache is human&mdash;not polite&mdash; 
The Film upon the eye 
Mortality's old Custom&mdash; 
Just locking up&mdash;to Die. 
She Died At Play 
 
She died at play, 
Gambolled away 
Her lease of spotted hours, 
Then sank as gaily as a Turn 
Upon a Couch of flowers. 
Her ghost strolled softly o'er the hill 
Yesterday, and Today, 
Her vestments as the silver fleece&mdash; 
Her countenance as spray. 
She Died—this Was The Way She Died 
 
She died—this was the way she died. 
And when her breath was done 
Took up her simple wardrobe 
And started for the sun. 
Her little figure at the gate 
The Angels must have spied, 
Since I could never find her 
Upon the mortal side.

She dwelleth in the Ground&mdash;

She Lay As If At Play 
 
She lay as if at play 
Her life had leaped away&mdash; 
Intending to return&mdash; 
But not so soon&mdash;

An instant had forgot&mdash; 
The Trick to start&mdash;

She Rose To His Requirement 
 
She rose to His Requirement&mdash;dropt 
The Playthings of Her Life 
To take the honorable Work 
Of Woman, and of Wife&mdash;

She slept beneath a tree&mdash;

She Staked Her Feathers—gained An Arc 
 
She staked her Feathers—Gained an Arc— 
Debated—Rose again— 
This time—beyond the estimate 
Of Envy, or of Men— 
And now, among Circumference— 
Her steady Boat be seen— 
At home—among the Billows—As

She Sweeps With Many-Colored Brooms, 
She sweeps with many-colored brooms, 
And leaves the shreds behind; 
Oh, housewife in the evening west, 
Come back, and dust the pond! 
You dropped a purple ravelling in, 
You dropped an amber thread; 
And now you've littered all the East 
With duds of emerald! 
And still she plies her spotted brooms, 
And still the aprons fly, 
Till brooms fade softly into stars -And 
then I come away.

She went as quiet as the Dew

At the Accustomed hour!

Less skillful than Le Verriere 
It's sorer to believe!

Sic Transit Gloria Mundi 
 
"Sic transit gloria mundi," 
"How doth the busy bee," 
"Dum vivimus vivamus," 
I stay mine enemy! 
Oh "veni, vidi, vici!" 
Oh caput cap-a-pie! 
And oh "memento mori" 
When I am far from thee! 
Hurrah for Peter Parley! 
Hurrah for Daniel Boone! 
Three cheers, sir, for the gentleman 
Who first observed the moon! 
Peter, put up the sunshine; 
Patti, arrange the stars; 
Tell Luna, tea is waiting, 
And call your brother Mars! 
Put down the apple, Adam, 
And come away with me, 
So shalt thou have a pippin 
From off my father's tree! 
I climb the "Hill of Science," 
I "view the landscape o'er;" 
Such transcendental prospect, 
I ne'er beheld before! 
Unto the Legislature 
My country bids me go; 
I'll take my india rubbers, 
In case the wind should blow! 
During my education, 
It was announced to me 
That gravitation, stumbling, 
Fell from an apple tree! 
The earth upon an axis 
Was once supposed to turn, 
By way of a gymnastic 
In honor of the sun! 
It was the brave Columbus, 
A sailing o'er the tide, 
Who notified the nations 
Of where I would reside! 
Mortality is fatal&mdash; 
Gentility is fine, 
Rascality, heroic, 
Insolvency, sublime! 
Our Fathers being weary, 
Laid down on Bunker Hill; 
And tho' full many a morning, 
Yet they are sleeping still,&mdash; 
The trumpet, sir, shall wake them, 
In dreams I see them rise, 
Each with a solemn musket 
A marching to the skies! 
A coward will remain, Sir, 
Until the fight is done; 
But an immortal hero 
Will take his hat, and run! 
Good bye, Sir, I am going; 
My country calleth me; 
Allow me, Sir, at parting, 
To wipe my weeping e'e. 
In token of our friendship 
Accept this "Bonnie Doon," 
And when the hand that plucked it 
Hath passed beyond the moon, 
The memory of my ashes 
Will consolation be; 
Then, farewell, Tuscarora, 
And farewell, Sir, to thee!

Silence is all we dread. 
There's Ransom in a Voice But

Himself have not a face.

Sleep Is Supposed To Be 
 
Sleep is supposed to be 
By souls of sanity 
The shutting of the eye. 
Sleep is the station grand 
Down which, on either hand 
The hosts of witness stand! 
Morn is supposed to be 
By people of degree 
The breaking of the Day. 
Morning has not occurred! 
That shall Aurora be&mdash; 
East of Eternity&mdash; 
One with the banner gay&mdash; 
One in the red array&mdash; 
That is the break of Day!

Sun&mdash;withdrawn to Recognition&mdash; 
Furthest shining&mdash;done&mdash; 
Yet was not the foe&mdash;of any&mdash; 
Not the smallest Bird 
In the nearest Orchard dwelling 
Be of Me&mdash;afraid. 
Most&mdash;I love the Cause that slew Me. 
Often as I die 
Its beloved Recognition 
Holds a Sun on Me&mdash; 
Best&mdash;at Setting&mdash;as is Nature's&mdash; 
Neither witnessed Rise 
Till the infinite Aurora 
In the other's eyes. 
Success Is Counted Sweetest 
Success is counted sweetest 
By those who ne'er succeed. 
To comprehend a nectar 
Requires sorest need. 
Not one of all the purple Host 
Who took the Flag today 
Can tell the definition 
So clear of Victory 
As he defeated--dying-On 
whose forbidden ear 
The distant strains of triumph 
Burst agonized and clear! 
Such Is The Force Of Happiness 
 
Such is the Force of Happiness&mdash; 
The Least&mdash;can lift a Ton 
Assisted by its stimulus&mdash; 
Who Misery&mdash;sustain&mdash; 
No Sinew can afford&mdash; 
The Cargo of Themselves&mdash; 
Too infinite for Consciousness' 
Slow capabilities. 
Summer For Thee, Grant I May Be 
 
Summer for thee, grant I may be 
When Summer days are flown! 
Thy music still, when Whipporwill 
And Oriole&mdash;are done! 
For thee to bloom, I'll skip the tomb 
And row my blossoms o'er! 
Pray gather me&mdash; 
Anemone&mdash; 
Thy flower&mdash;forevermore! 
Summer Shower 
A drop fell on the apple tree, 
Another on the roof; 
A half a dozen kissed the eaves, 
And made the gables laugh. 
A few went out to help the brook, 
That went to help the sea. 
Myself conjectured, Were they pearls, 
What necklaces could be! 
The dust replaced in hoisted roads, 
The birds jocoser sung; 
The sunshine threw his hat away, 
The orchards spangles hung. 
The breezes brought dejected lutes, 
And bathed them in the glee; 
The East put out a single flag, 
And signed the fete away. 
Sunset At Night—is Natural 
 
Sunset at Night—is natural— 
But Sunset on the Dawn 
Reverses Nature—Master— 
So Midnight's—due—at Noon. 
Eclipses be—predicted— 
And Science bows them in— 
But do one face us suddenly— 
Jehovah's Watch—is wrong. 
Superfluous Were The Sun 
 
Superfluous were the Sun 
When Excellence be dead 
He were superfluous every Day 
For every Day be said 
That syllable whose Faith 
Just saves it from Despair 
And whose "I'll meet You" hesitates 
If Love inquire "Where"? 
Upon His dateless Fame 
Our Periods may lie 
As Stars that drop anonymous 
From an abundant sky. 
Surgeons Must Be Very Careful 
 
Surgeons must be very careful 
When they take the knife! 
Underneath their fine incisions 
Stirs the Culprit&mdash;Life! 
Suspense—is Hostiler Than Death 
 
Suspense—is Hostiler than Death— 
Death—tho'soever Broad, 
Is Just Death, and cannot increase— 
Suspense—does not conclude— 
But perishes—to live anew— 
But just anew to die— 
Annihilation—plated fresh 
With Immortality— 
Sweet Mountains—ye Tell Me No Lie 
 
Sweet Mountains—Ye tell Me no lie— 
Never deny Me—Never fly— 
Those same unvarying Eyes 
Turn on Me—when I fail—or feign, 
Or take the Royal names in vain— 
Their far—slow—Violet Gaze— 
My Strong Madonnas—Cherish still— 
The Wayward Nun—beneath the Hill— 
Whose service—is to You— 
Her latest Worship—When the Day 
Fades from the Firmament away— 
To lift Her Brows on You— 
Sweet&Mdash;Safe&Mdash;Houses 
 
Sweet&mdash;safe&mdash;Houses&mdash; 
Glad&mdash;gay&mdash;Houses&mdash; 
Sealed so stately tight&mdash; 
Lids of Steel&mdash;on Lids of Marble&mdash; 
Locking Bare feet out&mdash; 
Brooks of Plush&mdash;in Banks of Satin 
Not so softly fall 
As the laughter&mdash;and the whisper&mdash; 
From their People Pearl&mdash; 
No Bald Death&mdash;affront their Parlors&mdash; 
No Bold Sickness come 
To deface their Stately Treasures&mdash; 
Anguish&mdash;and the Tomb&mdash; 
Hum by&mdash;in Muffled Coaches&mdash; 
Lest they&mdash;wonder Why&mdash; 
Any&mdash;for the Press of Smiling&mdash; 
Interrupt&mdash;to die&mdash; 
Sweet&Mdash;You Forgot&Mdash;But I Remembered 
 
Sweet&mdash;You forgot&mdash;but I remembered 
Every time&mdash;for Two&mdash; 
So that the Sum be never hindered 
Through Decay of You&mdash; 
Say if I erred? Accuse my Farthings&mdash; 
Blame the little Hand 
Happy it be for You&mdash;a Beggar's&mdash; 
Seeking More&mdash;to spend&mdash; 
Just to be Rich&mdash;to waste my Guineas 
On so Best a Heart&mdash; 
Just to be Poor&mdash;for Barefoot Vision 
You&mdash;Sweet&mdash;Shut me out&mdash; 
Sweet, To Have Had Them Lost 
 
Sweet, to have had them lost 
For news that they be saved&mdash; 
The nearer they departed Us 
The nearer they, restored, 
Shall stand to Our Right Hand&mdash; 
Most precious and the Dead&mdash; 
Next precious 
Those that rose to go&mdash; 
Then thought of Us, and stayed.

T Was Just This Time Last Year I Died. 
'T was just this time last year I died. 
I know I heard the corn, 
When I was carried by the farms,-It 
had the tassels on. 
I thought how yellow it would look 
When Richard went to mill; 
And then I wanted to get out, 
But something held my will. 
I thought just how red apples wedged 
The stubble's joints between; 
And carts went stooping round the fields 
To take the pumpkins in. 
I wondered which would miss me least, 
And when Thanksgiving came, 
If father'd multiply the plates 
To make an even sum. 
And if my stocking hung too high, 
Would it blur the Christmas glee, 
That not a Santa Claus could reach 
The altitude of me? 
But this sort grieved myself, and so 
I thought how it would be 
When just this time, some perfect year, 
Themselves should come to me. 
Take Your Heaven Further On 
 
Take your Heaven further on&mdash; 
This&mdash;to Heaven divine Has gone&mdash; 
Had You earlier blundered in 
Possibly, e'en You had seen 
An Eternity&mdash;put on&mdash; 
Now&mdash;to ring a Door beyond 
Is the utmost of Your Hand&mdash; 
To the Skies&mdash;apologize&mdash; 
Nearer to Your Courtesies 
Than this Sufferer polite&mdash; 
Dressed to meet You&mdash; 
See&mdash;in White! 
Taking Up The Fair Ideal 
 
Taking up the fair Ideal, 
Just to cast her down 
When a fracture&mdash;we discover&mdash; 
Or a splintered Crown&mdash; 
Makes the Heavens portable&mdash; 
And the Gods&mdash;a lie&mdash; 
Doubtless&mdash;"Adam"&mdash;scowled at Eden&mdash; 
For his perjury! 
Cherishing&mdash;our pool Ideal&mdash; 
Till in purer dress&mdash; 
We behold her&mdash;glorified&mdash; 
Comforts&mdash;search&mdash;like this&mdash; 
Till the broken creatures&mdash; 
We adored&mdash;for whole&mdash; 
Stains&mdash;all washed&mdash; 
Transfigured&mdash;mended&mdash; 
Meet us&mdash;with a smile&mdash; 
Talk With Prudence To A Beggar 
 
Talk with prudence to a Beggar 
Of "Potose," and the mines! 
Reverently, to the Hungry 
Of your viands, and your wines! 
Cautious, hint to any Captive 
You have passed enfranchised feet! 
Anecdotes of air in Dungeons 
Have sometimes proved deadly sweet! 
Teach Him—when He Makes The Names 
 
Teach Him—When He makes the names— 
Such an one—to say— 
On his babbling—Berry—lips— 
As should sound—to me— 
Were my Ear—as near his nest— 
As my thought—today— 
As should sound— 
"Forbid us not"— 
Some like "Emily." 
Tell All The Truth 
Tell all the truth but tell it slant, 
Success in circuit lies, 
Too bright for our infirm delight 
The truth's superb surprise; 
As lightning to the children eased 
With explanation kind, 
The truth must dazzle gradually 
Or every man be blind.

Tell as a Marksman -were forgotten

That After Horror—that 'Twas Us 
 
That after Horror—that 'twas us— 
That passed the mouldering Pier— 
Just as the Granite Crumb let go— 
Our Savior, by a Hair— 
A second more, had dropped too deep 
For Fisherman to plumb— 
The very profile of the Thought 
Puts Recollection numb— 
The possibility—to pass 
Without a Moment's Bell— 
Into Conjecture's presence— 
Is like a Face of Steel— 
That suddenly looks into ours 
With a metallic grin— 
The Cordiality of Death— 
Who drills his Welcome in— 
That Distance Was Between Us 
 
That Distance was between Us 
That is not of Mile or Main&mdash;

Equator&mdash;never can&mdash; 
That First Day, When You Praised Me, Sweet 
 
That first Day, when you praised Me, Sweet, 
And said that I was strong&mdash; 
And could be mighty, if I liked&mdash; 
That Day&mdash;the Days among&mdash; 
Glows Central&mdash;like a Jewel 
Between Diverging Golds&mdash; 
The Minor One&mdash;that gleamed behind&mdash; 
And Vaster&mdash;of the World's. 
That I Did Always Love 
 
That I did always love 
I bring thee Proof

I never lived&mdash;Enough&mdash; 
That I shall love alway&mdash; 
I argue thee 
That love is life&mdash; 
And life hath Immortality&mdash;

That is solemn we have ended 
Be it but a Play 
Or a Glee among the Garret

Or a leaving Home, or later, 
Parting with a World 
We have understood for better

The Admirations—and Contempts—of Time 
 
The Admirations—and Contempts—of time— 
Show justest—through an Open Tomb— 
The Dying—as it were a Height 
Reorganizes Estimate 
And what We saw not 
We distinguish clear— 
And mostly—see not 
What We saw before— 
'Tis Compound Vision— 
Light—enabling Light— 
The Finite—furnished 
With the Infinite— 
Convex—and Concave Witness— 
Back—toward Time— 
And forward— 
Toward the God of Him— 
The Angle Of A Landscape 
 
The Angle of a Landscape&mdash; 
That every time I wake&mdash; 
Between my Curtain and the Wall 
Upon an ample Crack&mdash; 
Like a Venetian&mdash;waiting&mdash; 
Accosts my open eye&mdash; 
Is just a Bough of Apples&mdash; 
Held slanting, in the Sky&mdash; 
The Pattern of a Chimney&mdash; 
The Forehead of a Hill&mdash; 
Sometimes&mdash;a Vane's Forefinger&mdash; 
But that's&mdash;Occasional&mdash; 
The Seasons&mdash;shift&mdash;my Picture&mdash; 
Upon my Emerald Bough, 
I wake&mdash;to find no&mdash;Emeralds&mdash; 
Then&mdash;Diamonds&mdash;which the Snow 
From Polar Caskets&mdash;fetched me&mdash; 
The Chimney&mdash;and the Hill&mdash; 
And just the Steeple's finger&mdash; 
These&mdash;never stir at all&mdash; 
The Bat Is Dun With Wrinkled Wings	 
THE BAT is dun with wrinkled wings	 
Like fallow article,	 
And not a song pervades his lips,	 
Or none perceptible.	 
His small umbrella, quaintly halved, 
Describing in the air	 
An arc alike inscrutable,—	 
Elate philosopher!	 
Deputed from what firmament	 
Of what astute abode, 
Empowered with what malevolence	 
Auspiciously withheld.	 
To his adroit Creator	 
Ascribe no less the praise;	 
Beneficent, believe me, 
His eccentricities. 
The Battle Fought Between The Soul 
 
The Battle fought between the Soul 
And No Man&mdash;is the One 
Of all the Battles prevalent&mdash; 
By far the Greater One&mdash; 
No News of it is had abroad&mdash; 
Its Bodiless Campaign 
Establishes, and terminates&mdash; 
Invisible&mdash;Unknown&mdash; 
Nor History&mdash;record it&mdash; 
As Legions of a Night 
The Sunrise scatters&mdash;These endure&mdash; 
Enact&mdash;and terminate&mdash; 
The Battlefield 
They dropped like flakes, they dropped like stars, 
Like petals from a rose, 
When suddenly across the June 
A wind with fingers goes. 
They perished in the seamless grass, — 
No eye could find the place; 
But God on his repealless list 
Can summon every face. 
The Bee Is Not Afraid Of Me 
 
The Bee is not afraid of me. 
I know the Butterfly. 
The pretty people in the Woods 
Receive me cordially&mdash; 
The Brooks laugh louder when I come&mdash; 
The Breezes madder play; 
Wherefore mine eye thy silver mists, 
Wherefore, Oh Summer's Day?

The Beggar Lad&Mdash;Dies Early 
 
The Beggar Lad&mdash;dies early&mdash;

The Bible Is An Antique Volume 
 
The Bible is an antique Volume&mdash; 
Written by faded men 
At the suggestion of Holy Spectres&mdash; 
Subjects&mdash;Bethlehem&mdash; 
Eden&mdash;the ancient Homestead&mdash; 
Satan&mdash;the Brigadier&mdash; 
Judas&mdash;the Great Defaulter&mdash; 
David&mdash;the Troubador&mdash; 
Sin&mdash;a distinguished Precipice 
Others must resist&mdash;

Other Boys are "lost"&mdash; 
Had but the Tale a warbling Teller&mdash; 
All the Boys would come&mdash; 
Orpheus' Sermon captivated&mdash; 
It did not condemn&mdash;

The Birds Begun At Four O'Clock 
 
The Birds begun at Four o'clock&mdash; 
Their period for Dawn&mdash; 
A Music numerous as space&mdash; 
But neighboring as Noon&mdash; 
I could not count their Force&mdash; 
Their Voices did expend 
As Brook by Brook bestows itself 
To multiply the Pond. 
Their Witnesses were not&mdash; 
Except occasional man&mdash; 
In homely industry arrayed&mdash; 
To overtake the Morn&mdash; 
Nor was it for applause&mdash; 
That I could ascertain&mdash; 
But independent Ecstasy 
Of Deity and Men&mdash; 
By Six, the Flood had done&mdash; 
No Tumult there had been 
Of Dressing, or Departure&mdash; 
And yet the Band was gone&mdash; 
The Sun engrossed the East&mdash; 
The Day controlled the World&mdash; 
The Miracle that introduced 
Forgotten, as fulfilled. 
The Birds Reported From The South 
 
The Birds reported from the South&mdash; 
A News express to Me&mdash; 
A spicy Charge, My little Posts&mdash; 
But I am deaf&mdash;Today&mdash; 
The Flowers&mdash;appealed&mdash;a timid Throng&mdash; 
I reinforced the Door&mdash; 
Go blossom for the Bees&mdash;I said&mdash; 
And trouble Me&mdash;no More&mdash; 
The Summer Grace, for Notice strove&mdash; 
Remote&mdash;Her best Array&mdash; 
The Heart&mdash;to stimulate the Eye 
Refused too utterly&mdash; 
At length, a Mourner, like Myself, 
She drew away austere&mdash; 
Her frosts to ponder&mdash;then it was 
I recollected Her&mdash; 
She suffered Me, for I had mourned&mdash; 
I offered Her no word&mdash; 
My Witness&mdash;was the Crape I bore&mdash; 
Her&mdash;Witness&mdash;was Her Dead&mdash; 
Thenceforward&mdash;We&mdash;together dwelt&mdash; 
I never questioned Her&mdash; 
Our Contract 
A Wiser Sympathy 
The Black Berry—wears A Thorn In His Side 
The Black Berry—wears a Thorn in his side— 
But no Man heard Him cry— 
He offers His Berry, just the same 
To Partridge—and to Boy— 
He sometimes holds upon the Fence— 
Or struggles to a Tree— 
Or clasps a Rock, with both His Hands— 
But not for Sympathy— 
We—tell a Hurt—to cool it— 
This Mourner—to the Sky 
A little further reaches—instead— 
Brave Black Berry— 
The Blue Jay 
No brigadier throughout the year 
So civic as the jay. 
A neighbor and a warrior too, 
With shrill felicity 
Pursuing winds that censure us 
A February day, 
The brother of the universe 
Was never blown away. 
The snow and he are intimate; 
I 've often seen them play 
When heaven looked upon us all 
With such severity, 
I felt apology were due 
To an insulted sky, 
Whose pompous frown was nutriment 
To their temerity. 
The pillow of this daring head 
Is pungent evergreens; 
His larder — terse and militant — 
Unknown, refreshing things; 
His character a tonic, 
His future a dispute; 
Unfair an immortality 
That leaves this neighbor out. 
The Body Grows Without 
 
The Body grows without&mdash; 
The more convenient way&mdash; 
That if the Spirit&mdash;like to hide 
Its Temple stands, alway, 
Ajar&mdash;secure&mdash;inviting&mdash; 
It never did betray 
The Soul that asked its shelter 
In solemn honesty

Runs evenly and true;

'T were easier for you 
To put the water back 
When floods have slit the hills, 
And scooped a turnpike for themselves, 
And blotted out the mills!

The Butterfly Upon The Sky 
The Butterfly upon the Sky, 
That doesn't know its Name 
And hasn't any tax to pay

The Butterfly's Assumption Gown 
The Butterfly's Assumption Gown 
In Chrysoprase Apartments hung

The Chariot 
Because I could not stop for Death, 
He kindly stopped for me; 
The carriage held but just ourselves 
And Immortality. 
We slowly drove, he knew no haste, 
And I had put away 
My labor, and my leisure too, 
For his civility. 
We passed the school where children played, 
Their lessons scarcely done; 
We passed the fields of gazing grain, 
We passed the setting sun. 
We paused before a house that seemed 
A swelling of the ground; 
The roof was scarcely visible. 
The cornice but a mound. 
Since then 'tis centuries; but each 
Feels shorter than the day 
I first surmised the horses' heads 
Were toward eternity. 
The Chemical Conviction 
 
The Chemical conviction 
That Nought be lost 
Enable in Disaster 
My fractured Trust&mdash; 
The Faces of the Atoms 
If I shall see 
How more the Finished Creatures 
Departed me! 
The Child's Faith Is New 
 
The Child's faith is new&mdash; 
Whole&mdash;like His Principle&mdash; 
Wide&mdash;like the Sunrise 
On fresh Eyes&mdash; 
Never had a Doubt&mdash; 
Laughs&mdash;at a Scruple&mdash; 
Believes all sham 
But Paradise&mdash; 
Credits the World&mdash;

To hold mistaken 
His pretty estimates 
Of Prickly Things 
He gains the skill 
Sorrowful&mdash;as certain&mdash; 
Men&mdash;to anticipate 
Instead of Kings&mdash;

The Clover's simple Fame

And workmen finished, one by one,
 Their seam the day upon. 
The low grass loaded with the dew, 
The twilight stood as strangers do 
With hat in hand, polite and new,
 To stay as if, or go. 
A vastness, as a neighbor, came,-A 
wisdom without face or name, 
A peace, as hemispheres at home,-
And so the night became. 
The Daisy Follows Soft The Sun 
 
The Daisy follows soft the Sun&mdash; 
And when his golden walk is done&mdash; 
Sits shyly at his feet&mdash; 
He&mdash;waking&mdash;finds the flower there&mdash; 
Wherefore&mdash;Marauder&mdash;art thou here? 
Because, Sir, love is sweet! 
We are the Flower&mdash;Thou the Sun! 
Forgive us, if as days decline&mdash; 
We nearer steal to Thee! 
Enamored of the parting West&mdash; 
The peace&mdash;the flight&mdash;the Amethyst&mdash; 
Night's possibility! 
The Day Came Slow 
The day came slow, till five o'clock, 
Then sprang before the hills, 
Like hindered rubies, or the light, 
A sudden musket spills. 
The purple could not keep the east. 
The sunrise shook from fold. 
Like breadths of topaz, packed a night, 
The lady just unrolled. 
The happy winds their timbrels took; 
The birds in docile rows, 
Arranged themselves around their prince. 
(The wind is prince of those.) 
The orchard sparkled like a Jew,--How 
mighty 'twas to stay, 
A guest in this stupendous place, 
The parlor of the day. 
The Day That I Was Crowned 
 
The Day that I was crowned 
Was like the other Days&mdash; 
Until the Coronation came&mdash; 
And then&mdash;'twas Otherwise&mdash; 
As Carbon in the Coal 
And Carbon in the Gem 
Are One&mdash;and yet the former 
Were dull for Diadem&mdash; 
I rose, and all was plain&mdash; 
But when the Day declined 
Myself and It, in Majesty 
Were equally&mdash;adorned&mdash; 
The Grace that I&mdash;was chose&mdash; 
To Me&mdash;surpassed the Crown 
That was the Witness for the Grace&mdash; 
'Twas even that 'twas Mine&mdash; 
The Day Undressed&Mdash;Herself 
 
The Day undressed&mdash;Herself&mdash; 
Her Garter&mdash;was of Gold&mdash; 
Her Petticoat&mdash;of Purple plain&mdash; 
Her Dimities&mdash;as old 
Exactly&mdash;as the World&mdash; 
And yet the newest Star&mdash; 
Enrolled upon the Hemisphere 
Be wrinkled&mdash;much as Her&mdash; 
Too near to God&mdash;to pray&mdash; 
Too near to Heaven&mdash;to fear&mdash; 
The Lady of the Occident 
Retired without a care&mdash; 
Her Candle so expire 
The flickering be seen 
On Ball of Mast in Bosporus&mdash; 
And Dome&mdash;and Window Pane&mdash; 
The Definition Of Beauty Is 
 
The Definition of Beauty is 
That Definition is none&mdash; 
Of Heaven, easing Analysis, 
Since Heaven and He are one. 
The Devil -had he fidelity 
The Devil -had he fidelity 
Would be the best friend Because 
he has ability But 
Devils cannot mend Perfidy 
is the virtue 
That would but he resign 
The Devil -without question 
Were thoroughly divine 
The Difference Between Despair 
 
The difference between Despair 
And Fear&mdash;is like the One 
Between the instant of a Wreck 
And when the Wreck has been&mdash; 
The Mind is smooth&mdash;no Motion&mdash; 
Contented as the Eye 
Upon the Forehead of a Bust&mdash; 
That knows&mdash;it cannot see&mdash; 
The Doomed—regard The Sunrise 
 
The Doomed—regard the Sunrise 
With different Delight— 
Because—when next it burns abroad 
They doubt to witness it— 
The Man—to die—tomorrow— 
Harks for the Meadow Bird— 
Because its Music stirs the Axe 
That clamors for his head— 
Joyful—to whom the Sunrise 
Precedes Enamored—Day— 
Joyful—for whom the Meadow Bird 
Has ought but Elegy! 
The Drop, That Wrestles In The Sea 
 
The Drop, that wrestles in the Sea&mdash; 
Forgets her own locality&mdash; 
As I&mdash;toward Thee&mdash; 
She knows herself an incense small&mdash; 
Yet small&mdash;she sighs&mdash;if All&mdash;is All&mdash; 
How larger&mdash;be? 
The Ocean&mdash;smiles&mdash;at her Conceit&mdash; 
But she, forgetting Amphitrite&mdash; 
Pleads&mdash;"Me"? 
The Dust Behind I Strove To Join 
 
The Dust behind I strove to join 
Unto the Disk before&mdash; 
But Sequence ravelled out of Sound 
Like Balls upon a Floor&mdash; 
The Duties Of The Wind Are Few 
The duties of the Wind are few, 
To cast the ships, at Sea, 
Establish March, the Floods escort, 
And usher Liberty. 
The pleasures of the Wind are broad, 
To dwell Extent among, 
Remain, or wander, 
Speculate, or Forests entertain. 
The kinsmen of the Wind are Peaks 
Azof -the Equinox, 
Also with Bird and Asteroid 
A bowing intercourse. 
The limitations of the Wind 
Do he exist, or die, 
Too wise he seems for Wakelessness, 
However, know not i. 
The Dying Need But Little, Dear,-
The dying need but little, dear,-A 
glass of water's all, 
A flower's unobtrusive face 
To punctuate the wall, 
A fan, perhaps, a friend's regret, 
And certainly that one 
No color in the rainbow 
Perceives when you are gone. 
The Earth Has Many Keys 
The earth has many keys, 
Where melody is not 
Is the unknown peninsula. 
Beauty is nature's fact. 
But witness for her land, 
And witness for her sea, 
The cricket is her utmost 
Of elegy to me. 
The Face I Carry With Me—last 
 
The face I carry with me—last— 
When I go out of Time— 
To take my Rank—by—in the West— 
That face—will just be thine— 
I'll hand it to the Angel— 
That—Sir—was my Degree— 
In Kingdoms—you have heard the Raised— 
Refer to—possibly. 
He'll take it—scan it—step aside— 
Return—with such a crown 
As Gabriel—never capered at— 
And beg me put it on— 
And then—he'll turn me round and round— 
To an admiring sky— 
As one that bore her Master's name— 
Sufficient Royalty! 
The Face we choose to miss 
The Face we choose to miss Be 
it but for a Day 
As absent as a Hundred Years, 
When it has rode away. 
The Feet Of People Walking Home 
 
The feet of people walking home 
With gayer sandals go&mdash; 
The Crocus&mdash; til she rises 
The Vassal of the snow&mdash; 
The lips at Hallelujah 
Long years of practise bore 
Til bye and bye these Bargemen 
Walked singing on the shore. 
Pearls are the Diver's farthings 
Extorted from the Sea&mdash; 
Pinions&mdash; the Seraph's wagon 
Pedestrian once&mdash; as we&mdash; 
Night is the morning's Canvas 
Larceny&mdash; legacy&mdash; 
Death, but our rapt attention 
To Immortality. 
My figures fail to tell me 
How far the Village lies&mdash; 
Whose peasants are the Angels&mdash; 
Whose Cantons dot the skies&mdash; 
My Classics veil their faces&mdash; 
My faith that Dark adores&mdash; 
Which from its solemn abbeys 
Such ressurection pours. 
The Fingers Of The Light 
 
The Fingers of the Light 
Tapped soft upon the Town 
With "I am great and cannot wait 
So therefore let me in." 
"You're soon," the Town replied, 
"My Faces are asleep&mdash; 
But swear, and I will let you by, 
You will not wake them up." 
The easy Guest complied 
But once within the Town 
The transport of His Countenance 
Awakened Maid and Man 
The Neighbor in the Pool 
Upon His Hip elate 
Made loud obeisance and the Gnat 
Held up His Cup for Light. 
The First Day That I Was A Life 
 
The first Day that I was a Life 
I recollect it&mdash;How still&mdash; 
That last Day that I was a Life 
I recollect it&mdash;as well&mdash; 
'Twas stiller&mdash;though the first 
Was still&mdash; 
"Twas empty&mdash;but the first 
Was full&mdash; 
This&mdash;was my finallest Occasion&mdash; 
But then 
My tenderer Experiment 
Toward Men&mdash; 
"Which choose I"? 
That&mdash;I cannot say&mdash; 
"Which choose They"? 
Question Memory! 
The First Day's Night Had Come 
 
The first Day's Night had come&mdash; 
And grateful that a thing 
So terrible&mdash;had been endured&mdash; 
I told my Soul to sing&mdash; 
She said her Strings were snapt&mdash; 
Her Bow&mdash;to Atoms blown&mdash; 
And so to mend her&mdash;gave me work 
Until another Morn&mdash; 
And then&mdash;a Day as huge 
As Yesterdays in pairs, 
Unrolled its horror in my face&mdash; 
Until it blocked my eyes&mdash; 
My Brain&mdash;begun to laugh&mdash; 
I mumbled&mdash;like a fool&mdash; 
And tho' 'tis Years ago&mdash;that Day&mdash; 
My Brain keeps giggling&mdash;still. 
And Something's odd&mdash;within&mdash; 
That person that I was&mdash; 
And this One&mdash;do not feel the same&mdash; 
Could it be Madness&mdash;this? 
The Flower Must Not Blame The Bee 
 
The Flower must not blame the Bee&mdash; 
That seeketh his felicity 
Too often at her door&mdash; 
But teach the Footman from Vevay&mdash; 
Mistress is "not at home"&mdash;to say&mdash; 
To people&mdash;any more! 
The Future—never Spoke 
 
The Future—never spoke— 
Nor will He—like the Dumb— 
Reveal by sign—a syllable 
Of His Profound To Come— 
But when the News be ripe— 
Presents it—in the Act— 
Forestalling Preparation— 
Escape—or Substitute— 
Indifference to Him— 
The Dower—as the Doom— 
His Office—but to execute 
Fate's—Telegram—to Him— 
The Gentian Weaves Her Fringes 
 
The Gentian weaves her fringes&mdash; 
The Maple's loom is red&mdash; 
My departing blossoms
 Obviate parade. 
A brief, but patient illness&mdash; 
An hour to prepare, 
And one below this morning 
Is where the angels are&mdash; 
It was a short procession, 
The Bobolink was there&mdash; 
An aged Bee addressed us&mdash; 
And then we knelt in prayer&mdash; 
We trust that she was willing&mdash; 
We ask that we may be. 
Summer&mdash;Sister&mdash;Seraph! 
Let us go with thee! 
In the name of the Bee&mdash; 
And of the Butterfly&mdash; 
And of the Breeze&mdash;Amen! 
The Going From A World We Know 
The going from a world we know 
To one a wonder still 
Is like the child's adversity 
Whose vista is a hill, 
Behind the hill is sorcery 
And everything unknown, 
But will the secret compensate 
For climbing it alone?

The good Will of a Flower

Must first present 
Certificate

The Grace—Myself—might not obtain—

For I—inhabit Her— 
The Grass So Little Has To Do 
The Grass so little has to do – 
A Sphere of simple Green – 
With only Butterflies to brood 
And Bees to entertain – 
And stir all day to pretty Tunes 
The Breezes fetch along – 
And hold the Sunshine in its lap 
And bow to everything – 
And thread the Dews, all night, like Pearls – 
And make itself so fine 
A Duchess were too common 
For such a noticing – 
And even when it dies – to pass 
In Odors so divine – 
Like Lowly spices, lain to sleep – 
Or Spikenards, perishing – 
And then, in Sovereign Barns to dwell – 
And dream the Days away, 
The Grass so little has to do 
I wish I were a Hay – 
The grave my little cottage is 
The grave my little cottage is, 
Where 'Keeping house' for thee 
I make my parlor orderly 
And lay the marble tea. 
For two divided, briefly, 
A cycle, it may be, 
Till everlasting life unite 
In strong society. 
The Guest Is Gold And Crimson 
 
The Guest is gold and crimson&mdash; 
An Opal guest and gray&mdash; 
Of Ermine is his doublet&mdash; 
His Capuchin gay&mdash; 
He reaches town at nightfall&mdash; 
He stops at every door&mdash; 
Who looks for him at morning 
I pray him too&mdash;explore 
The Lark's pure territory&mdash; 
Or the Lapwing's shore! 
The Hallowing Of Pain 
 
The hallowing of Pain 
Like hallowing of Heaven, 
Obtains at a corporeal cost&mdash; 
The Summit is not given 
To Him who strives severe 
At middle of the Hill&mdash; 
But He who has achieved the Top&mdash; 
All&mdash;is the price of All&mdash; 
The Heart Asks Pleasure First 
The heart asks pleasure first 
And then, excuse from pain-
And then, those little anodynes 
That deaden suffering; 
And then, to go to sleep; 
And then, if it should be 
The will of its Inquisitor, 
The liberty to die. 
The Heart Has Narrow Banks 
 
The Heart has narrow Banks 
It measures like the Sea 
In mighty&mdash;unremitting Bass 
And Blue Monotony 
Till Hurricane bisect 
And as itself discerns 
Its sufficient Area 
The Heart convulsive learns 
That Calm is but a Wall 
Of unattempted Gauze 
An instant's Push demolishes 
A Questioning&mdash;dissolves. 
The Heaven Vests For Each 
 
The Heaven vests for Each 
In that small Deity 
It craved the grace to worship 
Some bashful Summer's Day&mdash; 
Half shrinking from the Glory 
It importuned to see 
Till these faint Tabernacles drop 
In full Eternity&mdash; 
How imminent the Venture&mdash; 
As one should sue a Star&mdash; 
For His mean sake to leave the Row 
And entertain Despair&mdash; 
A Clemency so common&mdash; 
We almost cease to fear&mdash; 
Enabling the minutest&mdash; 
And furthest&mdash;to adore&mdash; 
The Hills erect their Purple Heads 
The Hills erect their Purple Heads 
The Rivers lean to see 
Yet Man has not of all the Throng 
A Curiosity. 
The Hills in Purple syllables 
The Hills in Purple syllables 
The Day's Adventures tell 
To little Groups of Continents 
Just going Home from School. 
The Himmaleh Was Known To Stoop 
 
The Himmaleh was known to stoop 
Unto the Daisy low&mdash; 
Transported with Compassion 
That such a Doll should grow 
Where Tent by Tent&mdash;Her Universe 
Hung out its Flags of Snow&mdash; 
The Hollows Round His Eager Eyes 
 
The Hollows round His eager Eyes 
Were Pages where to read 
Pathetic Histories&mdash;although 
Himself had not complained. 
Biography to All who passed 
Of Unobtrusive Pain 
Except for the italic Face 
Endured, unhelped&mdash;unknown.

The Judge Is Like The Owl 
 
The Judge is like the Owl&mdash; 
I've heard my Father tell&mdash; 
And Owls do build in Oaks&mdash; 
So here's an Amber Sill&mdash; 
That slanted in my Path&mdash; 
When going to the Barn&mdash;

Itself is not in vain&mdash; 
About the price&mdash;'tis small&mdash; 
I only ask a Tune 
At Midnight&mdash;Let the Owl select 
His favorite Refrain.

The Juggler's Hat her Country is&mdash;

The Lady feeds Her little Bird

The Lamp burns sure—within— 
Tho' Serfs—supply the Oil— 
It matters not the busy Wick— 
At her phosphoric toil! 
The Slave—forgets—to fill— 
The Lamp—burns golden—on— 
Unconscious that the oil is out— 
As that the Slave—is gone. 
The Last Night That She Lived 
 
The last Night that She lived 
It was a Common Night 
Except the Dying&mdash;this to Us 
Made Nature different 
We noticed smallest things&mdash; 
Things overlooked before 
By this great light upon our Minds 
Italicized&mdash;as 'twere. 
As We went out and in 
Between Her final Room 
And Rooms where Those to be alive 
Tomorrow were, a Blame 
That Others could exist 
While She must finish quite 
A Jealousy for Her arose 
So nearly infinite&mdash; 
We waited while She passed&mdash; 
It was a narrow time&mdash; 
Too jostled were Our Souls to speak 
At length the notice came. 
She mentioned, and forgot&mdash; 
Then lightly as a Reed 
Bent to the Water, struggled scarce&mdash; 
Consented, and was dead&mdash; 
And We&mdash;We placed the Hair&mdash; 
And drew the Head erect&mdash; 
And then an awful leisure was 
Belief to regulate&mdash; 
The Leaves Like Women Interchange 
 
The Leaves like Women interchange 
Exclusive Confidence&mdash; 
Somewhat of nods and somewhat 
Portentous inference. 
The Parties in both cases 
Enjoining secrecy&mdash; 
Inviolable compact 
To notoriety. 
The Loneliness One Dare Not Sound 
 
The Loneliness One dare not sound&mdash; 
And would as soon surmise 
As in its Grave go plumbing 
To ascertain the size&mdash; 
The Loneliness whose worst alarm 
Is lest itself should see&mdash; 
And perish from before itself 
For just a scrutiny&mdash; 
The Horror not to be surveyed&mdash; 
But skirted in the Dark&mdash; 
With Consciousness suspended&mdash; 
And Being under Lock&mdash; 
I fear me this&mdash;is Loneliness&mdash; 
The Maker of the soul 
Its Caverns and its Corridors 
Illuminate&mdash;or seal&mdash; 
The Lonesome For They Know Not What 
 
The lonesome for they know not What&mdash; 
The Eastern Exiles&mdash;be&mdash; 
Who strayed beyond the Amber line 
Some madder Holiday&mdash; 
And ever since&mdash;the purple Moat 
They strive to climb&mdash;in vain&mdash; 
As Birds&mdash;that tumble from the clouds 
Do fumble at the strain&mdash; 
The Blessed Ether&mdash;taught them&mdash; 
Some Transatlantic Morn&mdash; 
When Heaven&mdash;was too common&mdash;to miss&mdash; 
Too sure&mdash;to dote upon! 
The Love A Life Can Show Below 
 
The Love a Life can show Below 
Is but a filament, I know, 
Of that diviner thing 
That faints upon the face of Noon&mdash; 
And smites the Tinder in the Sun&mdash; 
And hinders Gabriel's Wing&mdash; 
'Tis this&mdash;in Music&mdash;hints and sways&mdash; 
And far abroad on Summer days&mdash; 
Distils uncertain pain&mdash; 
'Tis this enamors in the East&mdash; 
And tints the Transit in the West 
With harrowing Iodine&mdash; 
'Tis this&mdash;invites&mdash;appalls&mdash;endows&mdash; 
Flits&mdash;glimmers&mdash;proves&mdash;dissolves&mdash; 
Returns&mdash;suggests&mdash;convicts&mdash;enchants&mdash; 
Then&mdash;flings in Paradise&mdash; 
The Luxury To Apprehend 
 
The Luxury to apprehend 
The Luxury 'twould be 
To look at Thee a single time

In whatsoever Presence makes 
Till for a further Food 
I scarcely recollect to starve

The Luxury to meditate 
The Luxury it was 
To banguet on thy Countenance 
A Sumptuousness bestows 
On plainer Days, whose Table far

Is laden with a single Crumb 
The Consciousness of Thee.

The Malay—took the Pearl—

Home to the Hut! What lot 
Had I—the Jewel—got— 
Borne on a Dusky Breasty— 
I had not deemed a Vest 
Of Amber—fit— 
The Negro never knew 
I—wooed it—too— 
To gain, or be undone— 
Alike to Him—One—

The Months Have Ends—the Years—a Knot 
 
The Months have ends—the Years—a knot— 
No Power can untie

The Earth lays back these tired lives 
In her mysterious Drawers— 
Too tenderly, that any doubt 
An ultimate Repose— 
The manner of the Children— 
Who weary of the Day— 
Themself—the noisy Plaything 
They cannot put away— 
The Moon Was But A Chin Of Gold 
 
The Moon was but a Chin of Gold 
A Night or two ago&mdash; 
And now she turns Her perfect Face 
Upon the World below&mdash; 
Her Forehead is of Amplest Blonde&mdash; 
Her Cheek&mdash;a Beryl hewn&mdash; 
Her Eye unto the Summer Dew 
The likest I have known&mdash; 
Her Lips of Amber never part&mdash; 
But what must be the smile 
Upon Her Friend she could confer 
Were such Her Silver Will&mdash; 
And what a privilege to be 
But the remotest Star&mdash; 
For Certainty She take Her Way 
Beside Your Palace Door&mdash; 
Her Bonnet is the Firmament&mdash; 
The Universe&mdash;Her Shoe&mdash; 
The Stars&mdash;the Trinkets at Her Belt&mdash; 
Her Dimities&mdash;of Blue&mdash;

The Morning after Woe&mdash;

The Morns Are Meeker Than They Were

Lest I should be old fashioned

The Mountain sat upon the Plain

Grandfather of the Days is He

The Mountains—grow unnoticed—

The Murmur Of A Bee 
 
The Murmur of a Bee 
A Witchcraft&mdash;yieldeth me&mdash; 
If any ask me why&mdash; 
'Twere easier to die&mdash; 
Than tell&mdash; 
The Red upon the Hill 
Taketh away my will&mdash; 
If anybody sneer&mdash; 
Take care&mdash;for God is here&mdash; 
That's all. 
The Breaking of the Day 
Addeth to my Degree&mdash; 
If any ask me how&mdash; 
Artist&mdash;who drew me so&mdash; 
Must tell! 
The Mushroom is the Elf of Plants 
The Mushroom is the Elf of Plants At 
Evening, it is not 
At Morning, in a Truffled Hut 
It stop opon a Spot 
As if it tarried always 
And yet it's whole Career 
Is shorter than a Snake's Delay And 
fleeter than a Tare 
'Tis Vegetation's Juggler The 
Germ of Alibi Doth 
like a Bubble antedate 
And like a Bubble, hie 
I feel as if the Grass was pleased 
To have it intermit This 
surreptitious Scion 
Of Summer's circumspect. 
Had Nature any supple Face 
Or could she one contemn Had 
Nature an Apostate That 
Mushroom - it is Him! 
The Mystery Of Pain 
Pain has an element of blank; 
It cannot recollect 
When it began, or if there were 
A day when it was not. 
It has no future but itself, 
Its infinite realms contain 
Its past, enlightened to perceive 
New periods of pain. 
The Name—of It—is 'Autumn' 
 
The name—of it—is 'Autumn'— 
The hue—of it—is Blood— 
An Artery—upon the Hill— 
A Vein—along the Road— 
Great Globules—in the Alleys— 
And Oh, the Shower of Stain— 
When Winds—upset the Basin— 
And spill the Scarlet Rain— 
It sprinkles Bonnets—far below— 
It gathers ruddy Pools— 
Then—eddies like a Rose—away— 
Upon Vermilion Wheels— 
The Nearest Dream Recedes, Unrealized. 
The nearest dream recedes, unrealized. 
The heaven we chase 
Like the June bee 
Before the school-boy 
Invites the race; 
Stoops to an easy clover 
Dips--evades--teases--deploys; 
Then to the royal clouds 
Lifts his light pinnace 
Heedless of the boy 
Staring, bewildered, at the mocking sky.
 Homesick for steadfast honey, 
Ah! the bee flies not 
That brews that rare variety. 
The Night Was Wide, And Furnished Scant 
 
The Night was wide, and furnished scant 
With but a single Star&mdash;

The Only Ghost I Ever Saw 
The only ghost I ever saw 
Was dressed in mechlin, --so; 
He wore no sandal on his foot, 
And stepped like flakes of snow. 
His gait was soundless, like the bird, 
But rapid, like the roe; 
His fashions quaint, mosaic, 
Or, haply, mistletoe. 
Hi conversation seldom, 
His laughter like the breeze 
That dies away in dimples 
Among the pensive trees. 
Our interview was transient, -Of 
me, himself was shy; 
And God forbid I look behind 
Since that appalling day!

The Railway Train 
I like to see it lap the miles, 
And lick the valleys up, 
And stop to feed itself at tanks; 
And then, prodigious, step 
Around a pile of mountains, 
And, supercilious, peer 
In shanties by the sides of roads; 
And then a quarry pare 
To fit its sides, and crawl between, 
Complaining all the while 
In horrid, hooting stanza; 
Then chase itself down the hill 
And neigh like Boanerges; 
Then, punctual as a star, 
Stop - docile and omnipotent At 
its own stable door.

The Sun kept stooping—stooping—low!

Her unanointed forehead— 
Henceforth—Her only One!

The Way I read a Letter's—this—

The Wind Didn'T Come From The Orchard—today 
 
The Wind didn't come from the Orchard—today— 
Further than that— 
Nor stop to play with the Hay— 
Nor joggle a Hat— 
He's a transitive fellow—very— 
Rely on that— 
If He leave a Bur at the door 
We know He has climbed a Fir— 
But the Fir is Where—Declare— 
Were you ever there? 
If He brings Odors of Clovers— 
And that is His business—not Ours— 
Then He has been with the Mowers— 
Whetting away the Hours 
To sweet pauses of Hay— 
His Way—of a June Day— 
If He fling Sand, and Pebble— 
Little Boys Hats—and Stubble— 
With an occasional Steeple— 
And a hoarse "Get out of the way, I say," 
Who'd be the fool to stay? 
Would you—Say— 
Would you be the fool to stay? 
The Wind Tapped Like A Tired Man, 
The wind tapped like a tired man, 
And like a host, 'Come in,' 
I boldly answered; entered then 
My residence within 
A rapid, footless guest, 
To offer whom a chair 
Were as impossible as hand 
A sofa to the air. 
No bone had he to bind him, 
His speech was like the push 
Of numerous humming-birds at once 
From a superior bush. 
His countenance a billow, 
His fingers, if he pass, 
Let go a music, as of tunes 
Blown tremulous in glass. 
He visited, still flitting; 
Then, like a timid man, 
Again he tapped- 't was flurriedly-
And I became alone.

Myself&mdash;for scarcely settled&mdash; 
The Phoebes have begun&mdash; 
And then&mdash;it's time to strike my Tent&mdash; 
And open House&mdash;again&mdash; 
It's mostly, interruptions&mdash; 
My Summer&mdash;is despoiled&mdash; 
Because there was a Winter&mdash;once&mdash; 
And al the Cattle&mdash;starved&mdash; 
And so there was a Deluge&mdash; 
And swept the World away&mdash; 
But Ararat's a Legend&mdash;now&mdash; 
And no one credits Noah&mdash; 
The Woodpecker 
His bill an auger is, 
His head, a cap and frill. 
He laboreth at every tree,-A 
worm his utmost goal.

The words the happy say 
Are paltry melody 
But those the silent feel 
Are beautiful— 
The Work Of Her That Went 
The Work of Her that went, 
The Toil of Fellows done In 
Ovens green our Mother bakes, 
By Fires of the Sun.

Their Height In Heaven Comforts Not 
 
Their Height in Heaven comforts not&mdash;

There are two Ripenings—one—of sight—

There Came A Day At Summer's Full 
 
There came a Day at Summer's full, 
Entirely for me&mdash; 
I thought that such were for the Saints, 
Where Resurrections&mdash;be&mdash; 
The Sun, as common, went abroad, 
The flowers, accustomed, blew, 
As if no soul the solstice passed 
That maketh all things new&mdash; 
The time was scarce profaned, by speech&mdash; 
The symbol of a word 
Was needless, as at Sacrament, 
The Wardrobe&mdash;of our Lord&mdash; 
Each was to each The Sealed Church, 
Permitted to commune this&mdash;time&mdash; 
Lest we too awkward show 
At Supper of the Lamb. 
The Hours slid fast&mdash;as Hours will, 
Clutched tight, by greedy hands&mdash; 
So faces on two Decks, look back, 
Bound to opposing lands&mdash; 
And so when all the time had leaked, 
Without external sound 
Each bound the Other's Crucifix&mdash; 
We gave no other Bond&mdash; 
Sufficient troth, that we shall rise&mdash; 
Deposed&mdash;at length, the Grave&mdash; 
To that new Marriage, 
Justified&mdash;through Calvaries of Love&mdash;

There cam a Wind like a Bugle It 
quivered through the Grass 
And a Green Chill upon the Heat 
So ominous did pass 
We barred the Windows and the Doors 
As from an Emerald Ghost The 
Doom's electric Moccasin 
The very instant passed On 
a strange Mob of panting Trees 
And Fences fled away 
And Rivers where the Houses ran 
Those looked that lived - that Day The 
Bell within the steeple wild 
The flying tidings told How 
much can come 
And much can go, 
And yet abide the World!

There comes a warning like a spy

There Is A Flower That Bees Prefer 
 
There is a flower that Bees prefer&mdash; 
And Butterflies&mdash;desire&mdash; 
To gain the Purple Democrat 
The Humming Bird&mdash;aspire&mdash; 
And Whatsoever Insect pass&mdash; 
A Honey bear away 
Proportioned to his several dearth

Her face be rounder than the Moon 
And ruddier than the Gown

Before the World be Green&mdash; 
Her sturdy little Countenance 
Against the Wind&mdash;be seen&mdash; 
Contending with the Grass&mdash; 
Near Kinsman to Herself&mdash; 
For Privilege of Sod and Sun&mdash; 
Sweet Litigants for Life&mdash; 
And when the Hills be full&mdash; 
And newer fashions blow&mdash; 
Doth not retract a single spice

Her Public&mdash;be the Noon&mdash;

The Bravest&mdash;of the Host&mdash; 
Surrendering&mdash;the last&mdash; 
Nor even of Defeat&mdash;aware&mdash; 
What cancelled by the Frost&mdash; 
There Is A June When Corn Is Cut 
 
There is a June when Corn is cut 
And Roses in the Seed&mdash; 
A Summer briefer than the first 
But tenderer indeed 
As should a Face supposed the Grave's 
Emerge a single Noon 
In the Vermilion that it wore 
Affect us, and return&mdash; 
Two Seasons, it is said, exist&mdash; 
The Summer of the Just, 
And this of Ours, diversified 
With Prospect, and with Frost&mdash; 
May not our Second with its First 
So infinite compare 
That We but recollect the one 
The other to prefer? 
There Is A Languor Of The Life 
 
There is a Languor of the Life 
More imminent than Pain&mdash; 
'Tis Pain's Successor&mdash;When the Soul 
Has suffered all it can&mdash; 
A Drowsiness&mdash;diffuses&mdash; 
A Dimness like a Fog 
Envelops Consciousness&mdash; 
As Mists&mdash;obliterate a Crag. 
The Surgeon&mdash;does not blanch&mdash;at pain 
His Habit&mdash;is severe&mdash; 
But tell him that it ceased to feel&mdash; 
The Creature lying there&mdash; 
And he will tell you&mdash;skill is late&mdash; 
A Mightier than He&mdash; 
Has ministered before Him&mdash; 
There's no Vitality. 
There Is A Morn By Men Unseen 
 
There is a morn by men unseen&mdash; 
Whose maids upon remoter green 
Keep their Seraphic May&mdash; 
And all day long, with dance and game, 
And gambol I may never name&mdash; 
Employ their holiday. 
Here to light measure, move the feet 
Which walk no more the village street&mdash; 
Nor by the wood are found&mdash; 
Here are the birds that sought the sun 
When last year's distaff idle hung 
And summer's brows were bound. 
Ne'er saw I such a wondrous scene&mdash; 
Ne'er such a ring on such a green&mdash; 
Nor so serene array&mdash; 
As if the stars some summer night 
Should swing their cups of Chrysolite&mdash; 
And revel till the day&mdash; 
Like thee to dance&mdash;like thee to sing&mdash; 
People upon the mystic green&mdash; 
I ask, each new May Morn. 
I wait thy far, fantastic bells&mdash; 
Unto the different dawn!

There is a pain—so utter— 
It swallows substance up— 
Then covers the Abyss with Trance— 
So Memory can step 
Around—across—upon it— 
As one within a Swoon— 
Goes safely—where an open eye— 
Would drop Him—Bone by Bone.

There Is A Word 
 
There is a word 
Which bears a sword 
Can pierce an armed man&mdash; 
It hurls its barbed syllables 
And is mute again&mdash; 
But where it fell 
The saved will tell 
On patriotic day, 
Some epauletted Brother 
Gave his breath away. 
Wherever runs the breathless sun&mdash; 
Wherever roams the day&mdash; 
There is its noiseless onset&mdash; 
There is its victory! 
Behold the keenest marksman! 
The most accomplished shot! 
Time's sublimest target 
Is a soul "forgot!"

There Is Another Sky 
There is another sky, 
Ever serene and fair, 
And there is another sunshine, 
Though it be darkness there; 
Never mind faded forests, Austin, 
Never mind silent fields— 
Here is a little forest, 
Whose leaf is ever green; 
Here is a brighter garden, 
Where not a frost has been; 
In its unfading flowers 
I hear the bright bee hum: 
Prithee, my brother, 
Into my garden come!

There is no frigate like a book

Without oppress of toll; 
How frugal is the chariot

There is no Silence in the Earth -so silent

There's a certain Slant of light,

There's Been A Death In The Opposite House 
There's been a death in the opposite house 
As lately as to-day. 
I know it by the numb look 
Such houses have alway. 
The neighbors rustle in and out, 
The doctor drives away. 
A window opens like a pod, 
Abrupt, mechanically; 
Somebody flings a mattress out,-The 
children hurry by; 
They wonder if It died on that,-I 
used to when a boy. 
The minister goes stiffly in 
As if the house were his, 
And he owned all the mourners now, 
And little boys besides; 
And then the milliner, and the man 
Of the appalling trade, 
To take the measure of the house. 
There'll be that dark parade 
Of tassels and of coaches soon; 
It's easy as a sign,-
The intuition of the news 
In just a country town. 
There's Something Quieter Than Sleep 
 
There's something quieter than sleep 
Within this inner room! 
It wears a sprig upon its breast&mdash; 
And will not tell its name. 
Some touch it, and some kiss it&mdash; 
Some chafe its idle hand&mdash; 
It has a simple gravity 
I do not understand! 
I would not weep if I were they&mdash; 
How rude in one to sob! 
Might scare the quiet fairy 
Back to her native wood! 
While simple-hearted neighbors 
Chat of the "Early dead"&mdash; 
We&mdash;prone to periphrasis 
Remark that Birds have fled!

Eternity is ample,

This Chasm, Sweet, Upon My Life 
 
This Chasm, Sweet, upon my life 
I mention it to you, 
When Sunrise through a fissure drop 
The Day must follow too. 
If we demur, its gaping sides 
Disclose as 'twere a Tomb 
Ourself am lying straight wherein 
The Favorite of Doom. 
When it has just contained a Life 
Then, Darling, it will close 
And yet so bolder every Day 
So turbulent it grows 
I'm tempted half to stitch it up 
With a remaining Breath 
I should not miss in yielding, though 
To Him, it would be Death&mdash; 
And so I bear it big about 
My Burial&mdash;before 
A Life quite ready to depart 
Can harass me no more&mdash; 
This Consciousness That Is Aware 
 
This Consciousness that is aware 
Of Neighbors and the Sun 
Will be the one aware of Death 
And that itself alone 
Is traversing the interval 
Experience between 
And most profound experiment 
Appointed unto Men&mdash; 
How adequate unto itself 
Its properties shall be 
Itself unto itself and none 
Shall make discovery. 
Adventure most unto itself 
The Soul condemned to be&mdash; 
Attended by a single Hound 
Its own identity.

These feet that never flagged&mdash; 
This faith that watched for star in vain,
