This Is A Blossom Of The Brain 
 
This is a Blossom of the Brain&mdash; 
A small&mdash;italic Seed 
Lodged by Design or Happening 
The Spirit fructified&mdash; 
Shy as the Wind of his Chambers 
Swift as a Freshet's Tongue 
So of the Flower of the Soul 
Its process is unknown. 
When it is found, a few rejoice 
The Wise convey it Home 
Carefully cherishing the spot 
If other Flower become. 
When it is lost, that Day shall be 
The Funeral of God, 
Upon his Breast, a closing Soul 
The Flower of our Lord. 
This Is My Letter To The World, 
This is my letter to the world, 
That never wrote to me,
The simple news that Nature told, 
With tender majesty 
Her message is committed 
To hands I cannot see; 
For love of her, sweet countrymen, 
Judge tenderly of me! 
This Is The Land The Sunset Washes, 
This is the land the sunset washes, 
These are the banks of the Yellow Sea; 
Where it rose, or whither it rushes, 
These are the western mystery! 
Night after night her purple traffic 
Strews the landing with opal bales; 
Merchantmen poise upon horizons, 
Dip, and vanish with fairy sails.

This quiet dust was gentlemen and ladies

Where bloom and bees 
Fulfilled their oriental circuit, 
Then ceased like these.

This was in the White of the Year&mdash;

This World Is Not Conclusion 
 
This World is not Conclusion. 
A Species stands beyond&mdash; 
Invisible, as Music&mdash; 
But positive, as Sound&mdash; 
It beckons, and it baffles&mdash; 
Philosophy&mdash;don't know&mdash; 
And through a Riddle, at the last&mdash; 
Sagacity, must go&mdash; 
To guess it, puzzles scholars&mdash; 
To gain it, Men have borne 
Contempt of Generations 
And Crucifixion, shown&mdash; 
Faith slips&mdash;and laughs, and rallies&mdash; 
Blushes, if any see&mdash; 
Plucks at a twig of Evidence&mdash; 
And asks a Vane, the way&mdash; 
Much Gesture, from the Pulpit&mdash; 
Strong Hallelujahs roll&mdash; 
Narcotics cannot still the Tooth 
That nibbles at the soul&mdash;

These&mdash;are the Western Mystery!

Her purple traffic 
Strews the landing with Opal Bales&mdash; 
Merchantmen&mdash;poise upon Horizons&mdash; 
Dip&mdash;and vanish like Orioles! 
Tho' I Get Home How Late—how Late 
 
Tho' I get home how late—how late— 
So I get home - 'twill compensate— 
Better will be the Ecstasy 
That they have done expecting me— 
When Night—descending—dumb—and dark— 
They hear my unexpected knock— 
Transporting must the moment be— 
Brewed from decades of Agony! 
To think just how the fire will burn— 
Just how long-cheated eyes will turn— 
To wonder what myself will say, 
And what itself, will say to me— 
Beguiles the Centuries of way! 
Tho' My Destiny Be Fustian 
 
Tho' my destiny be Fustian&mdash; 
Hers be damask fine&mdash; 
Tho' she wear a silver apron&mdash; 
I, a less divine&mdash; 
Still, my little Gypsy being 
I would far prefer, 
Still, my little sunburnt bosom 
To her Rosier, 
For, when Frosts, their punctual fingers 
On her forehead lay, 
You and I, and Dr. Holland, 
Bloom Eternally! 
Roses of a steadfast summer 
In a steadfast land, 
Where no Autumn lifts her pencil&mdash; 
And no Reapers stand! 
Those Fair—fictitious People 
 
Those fair—fictitious People— 
The Women—plucked away 
From our familiar Lifetime— 
The Men of Ivory— 
Those Boys and Girls, in Canvas— 
Who stay upon the Wall 
In Everlasting Keepsake— 
Can Anybody tell? 
We trust—in places perfecter— 
Inheriting Delight 
Beyond our faint Conjecture— 
Our dizzy Estimate— 
Remembering ourselves, we trust— 
Yet Blesseder—than We— 
Through Knowing—where We only hope— 
Receiving—where we—pray— 
Of Expectation—also— 
Anticipating us 
With transport, that would be a pain 
Except for Holiness— 
Esteeming us—as Exile— 
Themself—admitted Home— 
Through easy Miracle of Death— 
The Way ourself, must come— 
Those Who Have Been In The Grave The Longest 
 
Those who have been in the Grave the longest&mdash; 
Those who begin Today&mdash; 
Equally perish from our Practise&mdash; 
Death is the other way&mdash; 
Foot of the Bold did least attempt it&mdash; 
It&mdash;is the White Exploit&mdash; 
Once to achieve, annuls the power 
Once to communicate&mdash; 
Three Times—we Parted—breath—and I 
 
Three times—we parted—Breath—and I— 
Three times—He would not go— 
But strove to stir the lifeless Fan 
The Waters—strove to stay. 
Three Times—the Billows tossed me up— 
Then caught me—like a Ball— 
Then made Blue faces in my face— 
And pushed away a sail 
That crawled Leagues off—I liked to see— 
For thinking—while I die— 
How pleasant to behold a Thing 
Where Human faces—be— 
The Waves grew sleepy—Breath—did not— 
The Winds—like Children—lulled— 
Then Sunrise kissed my Chrysalis— 
And I stood up—and lived— 
Through Lane It Lay—through Bramble 
 
Through lane it lay—through bramble— 
Through clearing and through wood— 
Banditti often passed us 
Upon the lonely road. 
The wolf came peering curious— 
The owl looked puzzled down— 
The serpent's satin figure 
Glid stealthily along— 
The tempests touched our garments— 
The lightning's poinards gleamed— 
Fierce from the Crag above us 
The hungry Vulture screamed— 
The satyr's fingers beckoned— 
The valley murmured "Come"— 
These were the mates— 
This was the road 
Those children fluttered home. 
Through The Dark Sod—as Education 
Through the Dark Sod—as Education— 
The Lily passes sure— 
Feels her white foot—no trepidation— 
Her faith—no fear— 
Afterward—in the Meadow— 
Swinging her Beryl Bell— 
The Mold-life—all forgotten—now— 
In Ecstasy—and Dell— 
Through The Strait Pass Of Suffering 
 
Through the strait pass of suffering&mdash; 
The Martyrs&mdash;even&mdash;trod. 
Their feet&mdash;upon Temptations&mdash; 
Their faces&mdash;upon God&mdash; 
A stately&mdash;shriven&mdash;Company&mdash; 
Convulsion&mdash;playing round&mdash; 
Harmless&mdash;as streaks of Meteor&mdash; 
Upon a Planet's Bond&mdash; 
Their faith&mdash;the everlasting troth&mdash; 
Their Expectation&mdash;fair&mdash; 
The Needle&mdash;to the North Degree&mdash; 
Wades&mdash;so&mdash;thro' polar Air! 
Tie The Strings To My Life, My Lord, 
Tie the strings to my life, my Lord, 
Then I am ready to go! 
Just a look at the horses -Rapid! 
That will do! 
Put me in on the firmest side, 
So I shall never fall; 
For we must ride to the Judgment, 
And it's partly down hill. 
But never I mind the bridges, 
And never I mind the sea; 
Held fast in everlasting race 
By my own choice and thee. 
Good-by to the life I used to lives, 
And the world I used to know; 
And kiss the hills for me, just once; 
Now I am ready to go! 
Till Death—is Narrow Loving 
 
Till Death—is narrow Loving— 
The scantest Heart extant 
Will hold you till your privilege 
Of Finiteness—be spent— 
But He whose loss procures you 
Such Destitution that 
Your Life too abject for itself 
Thenceforward imitate— 
Until—Resemblance perfect— 
Yourself, for His pursuit 
Delight of Nature—abdicate— 
Exhibit Love—somewhat— 
Time Feels So Vast That Were It Not 
 
Time feels so vast that were it not 
For an Eternity&mdash; 
I fear me this Circumference 
Engross my Finity&mdash; 
To His exclusion, who prepare 
By Processes of Size 
For the Stupendous Vision 
Of his diameters&mdash; 
'Tis Anguish Grander Than Delight 
 
'Tis Anguish grander than Delight 
'Tis Resurrection Pain&mdash; 
The meeting Bands of smitten Face 
We questioned to, again. 
'Tis Transport wild as thrills the Graves 
When Cerements let go 
And Creatures clad in Miracle 
Go up by Two and Two. 
'Tis Customary As We Part 
 
'Tis customary as we part 
A trinket&mdash;to confer&mdash; 
It helps to stimulate the faith 
When Lovers be afar&mdash; 
'Tis various&mdash;as the various taste&mdash; 
Clematis&mdash;journeying far&mdash; 
Presents me with a single Curl 
Of her Electric Hair&mdash; 
'Tis Good&Mdash;The Looking Back On Grief 
 
'Tis good&mdash;the looking back on Grief&mdash; 
To re-endure a Day&mdash; 
We thought the Mighty Funeral&mdash; 
Of All Conceived Joy&mdash; 
To recollect how Busy Grass 
Did meddle&mdash;one by one&mdash; 
Till all the Grief with Summer&mdash;waved 
And none could see the stone. 
And though the Woe you have Today 
Be larger&mdash;As the Sea 
Exceeds its Unremembered Drop&mdash; 
They're Water&mdash;equally&mdash; 
'Tis Little I—could Care For Pearls 
 
'Tis little I—could care for Pearls— 
Who own the ample sea— 
Or Brooches—when the Emperor— 
With Rubies—pelteth me— 
Or Gold—who am the Prince of Mines— 
Or Diamonds—when have I 
A Diadem to fit a Dom— 
Continual upon me— 
'Tis Not That Dying Hurts Us So 
 
'Tis not that Dying hurts us so&mdash; 
'Tis Living&mdash;hurts us more&mdash; 
But Dying&mdash;is a different way&mdash; 
A Kind behind the Door&mdash; 
The Southern Custom&mdash;of the Bird&mdash; 
That ere the Frosts are due&mdash; 
Accepts a better Latitude&mdash; 
We&mdash;are the Birds&mdash;that stay. 
The Shrivers round Farmers' doors&mdash; 
For whose reluctant Crumb&mdash; 
We stipulate&mdash;till pitying Snows 
Persuade our Feathers Home. 
'Tis One By One — The Father Counts 
 
'Tis One by One — the Father counts — 
And then a Tract between 
Set Cypherless — to teach the Eye 
The Value of its Ten — 
Until the peevish Student 
Acquire the Quick of Skill — 
Then Numerals are dowered back — 
Adorning all the Rule — 
'Tis mostly Slate and Pencil — 
And Darkness on the School 
Distracts the Children's fingers — 
Still the Eternal Rule 
Regards least Cypherer alike 
With Leader of the Band — 
And every separate Urchin's Sum — 
Is fashioned for his hand —

'Tis Opposites&mdash;entice&mdash; 
Deformed Men&mdash;ponder Grace&mdash;

The Lost&mdash;Day's face&mdash; 
The Blind&mdash;esteem it be

For deeming&mdash;Beggars&mdash;play&mdash; 
To lack&mdash;enamor Thee&mdash; 
Tho' the Divinity&mdash;

'Tis So Appalling&Mdash;It Exhilarates 
 
'Tis so appalling&mdash;it exhilarates&mdash; 
So over Horror, it half Captivates&mdash; 
The Soul stares after it, secure&mdash; 
A Sepulchre, fears frost, no more&mdash; 
To scan a Ghost, is faint&mdash; 
But grappling, conquers it&mdash; 
How easy, Torment, now&mdash; 
Suspense kept sawing so&mdash; 
The Truth, is Bald, and Cold&mdash; 
But that will hold&mdash; 
If any are not sure&mdash; 
We show them&mdash;prayer&mdash; 
But we, who know, 
Stop hoping, now&mdash; 
Looking at Death, is Dying&mdash; 
Just let go the Breath&mdash; 
And not the pillow at your Cheek 
So Slumbereth&mdash; 
Others, Can wrestle&mdash; 
Yours, is done&mdash; 
And so of Woe, bleak dreaded&mdash;come, 
It sets the Fright at liberty&mdash; 
And Terror's free&mdash; 
Gay, Ghastly, Holiday! 
'Tis So Much Joy! 
 
'Tis so much joy! 'Tis so much joy! 
If I should fail, what poverty! 
And yet, as poor as I, 
Have ventured all upon a throw! 
Have gained! Yes! Hesitated so— 
This side the Victory! 
Life is but Life! And Death, but Death! 
Bliss is, but Bliss, and Breath but Breath! 
And if indeed I fail, 
At least, to know the worst, is sweet! 
Defeat means nothing but Defeat, 
No drearier, can befall! 
And if I gain! Oh Gun at Sea! 
Oh Bells, that in the Steeples be! 
At first, repeat it slow! 
For Heaven is a different thing, 
Conjectured, and waked sudden in— 
And might extinguish me!

To Hear An Oriole Sing 
 
To hear an Oriole sing 
May be a common thing&mdash; 
Or only a divine. 
It is not of the Bird 
Who sings the same, unheard, 
As unto Crowd&mdash; 
The Fashion of the Ear 
Attireth that it hear 
In Dun, or fair&mdash; 
So whether it be Rune, 
Or whether it be none 
Is of within. 
The "Tune is in the Tree&mdash;" 
The Skeptic&mdash;showeth me&mdash; 
"No Sir! In Thee!"

To interrupt His Yellow Plan 
The Sun does not allow

Such a Day—

What last 
What One broke off with 
At the Drowsiest—

Might He know 
How Conscious Consciousness—could grow— 
Till Love that was—and Love too best to be— 
Meet—and the Junction be Eternity

To learn the Transport by the Pain

This&mdash;the signal woe!

Ascend in ceaseless Carol&mdash; 
Inaudible, indeed, 
To us&mdash;the duller scholars

Train 
I like to see it lap the miles, 
And lick the valleys up, 
And stop to feed itself at tanks; 
And then, prodigious, step 
Around a pile of mountains, 
And, supercilious, peer 
In shanties by the sides of roads; 
And then a quarry pare 
To fit its sides, and crawl between, 
Complaining all the while 
In horrid, hooting stanza; 
Then chase itself down the hill 
And neigh like Boanerges; 
Then, punctual as a star, 
Stop - docile and omnipotent At 
its own stable door.

Twas Crisis—all The Length Had Passed 
'Twas Crisis—All the length had passed— 
That dull—benumbing time 
There is in Fever or Event— 
And now the Chance had come— 
The instant holding in its claw 
The privilege to live 
Or warrant to report the Soul 
The other side the Grave. 
The Muscles grappled as with leads 
That would not let the Will— 
The Spirit shook the Adamant— 
But could not make it feel. 
The Second poised—debated—shot— 
Another had begun— 
And simultaneously, a Soul 
Escaped the House unseen— 
'Twas Just This Time, Last Year, I Died 
 
'Twas just this time, last year, I died. 
I know I heard the Corn, 
When I was carried by the Farms&mdash; 
It had the Tassels on&mdash; 
I thought how yellow it would look&mdash; 
When Richard went to mill&mdash; 
And then, I wanted to get out, 
But something held my will. 
I thought just how Red&mdash;Apples wedged 
The Stubble's joints between&mdash; 
And the Carts stooping round the fields 
To take the Pumpkins in&mdash; 
I wondered which would miss me, least, 
And when Thanksgiving, came, 
If Father'd multiply the plates&mdash; 
To make an even Sum&mdash; 
And would it blur the Christmas glee 
My Stocking hang too high 
For any Santa Claus to reach 
The Altitude of me&mdash; 
But this sort, grieved myself, 
And so, I thought the other way, 
How just this time, some perfect year&mdash; 
Themself, should come to me&mdash; 
'Twas Like A Maelstrom, With A Notch 
 
'Twas like a Maelstrom, with a notch, 
That nearer, every Day, 
Kept narrowing its boiling Wheel 
Until the Agony 
Toyed coolly with the final inch 
Of your delirious Hem&mdash; 
And you dropt, lost, 
When something broke&mdash; 
And let you from a Dream&mdash; 
As if a Goblin with a Gauge&mdash; 
Kept measuring the Hours&mdash; 
Until you felt your Second 
Weigh, helpless, in his Paws&mdash; 
And not a Sinew&mdash;stirred&mdash;could help, 
And sense was setting numb&mdash; 
When God&mdash;remembered&mdash;and the Fiend 
Let go, then, Overcome&mdash; 
As if your Sentence stood&mdash;pronounced&mdash; 
And you were frozen led 
From Dungeon's luxury of Doubt 
To Gibbets, and the Dead&mdash; 
And when the Film had stitched your eyes 
A Creature gasped "Reprieve"! 
Which Anguish was the utterest&mdash;then&mdash; 
To perish, or to live? 
'Twas Love—not Me 
 
'Twas Love—not me— 
Oh punish—pray— 
The Real one died for Thee— 
Just Him—not me— 
Such Guilt—to love Thee—most! 
Doom it beyond the Rest— 
Forgive it—last— 
'Twas base as Jesus—most! 
Let Justice not mistake— 
We Two—looked so alike— 
Which was the Guilty Sake— 
'Twas Love's—Now Strike! 
Twas Such A Little—little Boat 
 
'Twas such a little—little boat 
That toddled down the bay! 
'Twas such a gallant—gallant sea 
That beckoned it away! 
'Twas such a greedy, greedy wave 
That licked it from the Coast— 
Nor ever guessed the stately sails 
My little craft was lost! 
'Twas The Old—road—through Pain 
 
'Twas the old—road—through pain— 
That unfrequented—one— 
With many a turn—and thorn— 
That stops—at Heaven— 
This—was the Town—she passed— 
There—where she—rested—last— 
Then—stepped more fast— 
The little tracks—close prest— 
Then—not so swift— 
Slow—slow—as feet did weary—grow— 
Then—stopped—no other track! 
Wait! Look! Her little Book— 
The leaf—at love—turned back— 
Her very Hat— 
And this worn shoe just fits the track— 
Herself—though—fled! 
Another bed—a short one— 
Women make—tonight— 
In Chambers bright— 
Too out of sight—though— 
For our hoarse Good Night— 
To touch her Head! 
'Twas Warm—at First—like Us 
 
'Twas warm—at first—like Us— 
Until there crept upon 
A Chill—like frost upon a Glass— 
Till all the scene—be gone. 
The Forehead copied Stone— 
The Fingers grew too cold 
To ache—and like a Skater's Brook— 
The busy eyes—congealed— 
It straightened—that was all— 
It crowded Cold to Cold— 
It multiplied indifference— 
As Pride were all it could— 
And even when with Cords— 
'Twas lowered, like a Weight— 
It made no Signal, nor demurred, 
But dropped like Adamant. 
Twice Had Summer Her Fair Verdure 
 
Twice had Summer her fair Verdure 
Proffered to the Plain&mdash; 
Twice a Winter's silver Fracture 
On the Rivers been&mdash; 
Two full Autumns for the Squirrel 
Bounteous prepared&mdash; 
Nature, Had'st thou not a Berry 
For thy wandering Bird? 
Two Butterflies Went Out At Noon 
Two butterflies went out at noon 
And waltzed above a stream, 
Then stepped straight through the firmament 
And rested on a beam; 
And then together bore away 
Upon a shining sea,-Though 
never yet, in any port 
Their coming mentioned be. 
If spoken by the distant bird, 
If met in ether sea 
By frigate or by merchantman, 
Report was not to me. 
Two Swimmers Wrestled On The Spar 
 
Two swimmers wrestled on the spar&mdash; 
Until the morning sun&mdash; 
When One&mdash;turned smiling to the land&mdash; 
Oh God! the Other One! 
The stray ships&mdash;passing&mdash; 
Spied a face&mdash; 
Upon the waters borne&mdash; 
With eyes in death&mdash;still begging raised&mdash; 
And hands&mdash;beseeching&mdash;thrown! 
Two Travellers Perishing In Snow 
 
Two Travellers perishing in Snow 
The Forests as they froze 
Together heard them strengthening 
Each other with the words 
That Heaven if Heaven&mdash;must contain 
What Either left behind 
And then the cheer too solemn grew 
For language, and the wind 
Long steps across the features took 
That Love had touched the Morn 
With reverential Hyacinth&mdash; 
The taleless Days went on 
Till Mystery impatient drew 
And those They left behind 
Led absent, were procured of Heaven 
As Those first furnished, said&mdash; 
'Twould Ease—a Butterfly 
 
'Twould ease—a Butterfly— 
Elate—a Bee— 
Thou'rt neither— 
Neither—thy capacity— 
But, Blossom, were I, 
I would rather be 
Thy moment 
Than a Bee's Eternity— 
Content of fading 
Is enough for me— 
Fade I unto Divinity— 
And Dying—Lifetime— 
Ample as the Eye— 
Her least attention raise on me— 
Two—were Immortal Twice 
 
Two—were immortal twice— 
The privilege of few— 
Eternity—obtained—in Time— 
Reversed Divinity— 
That our ignoble Eyes 
The quality conceive 
Of Paradise superlative— 
Through their Comparative. 
Unable Are The Loved To Die 
 
Unable are the Loved to die 
For Love is Immortality, 
Nay, it is Deity&mdash; 
Unable they that love&mdash;to die 
For Love reforms Vitality 
Into Divinity. 
Uncertain Lease—develops Lustre 
 
Uncertain lease—develops lustre 
On Time 
Uncertain Grasp, appreciation 
Of Sum— 
The shorter Fate—is oftener the chiefest 
Because 
Inheritors upon a tenure 
Prize— 
Under The Light, Yet Under 
 
Under the Light, yet under, 
Under the Grass and the Dirt, 
Under the Beetle's Cellar 
Under the Clover's Root, 
Further than Arm could stretch 
Were it Giant long, 
Further than Sunshine could 
Were the Day Year long, 
Over the Light, yet over, 
Over the Arc of the Bird&mdash; 
Over the Comet's chimney&mdash; 
Over the Cubit's Head, 
Further than Guess can gallop 
Further than Riddle ride&mdash; 
Oh for a Disc to the Distance 
Between Ourselves and the Dead! 
Undue Significance A Starving Man Attaches 
 
Undue Significance a starving man attaches 
To Food&mdash; 
Far off&mdash;He sighs&mdash;and therefore&mdash;Hopeless&mdash; 
And therefore&mdash;Good&mdash; 
Partaken&mdash;it relieves&mdash;indeed&mdash; 
But proves us 
That Spices fly 
In the Receipt&mdash;It was the Distance&mdash; 
Was Savory&mdash; 
Unfulfilled To Observation 
 
Unfulfilled to Observation&mdash; 
Incomplete&mdash;to Eye&mdash; 
But to Faith&mdash;a Revolution 
In Locality&mdash; 
Unto Us&mdash;the Suns extinguish&mdash; 
To our Opposite&mdash; 
New Horizons&mdash;they embellish&mdash; 
Fronting Us&mdash;with Night. 
Unit, Like Death, For Whom? 
 
Unit, like Death, for Whom? 
True, like the Tomb, 
Who tells no secret 
Told to Him&mdash; 
The Grave is strict&mdash; 
Tickets admit 
Just two&mdash;the Bearer&mdash; 
And the Borne&mdash; 
And seat&mdash;just One&mdash; 
The Living&mdash;tell&mdash; 
The Dying&mdash;but a Syllable&mdash; 
The Coy Dead&mdash;None&mdash; 
No Chatter&mdash;here&mdash;no tea&mdash; 
So Babbler, and Bohea&mdash;stay there&mdash; 
But Gravity&mdash;and Expectation&mdash;and Fear&mdash; 
A tremor just, that All's not sure. 
Unto Like Story—trouble Has Enticed Me 
 
Unto like Story—Trouble has enticed me— 
How Kinsmen fell— 
Brothers and Sister—who preferred the Glory— 
And their young will 
Bent to the Scaffold, or in Dungeons—chanted— 
Till God's full time— 
When they let go the ignominy—smiling— 
And Shame went still— 
Unto guessed Crests, my moaning fancy, leads me, 
Worn fair 
By Heads rejected—in the lower country— 
Of honors there— 
Such spirit makes her perpetual mention, 
That I—grown bold— 
Step martial—at my Crucifixion— 
As Trumpets—rolled— 
Feet, small as mine—have marched in Revolution 
Firm to the Drum— 
Hands—not so stout—hoisted them—in witness— 
When Speech went numb— 
Let me not shame their sublime deportments— 
Drilled bright— 
Beckoning—Etruscan invitation— 
Toward Light— 
Unto Me? I Do Not Know You— 
"Unto Me?" I do not know you— 
Where may be your House? 
"I am Jesus—Late of Judea— 
Now—of Paradise"— 
Wagons—have you—to convey me? 
This is far from Thence— 
"Arms of Mine—sufficient Phaeton— 
Trust Omnipotence"— 
I am spotted—"I am Pardon"— 
I am small—"The Least 
Is esteemed in Heaven the Chiefest— 
Occupy my House"— 
Unto My Books—so Good To Turn 
 
Unto my Books—so good to turn— 
Far ends of tired Days— 
It half endears the Abstinence— 
And Pain—is missed—in Praise— 
As Flavors—cheer Retarded Guests 
With Banquettings to be— 
So Spices—stimulate the time 
Till my small Library— 
It may be Wilderness—without— 
Far feet of failing Men— 
But Holiday—excludes the night— 
And it is Bells—within— 
I thank these Kinsmen of the Shelf— 
Their Countenances Kid 
Enamor—in Prospective— 
And satisfy—obtained— 
Upon Concluded Lives 
 
Upon Concluded Lives 
There's nothing cooler falls&mdash; 
Than Life's sweet Calculations&mdash; 
The mixing Bells and Palls&mdash; 
Make Lacerating Tune&mdash; 
To Ears the Dying Side&mdash; 
'Tis Coronal&mdash;and Funeral&mdash; 
Saluting&mdash;in the Road&mdash; 
Victory Comes Late 
 
Victory comes late&mdash; 
And is held low to freezing lips&mdash; 
Too rapt with frost 
To take it&mdash; 
How sweet it would have tasted&mdash; 
Just a Drop&mdash; 
Was God so economical? 
His Table's spread too high for Us&mdash; 
Unless We dine on tiptoe&mdash; 
Crumbs&mdash;fit such little mouths&mdash; 
Cherries&mdash;suit Robbins&mdash; 
The Eagle's Golden Breakfast strangles&mdash;Them&mdash; 
God keep His Oath to Sparrows&mdash; 
Who of little Love&mdash;know how to starve&mdash; 
Volcanoes be in Sicily 
Volcanoes be in Sicily 
And South America 
I judge from my Geography -
Volcanos nearer here 
A Lava step at any time 
Am I inclined to climb A 
Crater I may contemplate 
Vesuvius at Home. 
Wait Till The Majesty Of Death 
 
Wait till the Majesty of Death 
Invests so mean a brow! 
Almost a powdered Footman 
Might dare to touch it now! 
Wait till in Everlasting Robes 
That Democrat is dressed, 
Then prate about "Preferment"&mdash; 
And "Station," and the rest! 
Around this quiet Courtier 
Obsequious Angels wait! 
Full royal is his Retinue! 
Full purple is his state! 
A Lord, might dare to lift the Hat 
To such a Modest Clay 
Since that My Lord, "the Lord of Lords" 
Receives unblushingly! 
Warm in her Hand these accents lie 
Warm in her Hand these accents lie 
While faithful and afar 
The Grace so awkward for her sake 
Its fond subjection wear 
Water Makes Many Beds 
Water makes many Beds 
For those averse to sleep Its 
awful chamber open stands Its 
Curtains blandly sweep Abhorrent 
is the Rest 
In undulating Rooms 
Whose Amplitude no end invades Whose 
Axis never comes. 
Water, Is Taught By Thirst 
 
Water, is taught by thirst. 
Land&mdash;by the Oceans passed. 
Transport&mdash;by throe&mdash; 
Peace&mdash;by its battles told&mdash; 
Love, by Memorial Mold&mdash; 
Birds, by the Snow. 
We Can But Follow To The Sun 
 
We can but follow to the Sun&mdash; 
As oft as He go down 
He leave Ourselves a Sphere behind&mdash; 
'Tis mostly&mdash;following&mdash; 
We go no further with the Dust 
Than to the Earthen Door&mdash; 
And then the Panels are reversed&mdash; 
And we behold&mdash;no more. 
We Cover Thee—sweet Face 
 
We Cover Thee—Sweet Face— 
Not that We tire of Thee— 
But that Thyself fatigue of Us— 
Remember—as Thou go— 
We follow Thee until 
Thou notice Us—no more— 
And then—reluctant—turn away 
To Con Thee o'er and o'er— 
And blame the scanty love 
We were Content to show— 
Augmented—Sweet—a Hundred fold— 
If Thou would'st take it—now— 
We Do Not Play On Graves 
 
We do not play on Graves&mdash; 
Because there isn't Room&mdash; 
Besides&mdash;it isn't even&mdash;it slants 
And People come&mdash; 
And put a Flower on it&mdash; 
And hang their faces so&mdash; 
We're fearing that their Hearts will drop&mdash; 
And crush our pretty play&mdash; 
And so we move as far 
As Enemies&mdash;away&mdash; 
Just looking round to see how far 
It is&mdash;Occasionally&mdash; 
We Don'T Cry—tim And I 
 
We don't cry—Tim and I, 
We are far too grand— 
But we bolt the door tight 
To prevent a friend— 
Then we hide our brave face 
Deep in our hand— 
Not to cry—Tim and I— 
We are far too grand— 
Nor to dream—he and me— 
Do we condescend— 
We just shut our brown eye 
To see to the end— 
Tim—see Cottages— 
But, Oh, so high! 
Then—we shake—Tim and I— 
And lest I—cry— 
Tim—reads a little Hymn— 
And we both pray— 
Please, Sir, I and Tim— 
Always lost the way! 
We must die—by and by— 
Clergymen say— 
Tim—shall—if I—do— 
I—too—if he— 
How shall we arrange it— 
Tim—was—so—shy? 
Take us simultaneous—Lord— 
I—"Tim"—and Me! 
We Dream—it Is Good We Are Dreaming 
 
We dream—it is good we are dreaming— 
It would hurt us—were we awake— 
But since it is playing—kill us, 
And we are playing—shriek— 
What harm? Men die—externally— 
It is a truth—of Blood— 
But we—are dying in Drama— 
And Drama—is never dead— 
Cautious—We jar each other— 
And either—open the eyes— 
Lest the Phantasm—prove the Mistake— 
And the livid Surprise 
Cool us to Shafts of Granite— 
With just an Age—and Name— 
And perhaps a phrase in Egyptian— 
It's prudenter—to dream— 
We Grow Accustomed To The Dark 
We grow accustomed to the Dark When 
light is put away As 
when the Neighbor holds the Lamp 
To witness her Goodbye 
A Moment -We uncertain step 
For newness of the night Then 
-fit our Vision to the Dark And 
meet the Road -erect 
And so of larger -Darknesses Those 
Evenings of the Brain When 
not a Moon disclose a sign Or 
Star -come out -within 
The Bravest -grope a little And 
sometimes hit a Tree 
Directly in the Forehead But 
as they learn to see 
Either the Darkness alters Or 
something in the sight 
Adjusts itself to Midnight And 
Life steps almost straight. 
We Learned The Whole Of Love 
 
We learned the Whole of Love&mdash; 
The Alphabet&mdash;the Words&mdash; 
A Chapter&mdash;then the mighty Book&mdash; 
Then&mdash;Revelation closed&mdash; 
But in Each Other's eyes 
An Ignorance beheld&mdash; 
Diviner than the Childhood's&mdash; 
And each to each, a Child&mdash; 
Attempted to expound 
What Neither&mdash;understood&mdash; 
Alas, that Wisdom is so large&mdash; 
And Truth&mdash;so manifold! 
We Like March, His Shoes Are Purple, 
We like March, his shoes are purple, 
He is new and high; 
Makes he mud for dog and peddler, 
Makes he forest dry; 
Knows the adder's tongue his coming, 
And begets her spot. 
Stands the sun so close and mighty 
That our minds are hot. 
News is he of all the others; 
Bold it were to die 
With the blue-birds buccaneering 
On his British sky. 
We Lose—because We Win 
 
We lose—because we win— 
Gamblers—recollecting which 
Toss their dice again! 
We Met As Sparks—diverging Flints 
 
We met as Sparks—Diverging Flints 
Sent various—scattered ways— 
We parted as the Central Flint 
Were cloven with an Adze— 
Subsisting on the Light We bore 
Before We felt the Dark— 
A Flint unto this Day—perhaps— 
But for that single Spark. 
We Miss Her, Not Because We See 
 
We miss Her, not because We see&mdash; 
The Absence of an Eye&mdash; 
Except its Mind accompany 
Abridge Society 
As slightly as the Routes of Stars&mdash; 
Ourselves&mdash;asleep below&mdash; 
We know that their superior Eyes 
Include Us&mdash;as they go&mdash; 
We Outgrow Love, Like Other Things 
 
We outgrow love, like other things 
And put it in the Drawer&mdash; 
Till it an Antique fashion shows&mdash; 
Like Costumes Grandsires wore. 
We Play At Paste, 
We play at paste, 
Till qualified for pearl, 
Then drop the paste, 
And deem ourself a fool. 
The shapes, though, were similar, 
And our new hands 
Learned gem-tactics 
Practising sands. 
We Pray&Mdash;To Heaven 
 
We pray&mdash;to Heaven&mdash; 
We prate&mdash;of Heaven&mdash; 
Relate&mdash;when Neighbors die&mdash; 
At what o'clock to heaven&mdash;they fled&mdash; 
Who saw them&mdash;Wherefore fly? 
Is Heaven a Place&mdash;a Sky&mdash;a Tree? 
Location's narrow way is for Ourselves&mdash; 
Unto the Dead 
There's no Geography&mdash; 
But State&mdash;Endowal&mdash;Focus&mdash; 
Where&mdash;Omnipresence&mdash;fly? 
We See&Mdash;Comparatively 
 
We see&mdash;Comparatively&mdash; 
The Thing so towering high 
We could not grasp its segment 
Unaided&mdash;Yesterday&mdash; 
This Morning's finer Verdict&mdash; 
Makes scarcely worth the toil&mdash; 
A furrow&mdash;Our Cordillera&mdash; 
Our Apennine&mdash;a Knoll&mdash; 
Perhaps 'tis kindly&mdash;done us&mdash; 
The Anguish&mdash;and the loss&mdash; 
The wrenching&mdash;for His Firmament 
The Thing belonged to us&mdash; 
To spare these Striding Spirits 
Some Morning of Chagrin&mdash; 
The waking in a Gnat's&mdash;embrace&mdash; 
Our Giants&mdash;further on&mdash; 
We Should Not Mind So Small A Flower 
 
We should not mind so small a flower&mdash; 
Except it quiet bring 
Our little garden that we lost 
Back to the Lawn again. 
So spicy her Carnations nod&mdash; 
So drunken, reel her Bees&mdash; 
So silver steal a hundred flutes 
From out a hundred trees&mdash; 
That whoso sees this little flower 
By faith may clear behold 
The Bobolinks around the throne 
And Dandelions gold. 
We Talked As Girls Do 
 
We talked as Girls do&mdash; 
Fond, and late&mdash; 
We speculated fair, on every subject, but the Grave&mdash; 
Of ours, none affair&mdash; 
We handled Destinies, as cool&mdash; 
As we&mdash;Disposers&mdash;be&mdash; 
And God, a Quiet Party 
To our Authority&mdash; 
But fondest, dwelt upon Ourself 
As we eventual&mdash;be&mdash; 
When Girls to Women, softly raised 
We&mdash;occupy&mdash;Degree&mdash; 
We parted with a contract 
To cherish, and to write 
But Heaven made both, impossible 
Before another night. 
We Thirst At First—'Tis Nature's Act 
 
We thirst at first—'tis Nature's Act— 
And later—when we die— 
A little Water supplicate— 
Of fingers going by— 
It intimates the finer want— 
Whose adequate supply 
Is that Great Water in the West— 
Termed Immortality— 
We—bee And I—live By The Quaffing 
 
We—Bee and I—live by the quaffing— 
'Tisn't all Hock—with us— 
Life has its Ale— 
But it's many a lay of the Dim Burgundy— 
We chant—for cheer—when the Wines—fail— 
Do we "get drunk"? 
Ask the jolly Clovers! 
Do we "beat" our "Wife"? 
I—never wed— 
Bee—pledges his—in minute flagons— 
Dainty—as the trees—on our deft Head— 
While runs the Rhine— 
He and I—revel— 
First—at the vat—and latest at the Vine— 
Noon—our last Cup— 
"Found dead"—"of Nectar"— 
By a humming Coroner— 
In a By-Thyme! 
Went Up A Year This Evening! 
 
Went up a year this evening! 
I recollect it well! 
Amid no bells nor bravoes 
The bystanders will tell! 
Cheerful&mdash;as to the village&mdash; 
Tranquil&mdash;as to repose&mdash; 
Chastened&mdash;as to the Chapel 
This humble Tourist rose! 
Did not talk of returning! 
Alluded to no time 
When, were the gales propitious&mdash; 
We might look for him! 
Was grateful for the Roses 
In life's diverse bouquet&mdash; 
Talked softly of new species 
To pick another day; 
Beguiling thus the wonder 
The wondrous nearer drew&mdash; 
Hands bustled at the moorings&mdash; 
The crown respectful grew&mdash; 
Ascended from our vision 
To Countenances new! 
A Difference&mdash;A Daisy&mdash; 
Is all the rest I knew! 
Wert Thou But Ill—that I Might Show Thee 
 
Wert Thou but ill—that I might show thee 
How long a Day I could endure 
Though thine attention stop not on me 
Nor the least signal, Me assure— 
Wert Thou but Stranger in ungracious country— 
And Mine—the Door 
Thou paused at, for a passing bounty— 
No More— 
Accused—wert Thou—and Myself—Tribunal— 
Convicted—Sentenced—Ermine—not to Me 
Half the Condition, thy Reverse—to follow— 
Just to partake—the infamy— 
The Tenant of the Narrow Cottage, wert Thou— 
Permit to be 
The Housewife in thy low attendance 
Contenteth Me— 
No Service hast Thou, I would not achieve it— 
To die—or live— 
The first—Sweet, proved I, ere I saw thee— 
For Life—be Love— 
What Care The Dead, For Chanticleer 
 
What care the Dead, for Chanticleer&mdash; 
What care the Dead for Day? 
'Tis late your Sunrise vex their face&mdash; 
And Purple Ribaldry&mdash;of Morning 
Pour as blank on them 
As on the Tier of Wall 
The Mason builded, yesterday, 
And equally as cool&mdash; 
What care the Dead for Summer? 
The Solstice had no Sun 
Could waste the Snow before their Gate&mdash; 
And knew One Bird a Tune&mdash; 
Could thrill their Mortised Ear 
Of all the Birds that be&mdash; 
This One&mdash;beloved of Mankind 
Henceforward cherished be&mdash; 
What care the Dead for Winter? 
Themselves as easy freeze&mdash; 
June Noon&mdash;as January Night&mdash; 
As soon the South&mdash;her Breeze 
Of Sycamore&mdash;or Cinnamon&mdash; 
Deposit in a Stone 
And put a Stone to keep it Warm&mdash; 
Give Spices&mdash;unto Men&mdash; 
What Did They Do Since I Saw Them? 
 
What did They do since I saw Them? 
Were They industrious? 
So many questions to put Them 
Have I the eagerness 
That could I snatch Their Faces 
That could Their lips reply 
Not till the last was answered 
Should They start for the Sky. 
Not if Their Party were waiting, 
Not if to talk with Me 
Were to Them now, Homesickness 
After Eternity. 
Not if the Just suspect me 
And offer a Reward 
Would I restore my Booty 
To that Bold Person, God&mdash; 
What I See Not, I Better See 
 
What I see not, I better see&mdash; 
Through Faith&mdash;my Hazel Eye 
Has periods of shutting&mdash; 
But, No lid has Memory&mdash; 
For frequent, all my sense obscured 
I equally behold 
As someone held a light unto 
The Features so beloved&mdash;
And I arise&mdash;and in my Dream&mdash; 
Do Thee distinguished Grace&mdash; 
Till jealous Daylight interrupt&mdash; 
And mar thy perfectness&mdash; 
What If I Say I Shall Not Wait! 
 
What if I say I shall not wait! 
What if I burst the fleshly Gate&mdash; 
And pass escaped&mdash;to thee! 
What if I file this Mortal&mdash;off&mdash; 
See where it hurt me&mdash;That's enough&mdash; 
And wade in Liberty! 
They cannot take me&mdash;any more! 
Dungeons can call&mdash;and Guns implore 
Unmeaning&mdash;now&mdash;to me&mdash; 
As laughter&mdash;was&mdash;an hour ago&mdash; 
Or Laces&mdash;or a Travelling Show&mdash; 
Or who died&mdash;yesterday! 
What Inn Is This 
 
What Inn is this 
Where for the night 
Peculiar Traveller comes? 
Who is the Landlord? 
Where the maids? 
Behold, what curious rooms! 
No ruddy fires on the hearth&mdash; 
No brimming Tankards flow&mdash; 
Necromancer! Landlord! 
Who are these below? 
What Is— 
 
What is—"Paradise"— 
Who live there— 
Are they "Farmers"— 
Do they "hoe"— 
Do they know that this is "Amherst"— 
And that I—am coming—too— 
Do they wear "new shoes"—in "Eden"— 
Is it always pleasant—there— 
Won't they scold us—when we're homesick— 
Or tell God—how cross we are— 
You are sure there's such a person 
As "a Father"—in the sky— 
So if I get lost—there—ever— 
Or do what the Nurse calls "die"— 
I shan't walk the "Jasper"—barefoot— 
Ransomed folks—won't laugh at me— 
Maybe—"Eden" a'n't so lonesome 
As New England used to be! 
What Shall I Do When The Summer Troubles 
 
What shall I do when the Summer troubles&mdash; 
What, when the Rose is ripe&mdash; 
What when the Eggs fly off in Music 
From the Maple Keep? 
What shall I do when the Skies a'chirrup 
Drop a Tune on me&mdash; 
When the Bee hangs all Noon in the Buttercup 
What will become of me? 
Oh, when the Squirrel fills His Pockets 
And the Berries stare 
How can I bear their jocund Faces 
Thou from Here, so far? 
'Twouldn't afflict a Robin&mdash; 
All His Goods have Wings&mdash; 
I&mdash;do not fly, so wherefore 
My Perennial Things? 
What Shall I Do—it Whimpers So 
 
What shall I do—it whimpers so— 
This little Hound within the Heart 
All day and night with bark and start— 
And yet, it will not go— 
Would you untie it, were you me— 
Would it stop whining—if to Thee— 
I sent it—even now? 
It should not tease you— 
By your chair—or, on the mat— 
Or if it dare—to climb your dizzy knee— 
Or—sometimes at your side to run— 
When you were willing— 
Shall it come? 
Tell Carlo— 
He'll tell me! 
What Soft—cherubic Creatures 
 
What Soft—Cherubic Creatures— 
These Gentlewomen are— 
One would as soon assault a Plush— 
Or violate a Star— 
Such Dimity Convictions— 
A Horror so refined 
Of freckled Human Nature— 
Of Deity—ashamed— 
It's such a common—Glory— 
A Fisherman's—Degree— 
Redemption—Brittle Lady— 
Be so—ashamed of Thee— 
What Would I Give To See His Face? 
 
What would I give to see his face? 
I'd give&mdash;I'd give my life&mdash;of course&mdash; 
But that is not enough! 
Stop just a minute&mdash;let me think! 
I'd give my biggest Bobolink! 
That makes two&mdash;Him&mdash;and Life! 
You know who "June" is&mdash; 
I'd give her&mdash; 
Roses a day from Zanzibar&mdash; 
And Lily tubes&mdash;like Wells&mdash; 
Bees&mdash;by the furlong&mdash; 
Straits of Blue 
Navies of Butterflies&mdash;sailed thro'&mdash; 
And dappled Cowslip Dells&mdash; 
Then I have "shares" in Primrose "Banks"&mdash; 
Daffodil Dowries&mdash;spicy "Stocks"&mdash; 
Dominions&mdash;broad as Dew&mdash; 
Bags of Doublons&mdash;adventurous Bees 
Brought me&mdash;from firmamental seas&mdash; 
And Purple&mdash;from Peru&mdash; 
Now&mdash;have I bought it&mdash; 
"Shylock"? Say! 
Sign me the Bond! 
"I vow to pay 
To Her&mdash;who pledges this&mdash; 
One hour&mdash;of her Sovereign's face"! 
Ecstatic Contract! 
Niggard Grace! 
My Kingdom's worth of Bliss!

When I Have Seen The Sun Emerge 
 
When I have seen the Sun emerge 
From His amazing House&mdash;

A Deed, in every place&mdash; 
Without the incident of Fame 
Or accident of Noise&mdash; 
The Earth has seemed to me a Drum,

When I Hoped, I Recollect 
 
When I hoped, I recollect 
Just the place I stood&mdash; 
At a Window facing West&mdash; 
Roughest Air&mdash;was good&mdash; 
Not a Sleet could bite me&mdash; 
Not a frost could cool&mdash; 
Hope it was that kept me warm&mdash; 
Not Merino shawl&mdash; 
When I feared&mdash;I recollect 
Just the Day it was&mdash; 
Worlds were lying out to Sun&mdash; 
Yet how Nature froze&mdash; 
Icicles upon my soul 
Prickled Blue and Cool&mdash; 
Bird went praising everywhere&mdash; 
Only Me&mdash;was still&mdash; 
And the Day that I despaired&mdash; 
This&mdash;if I forget 
Nature will&mdash;that it be Night 
After Sun has set&mdash; 
Darkness intersect her face&mdash; 
And put out her eye&mdash; 
Nature hesitate&mdash;before 
Memory and I&mdash; 
When I Was Small, A Woman Died 
 
When I was small, a Woman died&mdash; 
Today&mdash;her Only Boy 
Went up from the Potomac&mdash; 
His face all Victory 
To look at her&mdash;How slowly 
The Seasons must have turned 
Till Bullets clipt an Angle 
And He passed quickly round&mdash; 
If pride shall be in Paradise&mdash; 
Ourself cannot decide&mdash; 
Of their imperial Conduct&mdash; 
No person testified&mdash; 
But, proud in Apparition&mdash; 
That Woman and her Boy 
Pass back and forth, before my Brain 
As even in the sky&mdash; 
I'm confident that Bravoes&mdash; 
Perpetual break abroad 
For Braveries, remote as this 
In Scarlet Maryland&mdash;

When Roses cease to bloom, Sir,

When We Stand On The Tops Of Things 
 
When we stand on the tops of Things&mdash; 
And like the Trees, look down&mdash; 
The smoke all cleared away from it&mdash; 
And Mirrors on the scene&mdash; 
Just laying light&mdash;no soul will wink 
Except it have the flaw&mdash; 
The Sound ones, like the Hills&mdash;shall stand&mdash; 
No Lighting, scares away&mdash; 
The Perfect, nowhere be afraid&mdash; 
They bear their dauntless Heads, 
Where others, dare not go at Noon, 
Protected by their deeds&mdash;

Upon a spotted World&mdash; 
And Suns, go surer, for their Proof, 
As if an Axle, held&mdash;

Where bells no more affright the morn&mdash;

Where I Have Lost, I Softer Tread 
 
Where I have lost, I softer tread&mdash; 
I sow sweet flower from garden bed&mdash; 
I pause above that vanished head
 And mourn. 
Whom I have lost, I pious guard 
From accent harsh, or ruthless word&mdash; 
Feeling as if their pillow heard,
 Though stone! 
When I have lost, you'll know by this&mdash; 
A Bonnet black&mdash;A dusk surplice&mdash; 
A little tremor in my voice
 Like this! 
Why, I have lost, the people know 
Who dressed in flocks of purest snow 
Went home a century ago
 Next Bliss!

Who Occupies This House? 
 
Who occupies this House? 
A Stranger I must judge 
Since No one know His Circumstance&mdash; 
'Tis well the name and age 
Are writ upon the Door 
Or I should fear to pause 
Where not so much as Honest Dog 
Approach encourages. 
It seems a curious Town&mdash; 
Some Houses very old, 
Some&mdash;newly raised this Afternoon, 
Were I compelled to build 
It should not be among 
Inhabitants so still 
But where the Birds assemble 
And Boys were possible. 
Before Myself was born 
'Twas settled, so they say, 
A Territory for the Ghosts&mdash; 
And Squirrels, formerly. 
Until a Pioneer, as 
Settlers often do 
Liking the quiet of the Place 
Attracted more unto&mdash; 
And from a Settlement 
A Capital has grown 
Distinguished for the gravity 
Of every Citizen. 
The Owner of this House 
A Stranger He must be&mdash; 
Eternity's Acquaintances 
Are mostly so&mdash;to me.

Whose Are The Little Beds, I Asked 
 
Whose are the little beds, I asked 
Which in the valleys lie? 
Some shook their heads, and others smiled&mdash; 
And no one made reply. 
Perhaps they did not hear, I said, 
I will inquire again&mdash; 
Whose are the beds&mdash;the tiny beds 
So thick upon the plain? 
'Tis Daisy, in the shortest&mdash; 
A little further on&mdash; 
Nearest the door&mdash;to wake the Ist&mdash; 
Little Leontoden. 
'Tis Iris, Sir, and Aster&mdash; 
Anemone, and Bell&mdash; 
Bartsia, in the blanket red&mdash; 
And chubby Daffodil. 
Meanwhile, at many cradles 
Her busy foot she plied&mdash; 
Humming the quaintest lullaby 
That ever rocked a child. 
Hush! Epigea wakens! 
The Crocus stirs her lids&mdash; 
Rhodora's cheek is crimson, 
She's dreaming of the woods! 
Then turning from them reverent&mdash; 
Their bedtime 'tis, she said&mdash; 
The Bumble bees will wake them 
When April woods are red.

Whose cheek is this?

And bore her safe away. 
Robins, in the tradition 
Did cover such with leaves, 
But which the cheek&mdash; 
And which the pall 
My scrutiny deceives. 
Whose Pink career may have a close 
Whose Pink career may have a close 
Portentous as our own, who knows? 
To imitate these Neighbors fleet 
In awe and innocence, were meet.

"Why do I love" You, Sir?

Why Make It Doubt—it Hurts It So 
 
Why make it doubt—it hurts it so— 
So sick—to guess— 
So strong—to know— 
So brave—upon its little Bed 
To tell the very last They said 
Unto Itself—and smile—And shake— 
For that dear—distant—dangerous—Sake— 
But—the Instead—the Pinching fear 
That Something—it did do—or dare— 
Offend the Vision—and it flee— 
And They no more remember me— 
Nor ever turn to tell me why— 
Oh, Master, This is Misery—

Wild Nights! Wild Nights!

Will There Really Be A "Morning"? 
 
Will there really be a "Morning"? 
Is there such a thing as "Day"? 
Could I see it from the mountains 
If I were as tall as they? 
Has it feet like Water lilies? 
Has it feathers like a Bird? 
Is it brought from famous countries 
Of which I have never heard? 
Oh some Scholar! Oh some Sailor! 
Oh some Wise Men from the skies! 
Please to tell a little Pilgrim 
Where the place called "Morning" lies! 
Witchcraft Has Not A Pedigree 
Witchcraft has not a pedigree, 
‘Tis early as our breath, 
And mourners meet it going out 
The moment of our death.

Within My Garden, Rides A Bird 
 
Within my Garden, rides a Bird 
Upon a single Wheel&mdash; 
Whose spokes a dizzy Music make 
As 'twere a travelling Mill&mdash; 
He never stops, but slackens 
Above the Ripest Rose&mdash; 
Partakes without alighting 
And praises as he goes, 
Till every spice is tasted&mdash; 
And then his Fairy Gig 
Reels in remoter atmospheres&mdash; 
And I rejoin my Dog, 
And He and I, perplex us 
If positive, 'twere we&mdash; 
Or bore the Garden in the Brain 
This Curiosity&mdash; 
But He, the best Logician, 
Refers my clumsy eye&mdash; 
To just vibrating Blossoms! 
An Exquisite Reply!

Within my reach! 
I could have touched!

Sauntered as soft away!

Within the meadows go&mdash;

That passed, an hour ago!

Would You Like Summer? Taste Of Ours

You Love Me—you Are Sure 
 
You love me—you are sure— 
I shall not fear mistake—

Quite none? 
Be sure you're sure—you know—

You Love The Lord—you Cannot See 
 
You love the Lord—you cannot see—

And further in the Day. 
An Ample Letter—How you miss— 
And would delight to see— 
But then His House—is but a Step— 
And Mine's—in Heaven—You see. 
You Said That I 
You said that I "was Great"—one Day— 
Then "Great" it be—if that please Thee— 
Or Small—or any size at all— 
Nay—I'm the size suit Thee—

Or other thing—if other thing there be— 
With just this Stipulus— 
I suit Thee— 
You See I Cannot See—your Lifetime 
 
You see I cannot see—your lifetime— 
I must guess—

But I guess guessing hurts— 
Mine—got so dim! 
Too vague—the face— 
My own—so patient—covers—

My timidness enfolds— 
Haunting the Heart—

You Taught Me Waiting With Myself 
 
You taught me Waiting with Myself— 
Appointment strictly kept— 
You taught me fortitude of Fate— 
This—also—I have learnt— 
An Altitude of Death, that could 
No bitterer debar 
Than Life—had done—before it— 
Yet—there is a Science more— 
The Heaven you know—to understand 
That you be not ashamed 
Of Me—in Christ's bright Audience 
Upon the further Hand— 
You'Ll Find—it When You Try To Die 
 
You'll find—it when you try to die— 
The Easier to let go— 
For recollecting such as went— 
You could not spare—you know. 
And though their places somewhat filled— 
As did their Marble names 
With Moss—they never grew so full— 
You chose the newer names— 
And when this World—sets further back— 
As Dying—say it does— 
The former love—distincter grows— 
And supersedes the fresh— 
And Thought of them—so fair invites— 
It looks too tawdry Grace 
To stay behind—with just the Toys 
We bought—to ease their place— 
You'Ll Know Her—by Her Foot 
 
You'll know Her—by Her Foot— 
The smallest Gamboge Hand 
With Fingers—where the Toes should be— 
Would more affront the Sand— 
Than this Quaint Creature's Boot— 
Adjusted by a Stern— 
Without a Button—I could vouch— 
Unto a Velvet Limb— 
You'll know Her—by Her Vest— 
Tight fitting—Orange—Brown— 
Inside a Jacket duller— 
She wore when she was born— 
Her Cap is small—and snug— 
Constructed for the Winds— 
She'd pass for Barehead—short way off— 
But as She Closer stands— 
So finer 'tis than Wool— 
You cannot feel the Seam— 
Nor is it Clasped unto of Band— 
Nor held upon—of Brim— 
You'll know Her—by Her Voice— 
At first—a doubtful Tone— 
A sweet endeavor—but as March 
To April—hurries on— 
She squanders on your Ear 
Such Arguments of Pearl— 
You beg the Robin in your Brain 
To keep the other—still— 
You'Ll Know It—as You Know 'Tis Noon 
 
You'll know it—as you know 'tis Noon— 
By Glory— 
As you do the Sun— 
By Glory— 
As you will in Heaven— 
Know God the Father—and the Son. 
By intuition, Mightiest Things 
Assert themselves—and not by terms— 
"I'm Midnight"—need the Midnight say— 
"I'm Sunrise"—Need the Majesty? 
Omnipotence—had not a Tongue— 
His listp—is Lightning—and the Sun— 
His Conversation—with the Sea— 
"How shall you know"? 
Consult your Eye! 
Your Riches—taught Me—poverty 
 
Your Riches—taught me—Poverty. 
Myself—a Millionaire 
In little Wealths, as Girls could boast 
Till broad as Buenos Ayre— 
You drifted your Dominions— 
A Different Peru— 
And I esteemed All Poverty 
For Life's Estate with you— 
Of Mines, I little know—myself— 
But just the names, of Gems— 
The Colors of the Commonest— 
And scarce of Diadems— 
So much, that did I meet the Queen— 
Her Glory I should know— 
But this, must be a different Wealth— 
To miss it—beggars so— 
I'm sure 'tis India—all Day— 
To those who look on You— 
Without a stint—without a blame, 
Might I—but be the Jew— 
I'm sure it is Golconda— 
Beyond my power to deem— 
To have a smile for Mine—each Day, 
How better, than a Gem! 
At least, it solaces to know 
That there exists—a Gold— 
Altho' I prove it, just in time 
Its distance—to behold— 
Its far—far Treasure to surmise— 
And estimate the Pearl— 
That slipped my simple fingers through— 
While just a Girl at School. 
You'Re Right— 
 
You're right—"the way is narrow"— 
And "difficult the Gate"— 
And "few there be"—Correct again— 
That "enter in—thereat"— 
'Tis Costly—So are purples! 
'Tis just the price of Breath— 
With but the "Discount" of the Grave— 
Termed by the Brokers—"Death"! 
And after that—there's Heaven— 
The Good Man's—"Dividend"— 
And Bad Men—"go to Jail"— 
I guess—
